# Sebastopyr — The Bastion Campaign Bible

*Compiled from the canon bundle of 2026-06-01.*
*Source workflow: wf_0ef5c291-1e1.*

---

## On the Name "Sebastopyr"

Sebastopyr fuses the Old-Tongue root *sebast-* (the martyr-name; "the venerable one who endured the arrows and did not die of them, then was martyred anyway") with *-pyr*, the Old-Tongue suffix for "wall" or "ward-stone" — literally a watchfire-stone set in the curtain wall of a holy keep. So Sebastopyr means, in its first reading, "The Wall Named For The Enduring One" — but the same root *sebast-* in the older liturgical case carries the secondary, bitter sense of "the one who endured for nothing," because the saint endured the arrows only to be clubbed to death in the second martyrdom. The founders chose the name in 6th-century-old liturgical court Old-Tongue, and the scholiasts have argued for six hundred years which sense was intended. The Cathedral's official position is that both senses were intended at once — that the city's name is a deliberate paradox the founders left lit for their descendants — but at least one suppressed gloss in the archive reads the name as a confession, set in stone by men who already knew the war could not be won and named their wall accordingly. The city is universally called "the Pyr" in everyday speech (Pyrian for its citizens, the Pyric Wall for the curtain), which has the unintended effect of letting people forget, daily, what the second half of the name actually means.

Pyrians call their city **the Pyr** in nearly every register that is not a sermon, an inquisitorial reading, or a foreign embassy's greeting. The shortening is a daily, citywide act of theological forgetting. See the companion note **`01-sebastopyr-etymology.md`** for the full naming record and the alternatives considered.

---

## Reading Order & Orientation

This bible incorporates the ten finalized output documents from the canon pipeline. They are presented in the order a referee should read them when preparing a campaign:

1. **Atlas** — the world, the continent, the geography that determines what the kingdom is for.
2. **Pantheon** — the theology, the divine, what Grace actually *is*.
3. **Factions** — the political map: who wants what, who is owed what, who is reading whom.
4. **City Districts** — Sebastopyr ward by ward, where the campaign actually happens.
5. **Timeline** — deep history and recent history, the dates that explain every grievance.
6. **Daily Life** — what the bread costs, what the lamps burn, what the laundry smells like.
7. **Bestiary** — the hordes, the damned, the stained.
8. **NPC Roster** — the named figures who animate the spine.
9. **Plot Threads** — the twelve master arcs the campaign can hang on.
10. **Player Brief** — the trimmed handout a player can be given on day one.

The fourteen **canon layers** (geography, climate, cosmology, hell, grace, deep history, recent history, the city, church, order/paragon, inquisition, kingdom, the calling, bargain economy, mundane life, threats) feed every output above. They appear as cross-reference blockquotes inside the sections they enrich.

## Synthesis Notes — Decisions That Bind the Canon

### Key Decisions

- Year is PD 606; Standing was PD 583; current Sebastopater is Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX (elevated PD 604).
- The cheap-story refusals are upheld: the Paragon is genuinely a real holy man and his Stain readings come back clean every dawn for 23 years — the danger is not his secret corruption but the curated singularity that makes him the only one, plus the Quartermaster's open account he refused but cannot be certain about.
- The Custodes Numeri and the deep_history layer's Cantorial Scribes are ONE body with two names — operational name 'Cantorial Scribes,' self-name 'Custodes Numeri.' Seven seats, one currently empty (Thelos's), recruiting Liturge di Carrenost.
- Velim Aurriste is the central righteous-villain: principal author of Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity, senior Custodes Numeri, struck the Octave Bargain with the Quartermaster of Tongues, three Stain readings CLEAN/ANOMALY/UNKNOWN, fourth reading scheduled PD 608. He is one of the most important characters in the canon and his trajectory should be a load-bearing arc.
- The Aurriste-name proliferation is deliberate canon: Halidan polished into Aurriste, multiple Aurriste branches (cadet of Carrenost, cadet of Ferrostat, Halidan-Aurriste new-wealth, Vell-os-Carrenost lineage); the PD 602 chancery-clerk-stroke cross-reference failure is the load-bearing accident that protects the Paragon's ignorance of the keel-throne / surname coincidence.
- Two saint counts kept separately: the official Saint Count (143, 81-year plateau) AND the Suppressed Paragon Count (73 named + 48 nameless = 121, kept by the Cantorial Scribes in the Audit-Below). The Plate of Sebastian's ~400 'blessed unnamed' is a third stratum. The buried truth: at least 4 prior Paragons in living memory (per threats), more than that if counting back six centuries.
- The Pyric Wall has 7 concentric courses; the current outer-course has 80 chancery towers, 84 true towers, 4 silently condemned in PD 583 — the Standing year, which is the load-bearing throughline-6 timing coincidence.
- The aspersoir is dual-scale: a 0-10 underlying Stain grade AND a 1-6 tick readout, with mercury boil at tick-3/Stain~3.0 the shared threshold. The chancery has recalibrated the clinical-concern threshold upward four times since PD 602.
- Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind and Confessor-Ordinary Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost are the dual-Vesperine filter on the Sebastopater's reality — Mortane in the city (master of access, 23 years), Mauritz at Ferrostat (Paragon's bonded confessor, 23 years of CLEAN readings). Both devout, both editing truth in love, both serving the curation.
- Three Asperines (de la Pyrille / Nocta / Vesselain) and three Cassians de la Pyrille (Captain-Pyric / Inquisitor-Magisterial / Inquisitor-Vested cross-reference to the Long Confessor) are preserved as distinct characters; the Slag-Hand clan-name is shared by multiple Ferrenkin (mother-daughter Neras explicitly, plus Korreth Slag-Tongue and Marent of the Slag-Hand).
- The Quartermaster of Tongues' open account on Halidan Aurriste is the buried gun on the mantel — the throughline's deepest single character beat — and must be preserved as both possibly-true and possibly-paranoia.
- The Sixth Notary's incomplete name (Mournwing intelligence) creates a structural plot opportunity: the binding could be performed before completion, but the chancery does not have the intelligence because the Mournwing have withheld it.
- Severa Aurriste-cadet is in Sebastopyr (Vexillarius, Hall of the Long Vigil), NOT at Ferrostat; Cassian de la Pyrille is the field commander at Ferrostat.
- The Paragon has not been to Sebastopyr in 10 years (revised from 7 to match PD 606 timeline; last visit PD 596).
- The Calling rite's three-prototype routing happens at the Vocation House via Archvigil Severa di Mauritz's nine-second Discernment; Battle-Mages preferentially route to the Reclamation Corps's Auxiliary Roll because their pre-Cathedral arcane pool is theologically inconvenient.
- The Sebastopater chancery instability is canon: TWO Sebastopaters elevated in the last two years (Mauritz I died PD 604, Iohanne IX elevated immediately). The institution is fragile in the present moment.

The Concilium Sebastinum that invented the Aspirant rank is PD 587 (post-rising, pre-doctrine). Current year is c. PD 603-606 (twenty years on).

The 'Cassian VII/VIII' naming in recent_history is a working-draft variant superseded. His predecessor (Cassian VII in recent_history) died PD 591 of 'fatigue of the heart' having signed the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity. Iohanne kept the Cantor-Magisterial appointment that placed Velim Aurriste at the doctrinal helm.

CANTOR-MAGISTERIAL ASPERINE OS VEILLARDE (62, former opera singer, head of MUSICAL liturgy and composition, composes the current setting of the Watch-Cantos, can read cursivus sebastinus minor, has discovered the Vocatio Aurriste fragment of 581 PD). 'Severa di Pyrille' is reassigned as a different character: SEVERA DI PYRILLE = Inquisitor-Magisterial Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost (from the_inquisition), the Office's best Reader, working the Almongate Cluster. The hand also tremors after Grace expenditure — a tremor that the chancery medical archive notes is intensified by the prior injury but is structurally caused by the vetus aspirantis (the Grace-decline). The black glove conceals BOTH the scarring and the tremor.

She is NOT at Ferrostat. recent_history's 'Marshal-Captain at Ferrostat' is reassigned: CAPTAIN-PYRIC CASSIAN DE LA PYRILLE (from the_order, 34, Captain of the Reclamation Corps, Iron March) is the Paragon's principal field commander. Severa Aurriste-cadet's role at Banner-Fall (pulling Cassian di Pyrille out) is preserved as the act that earned her Vexillarius elevation.

NERA SLAG-HAND THE YOUNGER (called 'Nera the Younger' or just 'Nera' in Order contexts; 52, File-Leader of the Tenth File on the north Pyric Wall) is the daughter — the only Ferrenkin to reach File-Leader rank. The elder retired from the Lampwarden post in 585, the year her daughter joined the Order. Their estrangement is a quiet sorrow: the elder thinks the daughter has been seduced by the Cathedral; the daughter thinks the elder has compromised herself with the under-ward. Neither will speak of the other. Both know, separately, which wall-towers are silently condemned.

The TICK-COUNT (the_inquisition, 1-6) is the OPERATIONAL field instrument's readout, calibrated so each tick-band corresponds to a roughly-doubled range of the underlying scale (tick 1 = 0-0.5 underlying; tick 2 = 0.5-1.5; tick 3 = 1.5-3.0 anomaly; tick 4 = 3.0-5.0; tick 5 = 5.0-7.0; tick 6 = 7.0-10.0 immediate binding). Mercury boils at tick 3 / Stain ~3.0 (the layers agree at this critical threshold). The chancery's three quiet recalibrations (cosmology_hell) raised the clinical-concern threshold from underlying 0.9 to 1.2 to 1.5 to 2.0 — all within tick-band 2, all sub-clinical at the operational instrument. This is canon-consistent and throughline-perfect: the curation hides in the gap between the continuous truth and the operational measurement.
- ****
  - **Resolved:** CANON = THESE ARE TWO DIFFERENT COUNTS. The official SAINT COUNT (143, plateau 81 years) is the total of all canonized Vespertine saints across six centuries — patriarch-saints, lesser martyrs, beatified figures buried in the Sanctuary chapels. The SUPPRESSED PARAGON COUNT (73 known + 48 nameless = 121 cases) is a DIFFERENT registry inside the Audit-Below: the Aspirant-rank cases that were closed by the Office of the Cantorial Scribes. Both counts exist simultaneously and are curated by the Custodes Numeri (the seven-member group from threats layer = the Cantorial Scribes from deep_history; reconciled as a single body with two names, scribal/operational name 'Cantorial Scribes,' self-name 'Custodes Numeri'). The Plate of Sebastian (400 'blessed unnamed' bones) is yet a third stratum.

He is DISTINCT from CONFESSOR-ORDINARY MAURITZ VELL-OS-CARRENOST (47, Vesperine, the Paragon's bonded confessor at Ferrostat, from the_order). The two communicate by letter; Mauritz files his daily Stain-readings of the Paragon to Mortane, who decides which reach the Sebastopater. Mortane filters BOTH the chancery's reality AND the Paragon's reality from the Sebastopater. The Mournwing courier system's broken-and-resealed letters (recent_history) is Mortane's work, intercepting Mauritz's frontier reports.

He keeps the Aspirant's Lodgings in the Sanctuary Ring, mostly empty, used for ceremonial purposes (Octave of Triumph relic-display). The Cathedral has not formally invited him; the chancery has 'declined his return' three times citing 'strategic necessity.' Halidan himself, in the unread letter in his desk (the_order), called the decline 'fear of what the city has built me into in my absence.'

(2) VELIM HALIDAN-AURRISTE (44, new-wealth, chairman of Reclamation Concession, House Halidan-Aurriste of Halidan-stat) — distinct house, distinct person, the city's economic face. (3) CONFESSOR-ORDINARY VELIM AURRISTE OF THE PYRIC WALL (41, divine-bargain broker at the wall, writes price-clause first) — distinct cousin, lower-ranking. Plus SEBASTOPATER IOHANNE VELL-OS-CARRENOST (note Vell-os-Carrenost, not Aurriste). The Aurriste name proliferates exactly because the Paragon's polished surname has made it desirable, which is itself a throughline test 6 artifact: the curation has produced a fashion that obscures the lineage.

### Gaps Left Open for the Referee

- Current year-in-game: Layers float between c. PD 603-606 (twenty years post-PD-583). FILLED: Current year is PD 606. Twenty-three years since the Standing (matching threats' 'twenty-three years ago' for the Quartermaster offer to Halden Orriste). Reclaimed Crown is in its twenty-third year. Sebastopater Iohanne is in his eighteenth year of tenure.
- Sebastopater succession chain: FILLED. The chain is: Sebastopater Cassian VII (d. 591 PD, signed Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity in 589 PD, died fourteen months after) â†’ Sebastopater Mauritz I (d. 604 PD, signed Aspirant-Protection Ordinance 599 PD) â†’ Sebastopater Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX (elevated 604 PD at age 79, currently 81). Note: this means the chancery has elevated TWO Sebastopaters in the last two years; chancery instability is a present-moment political fact.
- Identity of the Sebast-Auditor: the_inquisition references the unnamed Sebast-Auditor with full read-access to the Sealed Anomaly Ledger. FLAGGED: Identity reserved for character-layer work; canonically the Sebast-Auditor's name is sealed even within the chancery. The current Sebast-Auditor is a Vesperine, served since 583 PD (suspicious timing coincidence with the Standing).
- Names of the seven Custodes Numeri / Cantorial Scribes: PARTIAL. Velim Aurriste named as senior. Five remaining seats: reserve for character-layer work. The seventh seat is the rotating Annotator and is currently empty (the previous holder, Confessor Thelos di Carrenost, was murdered, per threats).
- The Long Vigil of 583 PD detailed: FLAGGED for the_six_centuries_of_siege layer (referenced as needed input by recent_history). Canonically: relief-failure at the Almongate due to a simultaneous breach; Fourth Shieldwall held eleven hours past rotation; eleven other survivors of the Fourth deposed.
- The Cohort of the Lost Vespers (565 PD): FILLED in deep_history's Suppressed Paragons / Cantorial Scribes; the 117 names in slightly-darker slate are the suppressed paragon-adjacent souls of that year. Connect to threats' Carrion Census: the Sixth Notary's incomplete name began composition in 565 PD, which is why that cohort was suppressed.
- Whether the Paragon has been formally Stain-read: FILLED. He was read at elevation in PD 583 and the reading came back ANOMALY. The chancery filed it as 'consistent with divine attention residue' and has not re-read him. Confessor Mauritz reads him daily and the readings come back CLEAN — which is itself the anomaly. The Vesperine minority opinion (sealed) demands an independent re-reading; Hierarch Nocta has drafted a fourth report.
- The Calling rite's mechanical interaction with the three character prototypes (Human / Battle-Mage / Detective): FILLED. The rite is performed identically; the Vesperine processors' nine-second Discernment (Archvigil Severa di Mauritz's gesture) routes the new Called by prototype. Battle-Mages are theologically inconvenient (their arcane pool predates the Cathedral's grant) and are routed preferentially to the Reclamation Corps (Auxiliary Roll); Detectives are routed to the Inquisition or the Order's officer-track; Humans default to Order Numerati. The Cathedral's internal procedure for Battle-Mage 'inconvenience' is the Aspirant-Reluctant improvisation (threats: the Saintmire refuser is a Battle-Mage prototype, FLAGGED for resolution by the Called layer).
- Identity of the Sixth Notary's incomplete name: FLAGGED. Per threats and the Mournwing intelligence, the name is composed in real-time by 'the desk' demonic apparatus. The Cathedral does not have it. The Mournwing have not shared it. The buried opportunity: a binding before completion could sunder the entity.
- Whether the Paragon's surname coincidence with the Aurriste keel-throne is known to him: PARTIALLY FILLED. Halidan does NOT know the keel-throne connection. He believes 'Aurriste' was a polishing of his birth-name 'Orriste' by chancery clerks. The PD 602 cross-reference failure (chancery clerk's stroke) is the accident that protects his ignorance. Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste knows. Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde knows (from singing fragments of the Vocatio Aurriste).
- The fourteen high-Stain Carcer prisoners Korreth Slag-Tongue identified: FLAGGED for the_under_ward / Carcer character layer. Three are politically loaded; one is the Saintmire refuser ('Jin of Macau, 2019' from threats — her Stain reads anomaly because Battle-Mage arcane signatures cross-trip the Vesperine aspersoir).
- The chancery cipher on the 584 PD requisition slip removing the 565 PD Refusers' Index: FLAGGED. The cipher is identifiable to Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde, who has not spoken its identity. It belongs to a Sebastopater whose name has been redacted from the rank-roll (per deep_history). This is a deep-archive plot hook.

## I. Atlas — The World and the Continent

### ATLAS OF AEVARN AND THERIMAUR
##### A Text-Map of the World as It Stands in PD 606

> *"The world has six continents on the old plates. Five of them are deemed lost. The sixth is deemed held. Both verbs are conjugated in the deemed register."*
> — Lector Pell Vesselain, *A Postulant's Geography*, 5th ed. (chancery-approved, PD 587; outer-bands omitted by editorial decision)

---

#### I. THE WORLD CALLED AEVARN

**Aevarn** is the name the founders set on the plates. It is no longer in popular speech — the priests say *the world*, the soldiers say *the held*, the under-wards say *what's left*. The Caer-Druin sing it in vespers and the children do not learn it. The Cathedral teaches Aevarn has *six* continents. Eight pre-Fall fragments in the Audit-Below count *seven*. The seventh is not named; that page is bound in.

Of the six **deemed-mapped** continents, only one is held. The other five are **Hell-occupied territory** — the Hordeflesh, the Long Smoke, the Drowned Tier, the Shelved Coast, the Plate-of-Wounds. Their interiors are not mapped because no one returns to map them; what is drawn is shoreline-from-the-deck of the three remaining sea-watch sloops that still venture into the lifting weather west of Vesselain Roads, and even those drawings are *deemed coastline* rather than *coastline*. The chancery teaches the world is mostly water and the Hordes hold the rest. The Ferrenkin, who can read pre-Fall engineering, say the proportion is reversed and the water itself has been changing for six centuries — that the seas Aevarn used to have are not the seas Aevarn has now.

The sun rises and sets. The stars are mostly the same. The moon is the same moon. These three facts are the basis of the chancery's argument that the world is still itself.

##### Sky and Weather

- **Wind blows mostly off the Hordeflesh** in the east — a hot, sweet, iron-tasting wind the Pyric watchers call **the Censer Wind**. It carries Stain. A man can stand in it for an hour and read clean; for a season and read anomaly; for a year and the boil comes at sext.
- **Rain comes mostly from the west**, off the lifting weather that breaks against the Vesselain Roads. It is the only clean rain in the world. The cisterns of Sebastopyr are filled by it; the Vas Halidani's seventeen tons are blessed western rain, drawn at the Cathedral's western drains.
- **Snow falls north of the Iron March** four months a year. The Hordes do not winter — they thin and harry and do not break. The wall fights eleven months and reckons in the twelfth.
- **There is no future tense for weather** in the liturgical register. The chancery forecasts in the *deemed* mood: *the bell tomorrow is deemed clear*. Caer-Druin singers, who keep older almanacs, are not consulted.

---

#### II. THE CONTINENT OF THERIMAUR

Therimaur is roughly the shape of a half-broken shield, lying north-south, with its convex edge to the **Iron Sea** in the west and its broken edge to the **Hordeflesh Strait** in the east. From north tip to south tip is perhaps four hundred leagues by old-stade reckoning; the Cathedral does not publish total figures because total figures invite comparison with what was lost.

Three things you must know to stand on Therimaur and know where you are:

1. **The Continent is held only at its narrow waist.** The held territory — *The Reclaimed Crown of Vespertin* — is a thin band a hundred leagues long and forty leagues deep at its widest point, running east-west across Therimaur's middle, with Sebastopyr at the western anchor and Ferrostat-on-the-Mire at the eastern. The north of Therimaur is **the Long Smoke**; the south is **the Plate-of-Wounds**. Both are Hordes-held and not surveyed.
2. **Rivers east of Sustines now flow west.** Six centuries ago the watershed ran east into the sea. The Hordes' presence has reversed it. Rivers run inland now and pour into **the Hordeflesh sinkholes** — wet wounds where the ground swallows water and does not give it back. The Cathedral teaches these sinkholes are *holy mouths* and the reversal is *the world drinking back its tears*. The Ferrenkin teach nothing about it because the Ferrenkin do not teach; they note in their forge-ledgers that the reversal began in PD 41 and accelerated PD 583.
3. **There is one road that matters.** It is called **the Long Procession** in the chancery, **the Pilgrim's Cinder** in vulgar Vespertine, and **the Aurriste Road** on milestones the new wealth had recut at their own expense. It runs from the Almongate of Sebastopyr east-northeast across the Iron March to Ferrostat-on-the-Mire — sixty-three leagues by bell-distance (the chancery's deliberately-vague unit), four days by hard riding, eleven days by levy column, two weeks by pilgrim, never by night. Everything else is paths off it.

##### How Distances Are Measured

The Cathedral publishes distances in **bell-distance** — the number of bell-tollings a sound travels at dawn-still air. A bell-distance is *deemed* one league but is in fact closer to three-quarters of a league, the foreshortening protected by chancery editorial as "a kindness to the pilgrim's heart." The Order keeps **marching leagues** (true leagues) in its operational rolls. The Ferrenkin keep **rod-counts** (Old-Tongue *virga*) in their wall-engineering. The Caer-Druin keep **song-distance** — the number of verses a Watch-Canto fills walking — which is older and more accurate than any of the others, and which the Cathedral has folded into its vesper-mass without crediting the source.

When a pilgrim says *Ferrostat is sixty-three bells from Sebastopyr*, what they mean is *Ferrostat is forty-seven and a half leagues from Sebastopyr*. The discrepancy is a curated kindness.

---

#### III. THE RECLAIMED CROWN OF VESPERTIN — A WALKTHROUGH

I will walk you west to east, the way the levy columns walk, the way the Long Procession runs, the way a Called soul — fresh from the Vocation House and pointed at the front — is marched. We begin at the curtain of Sebastopyr and end at Ferrostat's outer redoubt, and then we look beyond the Wall.

##### The City Itself: Sebastopyr, the Western Anchor

(*This atlas treats Sebastopyr as a fixed point on the continent; a full city atlas is held separately. Here only enough to orient.*)

Sebastopyr stands on a triple-ridged knoll the Old-Tongue called *Promontorium Sebastinum*, sixty feet above the floodplain of the **River Cathara** (called *the Mort* by the under-wards because it carries the Cathedral's funeral ash downstream). The river runs north past the city and into the Iron Sea at a delta the Caer-Druin will not name. The Cathedral sits at the knoll's high point. The Pyric Wall — seven concentric courses, eighty towers chancery-listed, eighty-four true — descends the knoll in a tightening spiral. The landward gates face east, south, and southwest; the seaward postern faces northwest and is rarely opened. The city is roughly a flattened disc three miles across at its widest curtain.

You see Sebastopyr from twelve bells out — the Cathedral spires first, then the smoke of the Cinderbelow forges, then the upper Pyric towers. The Censer Wind, blowing from the east, carries the smell of incense and gun-grease and burned bone twenty bells downwind on a still day. *The city smells before it shows.*

##### Leaving Sebastopyr Eastward — The Almongate Road

You exit Sebastopyr eastward through the **Almongate** (Old-Tongue *Porta Elemosynaria*, "the gate of mercy" — so named because alms-bread is distributed here at dawn to the eastbound levies and to the Conscripted League's quiet refusers who will not be missed for an hour). The gate is heavy iron-banded oak twelve feet across, kept by **the Almongate Wardens** under Captain-Vested Halidan Marent (54, no relation to the Paragon, sometimes resentful of the surname-coincidence, scrupulously honest). The Wardens take a half-bell to inspect a levy column, a full bell to inspect a Reclamation supply train, a quarter-bell to wave a pilgrim through. A demonic broker named Mother Aspine Vell-os-Carrenost keeps her sanctioned bench seventy yards inside the gate; you will hear the bell-rope for her line jangling as you leave.

The road descends the knoll for two bells through cleared killing-ground (no tree taller than a man within crossbow-range, by chancery ordinance since PD 567). At the foot of the knoll the road crosses the **River Cathara** by the **Bridge of the Hundred Names** — a Ferrenkin-built iron-and-stone bridge with one hundred plaques set in the parapet, each plaque bearing the name of a Pyrian who fell holding the bridge during the Long Vigil of PD 583. Pilgrims throw a small bronze sebast-piece in the water as they cross. The bottom is silver with them. Children of the Lampwarden's parish wade for them at midsummer when the river runs low and the Cathedral cannot stop them.

Beyond the bridge, you enter the first true frontier landscape: **the Almongate Plain** — three days' ride of cleared, leveled, ditched, and double-warded farmland kept by tied tenants of House Veillarde and House Aurriste of Carrenost. The fields are striped: wheat, vigil-grain (a black-eared barley the Cathedral consecrates and the Vas Halidani's water grows), and **fallow lit by lanterns at dusk** — a chancery ordinance since PD 597, the year of the Lampgard Breach. Every furlong has a lamp-pole; every pole has a parish-tended lantern; every lantern is lit at vespers and tended through the night by Lamp-Tenders of the Compact (Veriarch Thelos di Cinderost's people, who also print the seditious *Reflected* press, which is among the chancery's many tolerated open secrets).

The road in this stretch is busy: pilgrims west, levies east, supply wagons both directions, censer-priests blessing the milestones every third mile. You see no Hordes here, but every wagon's outrider carries an aspersoir on a chain, and every two bells a Pyric horn sounds from the rearguard to mark the column's pace.

##### THE IRON MARCH

You enter the Iron March three days east of the Almongate, at the village of **Old Pell's Crossing** (named for a real woman, a Ferrenkin midwife who held the ford against a single horde-fang in PD 588 with a kitchen cleaver; she is not the Old Pell who runs the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp parlor in Sebastopyr, but she is that Pell's great-aunt, and the family has worked the ration-trade in some form for a hundred years). The crossing is a stone-paved ford over the **Iron Run**, a clean fast tributary of the Cathara that drains the northern uplands. There is a chapel here, three taverns, a Reclamation Corps requisition-house, and an Office of the Pyric Audit substation that does Stain-readings on every traveler entering the March.

The Iron March is the heart of the kingdom and the spine of the Reclamation. It is fifty leagues wide, twenty leagues deep at its broadest, an undulating country of low ridges and shallow valleys cut by north-flowing tributaries. The soil is dark, iron-rich (hence the name, though the chancery teaches the name comes from *the iron will of those who hold it*), and grows vigil-grain twice a year. There are **eleven walled towns and twenty-seven fortified holds** in the March. From west to east, the towns that matter:

###### 1. **Vigilstat-on-the-Run** (3 bells east of Old Pell's Crossing)
A Reclamation Corps depot town of about 4,000 souls, walled in PD 594 with Ferrenkin-set black basalt. The wall is sixteen feet high, the keep is taller. Its commander is **Captain-Vested Marent Veillarde-cadet** (38, niece of the Regent, sober and tactically gifted, drinks only watered Pyric ale, attends mass twice daily, would arrest her own mother if the chancery so ordered). Vigilstat hosts the **Iron March Grain-Reserve** — three subterranean Ferrenkin granaries holding a winter's worth of bread for the entire kingdom. The granaries' true capacity is half what the chancery's roll states; the missing half is the Bypassed Pensions food-debt no one in this town will say aloud. Every soul in Vigilstat knows the larders are short. None has said so to a chancery clerk in three years.

###### 2. **Halidan-stat** (5 bells northeast of Vigilstat)
The polished-name town. New-wealth, built PD 591, occupied PD 593, walled PD 595. The new-wealth Halidan-Aurristes — *Velim Halidan-Aurriste*, 44, chairman of the Reclamation Concession — bought the chartering from the chancery for thirty thousand sebast-pieces and named the town to honor the Paragon. Halidan himself has never been there. The town is well-fed, well-walled, hosts a Cathedral mission and a private apothecary that holds one-seventh of the city's masking-tincture trade. It is also where the **Auxiliary Roll** is officially kept — the kingdom's count of frontier-irregular dead, Battle-Mage Called routed to Reclamation. The Roll is read at Halidan-stat's morning office by Captain-Pyric Cassian de la Pyrille's clerk on the first of each month, with the Paragon's prior authorization *"Count them well."* No one in Halidan-stat knows the count's true scale. The clerk who reads it has begun keeping a private copy chained inside her vestment.

###### 3. **Lectors' Fall** (8 bells south-southeast of Halidan-stat)
A memorial town, kept rather than grown. PD 9 PT (Post-Triumph, the new dating the chancery introduced PD 597 to mark *the era after the deemed-eternity ended*; the PT calendar runs alongside PD and the two do not align cleanly) — in that year, an ambush of Reclamation Corps officers (the Lectors of the title — twenty-two scripture-trained line officers who had been promoted in a single chancery decree) was destroyed by horde-fang infiltration at the eastern edge of the March. The chancery teaches it as *the trial of the new-blessed lectors*. The truth is the ambush was set by a horde-fang carrying the Sixth Notary's incomplete writ and the lectors were intelligence carriers for the Custodes Numeri. Patriarch Thelos Cassian-cadet of Lectors' Fall has been corresponding with Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste about this. His letters arrive opened; he does not stop writing them.

Lectors' Fall is now a small town of 800 souls, mostly tied tenants of the memorial-hold, with a chapel built over the ambush ground where every dawn a Veriarch reads the twenty-two names. The names read are the *deemed* names; one of the lectors is missing from the Reclamation muster-roll, and the chancery has filled the gap with a name that does not appear in any other record.

###### 4. **Aurgard** (4 bells east of Vigilstat, on the Long Procession)
The largest town in the March, 7,500 souls, a Cathedral seat with a Hierarch and a Pyric Audit office. Walled in PD 590 with **two courses** — an outer earthwork, an inner Ferrenkin curtain. Hosts the only **public Vocation chapel** outside Sebastopyr, where Called who survive their first six months and consent are formally enrolled in the Order. The town's bread is half vigil-grain and half barley, its ale is honest, its inquisitorial readings come back clean at a rate two percentage points higher than chancery average for towns of its size. The local Inquisitor-Vested has been there nine years. No one is sure why the rate is high; the Audit-Below has noticed and not investigated. **A pilgrim hospice run by the Sisters of the Almonine** sits against the inner wall and is the best place in the March to overhear what people actually believe.

###### 5. **Drownmire** (south of the Long Procession, 9 bells south of Aurgard)
A lost hold. Walled PD 591, lost PD 597 in the Lampgard Breach campaign, never reclaimed. The chancery does not list it on current maps; it appears only on Reclamation-era surveys held in the Hall of the Long Vigil. The miry ground around it is impassable to columns. **Horde-fangs nest there.** The Brothers of the Cinder Hand have a clandestine cell here, in a half-flooded chapel above a slumped Ferrenkin cellar; they print *The Refusal* on a press they recovered from the cellar floors. The chancery knows the cell exists and has chosen not to assault — the strategic position is too miserable to assault for a doctrinal target, and the Brothers' press is a useful pressure valve for the Conscripted League. Drownmire is the open secret the kingdom keeps because closing it would cost more than it would save.

###### 6. **Saintmire** (north of the Long Procession, 11 bells north-northeast of Lectors' Fall)
A reclaimed hold; lost PD 581, retaken PD 589, the second reclaimed town after Ferrostat. Built on the ruins of an older Caer-Druin shrine that the chancery has covered over with a Vespertine sanctuary. Hosts a Carcer-substation — a frontier prison for Stain-anomaly cases not yet ready for transport to the Sebastopyr Carcer — and is the holding-place of **Jin** (the Battle-Mage refuser, Macau 2019, Called PD 605, who refused the oath at Vocation and whose Stain reads anomaly because her arcane signature trips the aspersoir's calibration). Jin sits in cell three of the substation. The Veriarch invented the "Aspirant-Reluctant" category to hold her without trial. The Brothers of the Cinder Hand know where she is. The Sixth Notary's writ-clerks have noticed her account.

###### 7. **Caer Pyrigorne** (12 bells south of Aurgard, deep in the March)
A pre-collapse elder-style hold, originally a hilltop court of the Caer-Druin's southern brethren, reclaimed PD 593 and now a Cathedral-administered shrine and waystop. The original stonework is unmistakable: spiral hill-court walls, song-grooves cut into the stone where Caer-Druin wardens once placed their reliquary-harps. The Cathedral has placed a chapel inside the spiral. Caer-Druin pilgrims still come; the chancery permits this and watches it. The hold is administered by a Veriarch and three Sisters of the Almonine. A pre-Old-Tongue inscription runs around the inner court that no Cathedral cleric will translate. Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde has been there twice; the second visit she stayed a night and did not file a report.

###### 8. **Banner-Fall** (17 bells east of Aurgard, on the Long Procession near the Mire March transition)
The site of the only major defeat of the Reclamation, PD 601. A planned eastward advance broke against a horde-fang reinforced by something the survivors will not name. **Three hundred and four** Order soldiers died, including Captain-Pyric Cassian di Pyrille (predecessor and distant kin to the current Captain-Pyric Cassian de la Pyrille). The Paragon was at the engagement. His left hand was crushed by a falling stone from a wall they were holding too late. Marshal-Vested Severa Aurriste-cadet — then a young line-officer — pulled the dying Cassian di Pyrille out under fire and was raised to Vexillarius for it. The place is now a battlefield-memorial: a low cairn, a chapel, two hundred and twelve named stones (the other ninety-two could not be identified), and a single black silk banner that is replaced annually by the Order's Honors Office. The Paragon has not been to Banner-Fall since the day his hand was crushed. He will not speak of it. Confessor-Ordinary Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost has heard him weep there in dream, twice, in twenty-three years.

##### THE MIRE MARCH

Past Banner-Fall the Iron March gives way to the **Mire March** — a low, sodden country of slow rivers, peat-bogs, salt-mires (where the Hordeflesh's reversed tides have pushed brine inland), and the lifting hot wind from the Hordeflesh Strait. The road continues — the Long Procession is metalled with crushed basalt through this stretch, an immense Ferrenkin engineering work completed PD 595 — but everything off the road is dangerous. The Mire March is **thirty leagues wide** and **fifteen leagues deep** at its broadest. The Cathedral teaches that the Mire is *the land repenting* — soaking itself in tears after six centuries of dryness. The truth is simpler: the watershed reversal has drowned it.

###### 9. **Ferrostat-on-the-Mire** (10 bells east of Banner-Fall, the eastern anchor of the kingdom)
The Paragon's seat. The frontier outpost. The fortress town that is the kingdom's whole eastern reach. Built PD 588 — the year after the Standing — on the ruins of a pre-Fall Ferrenkin fortified station called *Ferrum-Stat* (literally "the iron stands"), of which a single sublevel and a partial outer wall survived. The Ferrenkin rebuilt the curtain in eight months by working through three shifts a day in the autumn rains. The Paragon walked east at the head of the column and was the first to set hand on the new keystone.

Ferrostat is *built into* the ruin. The outer wall is half pre-Fall Ferrenkin black basalt and half PD 588 rebuild, the two stones distinguishable only by the angle of the chisel-marks. The keep — **the Hand's Keep** — is a low five-sided drum tower with the Paragon's standard (a single arrow flighted with black feathers, fletched against a silver-grey field) flying from the rooftop. The Hand's Keep holds the Paragon's quarters (one room, a cot, a desk, a single icon, no fire), the Reclamation Corps command post, the Octave Chapel where the Paragon hears mass alone at dawn, and the **scriptorium** where Confessor-Ordinary Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost takes the Paragon's daily Stain-reading and files the report.

Ferrostat houses **2,400 Order soldiers** of the Reclamation Corps (under Captain-Pyric Cassian de la Pyrille), **600 Auxiliary** (the Battle-Mage Called and other irregulars whose roll is the Auxiliary Roll), **300 Pyric Wardens** (engineers, sappers, Ferrenkin smiths), **100 chancery clerks and confessors**, and approximately **1,500 civilians** — tied tenants, Almoners, victuallers, the Caer-Druin singers who walk the curtain at dusk, the Sisters of the Almonine who run the infirmary, the Cinder-Hand sympathizers who run the laundry and the latrine details. The civilian count does not appear on the chancery roll.

The town is built in a tight triangle pressed against the curtain: a market triangle, a chapel triangle, a barracks triangle, and a single approach road that doubles back on itself twice before reaching the inner gate. The streets are crushed Ferrenkin slag; they ring underfoot. The bells of Ferrostat are three: the dawn bell (rung by Confessor Mauritz himself), the watch bell (rung at every hour-change), and the **Vespers Bell** — the largest, rung only by the Paragon, only when he is in Ferrostat, only at the close of every action. It has not been rung in three months.

**What you see traveling here from Banner-Fall:** the road narrows from twelve paces to eight; the lamp-poles thin from every furlong to every three furlongs; the killing-ground beside the road is no longer cleared but burned bi-monthly by sapper teams. There are corpse-pits at the half-bell intervals, freshly limed. The Censer Wind blows steady. You smell Ferrostat from four bells out — burned bone, hot iron, vigil-grain bread, and the curious metallic-sweet of the salt-mires. You see its standard before you see its walls.

##### BEYOND FERROSTAT — THE EASTWARD ROADS THAT DO NOT EXIST

There are three roads east of Ferrostat. The Cathedral lists none of them on chancery maps.

- **The Cinder Trail** — a horde-track now used by scouts of the Reclamation Corps. Runs east-northeast across the Mire March's outer edge into the **Stain-Lands**. No Pyrian has gone past its third bend in nine years. The trail is checked by a Ferrenkin scout-pair every fortnight; they reach the second bend and return. The Sixth Notary's writ-clerks have left things on the trail — chips of slate with marginalia in cursivus sebastinus minor — and the scouts bring them back and Confessor Mauritz burns them without reading.
- **The Pilgrim's Cinder East** — a name the under-wards use for the road the Conscripted League follows when they desert. There is no actual road; there is only a pattern of paths through the salt-mires that, walked correctly, gets you twenty leagues east of Ferrostat to **a fishing village called Vesselain Roads** that may or may not exist and may or may not be controlled by Hordes. Twelve Conscripted have walked it in twenty years. One returned. He is in the Saintmire Carcer.
- **The Long Procession East** — what the Paragon's planned next advance will build. The route is surveyed (Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste's planning, with chancery cartographers, completed PD 604) and the engineering is drawn. The road will run **nineteen leagues** east of Ferrostat to a planned new hold called **Aurristead** at a defensible river-bend on the **Ash River** (which still flows east, anomalously — the Cathedral has not noticed). The advance has been deferred three times. The chancery position is *strategic necessity*; the Paragon's position is *the men are not ready*; the truth is the chancery cannot pay the muster, because the Auxiliary Roll's true scale would have to be acknowledged to fund the advance honestly, and acknowledging it would require admitting the Bypassed Pensions crisis. The advance will not happen in PD 606. It may not happen in PD 610. The Paragon knows this and has not yet decided whether to break the chancery over it.

---

#### IV. NORTH AND SOUTH — WHAT IS NOT HELD

##### North of the Iron March — The Long Smoke

You travel north from Vigilstat and within two days the lit lamps end. The land rises into a thin chain of broken hills the chancery maps call **the Vigil Hills**. Past the hills, the land becomes the **Long Smoke** — a country burning continuously for six hundred years. The fires are slow, low, and never fully out; the smoke rises in a column visible from the upper towers of Sebastopyr on still days as a smudge on the northern horizon. The Cathedral teaches the Long Smoke is *the world's grief made visible*. The Ferrenkin teach it is *the surface burning of the lower delvings* — the same heat-from-below that drove their people up six centuries ago, now expressed in surface combustion. The Caer-Druin teach nothing because they will not look north.

The Hordes that come at the wall come mostly from the Long Smoke. The Hordeflesh of the Long Smoke is **thin and fast** — *horde-fangs*, the chancery's word, small bands of three to twenty, sometimes carrying writ-clerks. The Long Smoke is not surveyed past two days out. The chancery commissioned a survey in PD 597; the survey party was 23 souls; one returned with no eyes and could not speak; she lived eleven days and wrote one phrase on slate, *the count there is also kept*. She was buried under the Mort-Censorium and the slate is in the Audit-Below.

Maps published by the Cathedral show the Long Smoke as a single hatched region with the Old-Tongue legend **HIC FUMUS AETERNUS** (here is the eternal smoke). It is the only region on the chancery map drawn in the indicative case rather than the deemed; the editor who drew it that way died PD 597. The current chancery map-keeper has not yet corrected the mood. The error is therefore canon: by Cathedral grammar, the Long Smoke is the one place in Aevarn that has been admitted to be what it is.

##### South of the Mire March — The Plate-of-Wounds

South is worse. South is **the Plate-of-Wounds** — a flat, ash-grey, rock-and-bone plain the Hordes hold completely. It begins six leagues south of the Long Procession and runs to the world's southern edge, which the chancery teaches is *the end of the held world's mercy*. The Plate is crossed by no rivers (they all sink into the Hordeflesh sinkholes), holds no settlements, supports no life the chancery has admitted to. The Cathedral teaches the Plate was once *the Garden of Vespera* and that it became the Plate at the Fall when *all the gardens were given over*.

The truth, in the Audit-Below's ninth stratum: the Plate-of-Wounds was the **administrative heartland of the pre-Fall Saemurian Theocracy** — six city-prefectures, a court, and the Long Door through which the Theocracy bargained Hell into the world. The Plate is where the bargain was made. The chancery has known this for six hundred years and has chosen not to teach it.

The Plate-of-Wounds is approached from the kingdom along **the Mire March's southern edge**, where a wide salt-flat called **the Drowned Vespers** marks the border. Standing on the edge of the Drowned Vespers you can see the Plate beginning — flat, grey, slightly luminous at dusk, smelling of cold iron and incense. The Hordes do not come from the Plate; they wait there. The Reclamation Corps has not crossed the Drowned Vespers in twenty years. The Paragon has not crossed it. No one alive has.

---

#### V. WEST OF SEBASTOPYR — THE IRON SEA AND VESSELAIN ROADS

West of Sebastopyr the **Cathara floodplain** flattens for eleven bells and then the land breaks into the **Iron Sea** — Aevarn's western water, cold, grey, salt, prevailing-wind westerly. The coast is a hundred leagues of low cliffs cut by river-mouths and pebble beaches. Three things are on the coast that matter.

###### 10. **Vesselain Roads** (16 bells west-northwest of Sebastopyr)
The kingdom's only sea-port. Three sea-watch sloops of the Order, one Ferrenkin foundry-barge, four merchant cogs of mixed registry, two Caer-Druin singer-boats that go out to the lifting weather and come back. **Population 1,400**, walled with a single course of Ferrenkin black basalt (PD 592), commanded by Captain-Vested **Asperine Vesselain** — the heretic-broker (the canon-renamed Asperine Vesselain, formerly Asperine Nocta in older drafts; the same woman with the moveable Cinderbelow parlor *also* keeps a legitimate captaincy at Vesselain Roads under a clean roll-name, which is itself the perfect Constantine arrangement). The Cathedral suspects this. The chancery has not proven it. The Inquisition has interrogated her six times.

Vesselain Roads is where the kingdom's clean rain comes from — the lifting weather breaks against the Roads' cliffs and the rain that falls there is collected in cisterns and shipped east by ox-cart to Sebastopyr's western drains. The cistern-trade is run by **House Vell-os-Carrenost's** holding company (the same house that has the brimstone-shard monopoly; the brimstone goes east, the rain goes east, and the silver flows back west). It is the only fully clean economic transaction in the kingdom, and even it is curated — the cistern-records understate the rain take, and the missing third is sold privately to under-ward apothecaries who use it to fix masking-tincture batches that would otherwise read tainted.

###### 11. **Caer Vesselain** (4 bells north of Vesselain Roads, on a coastal headland)
A pre-collapse Caer-Druin fortified place, reclaimed in name only — the Cathedral keeps a Veriarch and a chapel there but the actual hold is administered by the Caer-Druin's coastal moiety, who have been there continuously for nine hundred years and who tolerate the Cathedral's presence with a courteous silence. The hold's reliquary-harps are still played at dusk by the Caer-Druin singers and the Cathedral has not interfered. Caer Vesselain is the only place in the kingdom where the Old Tongue's older substrate — the pre-Old-Tongue the Caer-Druin still partially speak — is heard openly. Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde has visited four times and stayed each time longer than the previous; the last visit she stayed eleven days and brought back two pages of notes in cursivus sebastinus minor that no one in the Cathedral but she can read.

###### 12. **The Drinking Coast** (south of Vesselain Roads, 8-22 bells)
A line of small fishing villages — **Saltgate**, **Pell's Landing**, **Bone-Stake**, **Lampgate-by-Sea**, **Old Vesperine** — each of fewer than two hundred souls, each with a chapel and a Veriarch and a single Ferrenkin smith. The Drinking Coast is the kingdom's quiet edge. It is poor, half-deserted in winter, full of pilgrims walking the coast in late summer for the saint-days of the western martyrs. The Order keeps a single light-tower at Bone-Stake and a single coastguard sloop that patrols the coast in good weather. The villages know each other's business, marry across one another, and trade fish for grain with Vesselain Roads. They are also the kingdom's quiet exit — three or four souls every winter slip onto a Caer-Druin singer-boat and are not heard from again. The Cathedral does not pursue. The chancery's quiet position is that those who leave westward are *deemed-lost-to-the-sea*, which is grammatically true.

---

#### VI. THE WIDER CONTINENT — UNHELD THERIMAUR

Beyond the Reclaimed Crown of Vespertin, Therimaur is **deemed-lost**. What follows is what is *known* — meaning *what records exist* in the Cathedral's published works, the Audit-Below's restricted strata, the Ferrenkin's forge-ledgers, and the Caer-Druin's vesper-songs. None of it is *seen*; all of it is *deemed-deemed* — a recursion the Cathedral does not perform on its own maps.

###### 13. **Hordeflesh Proper** (the entire eastern half of Therimaur, beyond the Drowned Vespers)
The Hordeflesh is the body of the land where Hell has settled into the soil. The Cathedral teaches it as a single region with a single name. The Ferrenkin's forge-ledgers describe at least **seven sub-territories** within it, each with a different character: the Boiling Strait (water), the Limecount (broken cities), the Spire-Walk (the standing remains of pre-Fall towers, occupied), the Slow Fields (a parody of farmland), the Audit House (a place where Hell maintains its own ledgers in real correspondence with the Long Ledger), the Doormouth (a hole in the world the Cathedral teaches does not exist), and **the Garden** (which the Ferrenkin will not describe). The Hordes that strike the wall come *from* the Hordeflesh; they are not *of* the Hordeflesh, in the same way an arrow is not of the bow. The Hordeflesh produces the arrows endlessly. The arrow-count, by Ferrenkin reckoning of horde-fang carcasses recovered at the wall, has not declined in six centuries.

###### 14. **The Northern Reach** (north of the Long Smoke, beyond the Vigil Hills, on the chancery map drawn as a single arrow pointing into white space)
What was once the **Theocratic Borderlands** of the pre-Fall Saemurian polity. The Cathedral teaches the Northern Reach is *Hordes and snow*. The Caer-Druin teach it is *empty* — that the Hordes do not occupy it because there is nothing there to occupy, and the snow has covered what was once the Theocracy's northern grain-belt. The two teachings are not in conflict if both are taken in the deemed mood. The Northern Reach is the most plausible direction for a quiet refusal that wishes not to be found.

###### 15. **The Sundered Cape** (the southwestern peninsula of Therimaur, broken from the mainland by the Cape Strait)
A jagged finger of land sticking south-southwest into the Iron Sea, broken from Therimaur proper by a shallow strait the Caer-Druin's southern moiety used to cross by reed-boat. The chancery does not list the Sundered Cape on current maps. The Caer-Druin sing about it in a winter canto called *the Cape's Last Hymn*, which has fourteen verses and which the Cathedral has not folded into vesper-mass because the Cathedral cannot translate it. The Cape is **not held** by Hordes; the Cape is **abandoned**. The Caer-Druin's southern moiety walked off it during the Long Vigil of PD 583 — every soul, in one autumn — and joined their northern brethren at Sebastopyr. The Cape has therefore been empty of human and elder presence for twenty-three years. It is reachable, by sea, by Caer-Druin singer-boat. The Cathedral has never visited.

---

```
        ~        \_______                             ____/   ~
        ~                ====== PLATE-OF-WOUNDS =====         ~
        ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~  (deemed-lost,                  ~~
                              Garden of Vespera,
                              Saemurian Theocratic heartland)
                                       |
                                       S

         [Sundered Cape, off-map SW, abandoned PD 583]
         [Hordeflesh interior, off-map E: seven sub-territories]
         [Northern Reach, off-map N: empty under snow]

   Distance Sebastopyr-Ferrostat:  63 bells / 47.5 leagues
   Distance bell:  3/4 league (chancery, curated)
   Wind: prevailing W (rain) and E (Censer)
   Rivers east of Sustines: now flow west into Hordeflesh sinkholes
```

---

#### VIII. WHAT THE LANDSCAPE REMEMBERS

Six centuries of siege have *lived in* the kingdom's geography in ways the Cathedral does not name on its maps but which any traveler with a good eye and a quiet conversation can read:

- **The killing-grounds outside every walled town are striped with bone-meal**, mixed into the soil to make the vigil-grain grow. The chancery teaches this as *the holy mixing*. The under-wards know it as *the bone-pour*. The yield is higher than wheat would be without it.
- **No tree in the Iron March is older than 130 years.** The wood was burned in PD 477 during the Great Censer Year when the Cathedral burned the eastern forests to deny the horde-fangs cover. The replanting was haphazard and the chancery's forester-rolls are a fiction.
- **Every milestone on the Long Procession has been carved twice**, and on close inspection you can see the second carving over the first. The original distances were in pre-Fall stadia; the recutting in PD 588 changed them to bells. The Ferrenkin who recut them left a single rod-count incised on the back of every twentieth milestone for anyone who knows to read it.
- **The lamp-poles in the Almongate Plain are made of Ferrenkin iron**, but the lanterns are made of Caer-Druin glass — a quiet division of labor that has persisted for two hundred years and that the Cathedral does not credit because the Cathedral teaches the lamp as a single Vespertine artifact.
- **The chapels in every town in the Iron March have an empty north-facing alcove.** The Cathedral teaches this as the *Place of the Coming Saint* — an architectural devotional preserving room for the next Paragon. The pre-PD 583 chapels do not have the alcove. The post-PD 588 chapels do. The retrofit of the older chapels began PD 590 and continues; the diocesan budget for *Alcoves of the Coming* is the only line-item in the chancery's published accounts that has grown every year for sixteen years.
- **The bridges in the Mire March are all Ferrenkin work and all signed.** Each bridge has a maker's mark cut into the underside of its first arch, including the date in rod-counts. The Mort Bridge at Banner-Fall is signed *Brak Iron-Eye, Anno Damnationis 595*. Brak Iron-Eye is the same Ferrenkin who keeps the private slate in the Cinderbelow forge with the true wall-tower count. He has signed every major bridge in the kingdom. The Cathedral does not know the bridges are signed.

---

#### IX. AT NIGHT, FROM A HIGH PLACE

If you climb to the upper Pyric Wall of Sebastopyr on a clear cold night in late autumn and look east, this is what you see, from nearest to farthest:

The lamp-poles of the Almongate Plain — a chain of yellow points in the dark, regular as a litany.

The watchfires of Old Pell's Crossing — three bright points at the ford.

The walls of Vigilstat — a smudge of warmer light low on the horizon, the lamp-watch and the chapel windows.

Beyond that, dark.

Then, much farther — the column-fire of the Long Smoke to the north, a slow flicker on the northern horizon, never bright, never out.

Then, eastward, on still nights only, a faint glow that is **Ferrostat's curtain-lamps** — sixty-three leagues away, just visible through the iron-tasting Censer Wind. The Pyrian children call this glow *the Hand's Lamp* and believe (incorrectly) that it is the Paragon's reading-candle in the Hand's Keep. It is in fact the muster-lights of Ferrostat's outer redoubt, which are kept lit all night so that the horde-fangs out in the Mire can see they are being watched.

Past that — past the kingdom — there is no light. The Hordeflesh does not light its fires for human eyes. Ferrenkin watchers on the upper Pyric towers, who can see further than men, report a faint movement of pale shapes in the eastern dark that the chancery has classified as *atmospheric*. The Ferrenkin's forge-ledgers describe these shapes as *the carrion that walks, the count that keeps itself*. The Sixth Notary's writ-clerks have been working at the eastern edge of the Mire March for six months in the dark and the chancery does not know.

The bell tolls compline. The wall-marshal makes his round. The lamps of the kingdom hold. The eastern wind smells of iron and incense and burned bone. The land has been like this for six hundred years and twenty-three. The doctrine says it can be otherwise.

*Sustineo et numero.* I endure and I count.

The lamp does not go out — yet.

---
