---

*Geography is a ledger the world keeps in stone. The chancery edits the printed copy. The Ferrenkin keep the original. The Caer-Druin sing it. The Hordes know all of it and tell no one. The Paragon stands at Ferrostat and does not know that the road behind him has been recarved and the road in front of him cannot be built.*

*The lamp does not go out — yet. The bell rings. The count is kept.*

*Per Sebast.*

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:geography_climate` (geography and climate)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* Sebastopyr sits on the Sebastine Promontory — a basalt prow thrust into the Cauldron Sea where the Therimaur continent buckles before falling into the brackish marshes of the Mire March. The city's siting is its first theology: the Cathedral occupies the highest tor (the Sebast-Crag), so the Pyric Wall does not merely surround the city, it descends in tiered circuits down the crag toward the landward gates, meaning every Pyrian lives perpetually downhill from the Cathedral and uphill from the under-wards — Grace, in Sebastopyr, literally flows downhill in the form of the Cantor's Aqueduct, which carries blessed water from the Crag's spring through the Sanctuary Ring down through the Choir Ring, the Marshal Ring, the Common Ring, and arrives in the Under-Ward Ring already cycled through six hundred years of municipal use, which the Cinderbelow drinks. The 20-year-thaw has done a particular thing to Sebastopyr: it has changed which gates matter. For six centuries the only gates were the Pyric Gates (sealed, ceremonial, opened only for sallies and corpse-details). Now the new Reclaimed Gate — punched through the wall in year 7 of the Paragonate to permit the Aurriste Road convoys — has become the commercial heart of the city, and a whole new district of warehouses, contractor offices, and chartered banks has sprung up against the inside of the curtain wall, a parasitic crescent the older houses call the Wen. The frontier has made Sebastopyr richer and uglier; the Cinderbelow has not seen a copper of it. The climate sits inside the city as a daily fact: the Pyric Smother (a permanent low-pressure inversion held in place by the Cathedral's wardings and the smoke of forty thousand chimneys) means the sky is always a low grey lid, and a clear day is called a Reading Day because the inquisition's instruments work better — it is also a day people stay indoors, because being LEGIBLE in Sebastopyr is dangerous. Inside the Pyric Wall, distance is measured not in miles but in BELLS: how many tolls of the Pyric Bell it takes to walk between two points at a penitent's pace. The Cathedral to the Carcer is Nine Bells; the Reclaimed Gate to the Cinderbelow is Three Bells but downhill, which Pyrians say with a particular emphasis.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The smell of the Pyric Smother in late autumn: wet basalt, censer-resin, gun-grease, and the faint chemical sweetness of the Ferrenkin foundries running the night-shift in the Cinderbelow — Pyrians call it 'the breath of the Pyr' and the Caer-Druin call it 'the long incense' and refuse to inhale through the mouth.
> - The sound of the Hush-Wind at the Outpost: a tone-deaf moan that comes off the Drownmire at dusk and carries no birdsong with it — the Mournwing scouts say it is the sound of un-sung air, air no throat has yet shaped, and they refuse to fly into it.
> - A child's rhyme sung in the Common Ring: 'One bell mother, two bell crown, / three bell hunger, four bell down, / five bell candle, six bell rain, / seven bell saint, but he don't come again.' (Mothers stop their children at six.)
> - The Old-Tongue curse 'Ad Mire!' — 'to the Mire!' — used by frontier soldiers the way other cities use 'to hell,' but spat rather than spoken; in the Carcer it is a death-threat and in the Cinderbelow it is just an exhalation.
> - The exact gesture a Vesperine inquisitor uses when crossing the Cantor's Aqueduct: two fingers laid against the stone and lifted to touch the tongue, tasting the water at that elevation. They will not tell you what they are tasting for.
> - Black incense called Vigilum, burned only at the watch-change on the Pyric Wall, smelling of iron filings and burnt resin and something faintly meaty — the recipe is Ferrenkin and the Cathedral has been unable to reproduce it for four centuries despite knowing every ingredient by weight.

---

## II. Pantheon — The Divine, Grace, and the Damned

### The Divine and the Pantheon
##### A Theological Document of the Vespertine Cathedrate, As Sanctioned and As Suspected
*Cathedrate-of-Sebastopyr / Office of Doctrinal Liturgy / for clergy use, lay catechesis, and the unsealed strata of the Audit-Below*

> *"Sustineo et numero. I endure and I count. There is no third clause."*
> — opening antiphon of the Vespers of the Wall, attributed to Saint Severa di Pyrigorne, PD 47, redacted twice

> *"There is no third clause because the third clause is the price, and the price is not for the singer."*
> — marginalia in the same antiphon, in cursivus sebastinus minor, hand unidentified, Audit-Below stratum six

---

#### I. THE DIVINE — Nature, Names, Structure

##### A. The Single Confession

The Cathedrate confesses **ONE God**, called in liturgy **the Enduring One** (Old Tongue *Sebastus Aeternus*, vocative *Sebaste*), and known in the seven other sanctioned addresses corresponding to the seven concentric courses of the Pyric Wall. The Enduring One is held to be:

| Attribute | Old Tongue formula | Operational consequence |
|---|---|---|
| Singular | *Unus Sebastus* | No second god is confessed; all other agencies are creatures, angels, demons, or saints |
| Wounded | *Vulneratus, Non Frangens* | God endured the arrows; God did not break; the wound is real and is still open |
| Attentive | *Aspector Mundi* | God can LOOK; the look is finite, costly, and the cause of the Paragon |
| Withholding | *Qui Differt* | God's silence is doctrinally a *deferral*, not an absence — a theological cope of monumental tensile load |
| Indebted-to-none | *Sine Debito* | God strikes no Bargain; the price-clause does not apply upward |
| Past-tense | *Qui Stetit* | "He Stood"; in the strict liturgical register God has no future tense |
| Operational | *Qui Manat in Gratia* | God is fuel that flows through rite; God is met in the meter |

The seventh attribute is the dangerous one and the operative one. It is the only doctrine the laity is taught with full vigor; the other six are taught in proportion to the parish's literacy.

##### B. The Seven Addresses (One God, Seven Names)

Cathedrate orthodoxy holds that the Enduring One is one being addressed by seven cases — not seven persons, not a trinity-doubled, but a SINGLE GOD invoked under the case-ending appropriate to the petitioner's need. The cases mirror the seven concentric courses of the Pyric Wall and the seven strata of the Audit-Below, which the Cantorial Scribes consider not a coincidence.

| Course | Address | Case | Petitionary use | Doctrinal status |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| First (outermost) | **Sebaste** | vocative | the soldier's last cry at the wall | universal, taught to all |
| Second | **Sebastum** | accusative | the supplicant's reach (Grace-petition) | universal |
| Third | **Sebasto** | dative | the gift-direction (oath, vow, tithe) | universal |
| Fourth | **Sebasti** | genitive | "of the Enduring One" (relic-claim, saint-claim) | restricted to clergy |
| Fifth | **Sebaste-Aspector** | vocative + attributive | called only by the dying and by those who have BEEN looked-upon (Paragons) | restricted; one living user |
| Sixth | **Sebasto-in-Tenebris** | dative + locative | the address in deep darkness — used only in the Audit-Below | restricted to Cantorial Scribes and the Sebast-Auditor |
| Seventh (innermost, hypothetical) | *unnamed* | reserved | held by doctrine to exist; doctrine holds that NO MORTAL has cause to use it | *the seventh case is itself a gap-fill — see Heresies §V* |

The Cathedrate's official position on the seventh address is that the case exists but is empty, like the empty seat at the Custodes Numeri's table. Compare the **Heresy of the Indicative Speaker** (§V.D).

##### C. The Two Things the Divine Is Not

1. **The Divine is NOT belief.** Conviction does not refill Grace. Doubt does not deplete it. A faithless mercenary and a weeping zealot draw the same pool by the same rules; both can be RIGHT WITH THE METER and wrong with God.
2. **The Divine is NOT mercy in the sentimental sense.** The Cathedrate confesses *misericordia operativa* — operational mercy, mercy that calculates, mercy with a price-clause. The mercies that do not calculate are administered by demons (see §VI.E, the Cathedrate's quiet doctrine of *misericordia infernalis*).

---

#### II. SANCTIONED DOCTRINE — What the Cathedrate Teaches

Three doctrinal pillars stand as the **Sanctioned Confession of the Reclaimed Crown of Vespertin**, promulgated in the Concilium Sebastinum of PD 587 and amended thrice. Every Pyrian child memorizes them in the Polished form by age nine. The Unpolished form is held in the Audit-Below.

##### A. The Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity (PD 589)

> *"The war that was deemed eternal has been deemed-otherwise. The Enduring One has Looked, and the Look has issued a Paragon, and the Paragon is the sign of the rescission. What was eternal in our blindness is finite in our sight. We march."*

**Principal author:** Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste, drafted at age 31, signed by Sebastopater Cassian VII fourteen months before the latter's death.

**The Polished gloss (taught to laity):** the war is winnable; the Paragon is the proof; the kingdom is the consequence.

**The Unpolished gloss (taught to Custodes Numeri):** the war was never deemed eternal in earnest. The doctrine of eternity was a managerial posture by which the Cathedrate explained its inability to advance. The Look did not END the eternity; the Look ENDED the explanation. We are not winning; we are no longer *permitted* to call it eternal.

**The Buried gloss (cursivus sebastinus minor, Audit-Below stratum four):** "And the rescission requires a single Paragon. The previous Paragons must be unmade for this one to be authentic. The price of the new eternity is the burial of the old singularities. Count them well." Hand: a redacted Sebastopater. Stratum verified by Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde, who has not spoken of it.

##### B. The Doctrine of Operational Grace (PD c. 100, codified PD 587)

> *"Grace is the fuel of the Enduring One's attention, granted by rite, spent by rite, recovered by rite. There is no Grace outside the meter. The faithful are not radiant; they are accounted."*

**Operational consequences:**

- **Grace is a number.** Every cleric in the Crown has a Grace-roll. The Paragon's is 1240 (declining; chancery records show ~73% of peak).
- **Grace is RATIONED.** The Vas Halidani — the seventeen-ton consecrated cistern in the Sanctuary Ring — empties by sext on most days; the chancery has begun consolidating the thirteen-hour rite to extend the supply.
- **Grace REFUSES the unworthy by ABSENCE, not by judgment.** A soul whose rite is wrong simply receives nothing. The meter does not condemn; it does not respond. This is theologically critical and Constantine to the bone: the Divine does not punish the inadequate rite. It declines to *fund* it.
- **Grace cannot be borrowed across souls** (orthodox) — except by the Oath of Numeration, which is the Order of the Stood Line's mass-Grace-pooling rite, which the Cathedrate has sanctioned and the Inquisition has reservations about. See *libellus gratiae*, the Grace-chit.

**The Polished gloss:** Grace is God's gift, rationed because the war is hard.

**The Buried gloss:** Grace is rationed because *something is consuming it that is not rite*. The Vas Halidani's drainage has tripled since PD 583. The Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste's PD 599 audit attributed the loss to "the Paragon's sustaining attention upon the frontier." The Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde's PD 604 musical audit attributed the loss to "an unmetered withdrawal at the seventh address." She filed the second report and the chancery shelved it.

##### C. The Doctrine of the Three Bargains (PD 587)

The Cathedrate confesses that mortals strike three kinds of bargain, and confesses that **two of them are sanctioned**: the Divine Bargain (oath, vow, binding) and the Mortal Bargain (debt, favor, marker). The Demonic Bargain is anathematized.

> *"The Enduring One offers the Oath; the brother offers the Debt; only hell offers the Trade-for-Stain."*

**The Polished gloss:** the Cathedrate is on the right side of the ledger.

**The Unpolished gloss:** the binding-formula of the Curiate Vincula's Divine Bargain is *word-for-word identical* to the heretic-broker clause confiscated at PD 712. The chancery position is that the heretics stole it. The founding ledger marginalia, in cursivus sebastinus minor, records the reverse. The price-clause was inherited from somewhere older than the Cathedrate, and the legally-mandated breath of silence between grant-clause and price-clause — the *gap-where-the-saint-stood* — was inserted to disguise this. In 314 years of records, no oath-taker has ever withdrawn at the gap.

The Cathedrate is doing what hell does. It does so in love. It does so under license. It does not see itself doing so, and this not-seeing is itself the price.

---

#### III. DOCTRINAL SCHOOLS — Where the Orthodox Disagree

Within sanctioned orthodoxy, four schools contend. None of these is heretical; all are LICENSED disputes inside the Concilium. The DM should track which school any clerical NPC belongs to; it determines what they fear, what they accept, and what they will not sign.

##### A. The Pyric Cathedrate (the wall-school)
- **Center:** the Cathedral and the Pyric Wall proper
- **Trained at:** the Pyric Seminary in the Sanctuary Ring
- **Tenet:** the wall is the Divine's preferred site of action. Grace expended in defense of the wall is grace *most pleasing*. The Paragon is a wall-saint by origin and must remain a wall-figure by function. Eastward advance is theologically secondary.
- **Quiet position:** the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity is operationally correct but theologically OVER-INTERPRETED. The Look did not rescind; the Look *visited*.
- **Living standard-bearers:** Sebastopater Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX (trained here); Archvigil Severa di Mauritz; Marshal-Vested Orric Veillarde of the Lower Pyr (covertly).
- **Throughline weight:** TEST 2 (damnation hides — the wall-school is least equipped to imagine the rot is INSIDE the wall)

##### B. The Almonine (the parish-school)
- **Center:** the under-ward parishes (Lamplost, Quietus, the Carcer)
- **Trained at:** apprenticeship to a Veriarch; no central seminary
- **Tenet:** Grace expended in mercy is grace most pleasing. The wall and the frontier are necessary, but the COUNT of the Crown is in its parishes. The Paragon's miracle was a parish-soul lifted; the kingdom's righteousness is in whether the parish soul is still being lifted.
- **Quiet position:** the Octave Bargain Velim Aurriste struck has costs the parish is paying. The Bypassed Pensions crisis is THEIR crisis.
- **Living standard-bearers:** Veriarch Thelos di Cinderost (Lamplost; also the secret head of the Reflected printer's press); the Almoners' Vigil; Marshal-Vested Severa Aurriste-cadet (Almonine by sympathy, Pyric by training, the most spiritually conflicted senior cleric in the city).
- **Throughline weight:** TEST 5 (sacred-and-seedy share the street — the Almonine LIVE on that street)

##### C. The Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity (the triumphal-school)
- **Center:** the Choir Ring chancery and the Custodes Numeri
- **Trained at:** the Doctrinal Seminary, founded PD 591
- **Tenet:** the Look was an explicit rescission. The war is winnable AND will be won. Eastward advance is theologically PRIMARY. The frontier is the new wall.
- **Quiet position:** the Paragon's singularity is doctrinal necessity. To suggest prior Paragons is to suggest the rescission has happened before and reverted, which is to suggest the rescission can revert again, which is to threaten the doctrine that the kingdom is built on.
- **Living standard-bearers:** Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste; Hierarch-of-the-Mire Cassian Aurriste; the regent Mauritz Veillarde di Lampgard (by political alignment).
- **Throughline weight:** TEST 4 (the righteous are the danger — Velim is the world's most certain righteous man, and the Octave Bargain is what his certainty cost)

##### D. The Eternalist Remnant (the wait-school)
- **Center:** scattered; openly tolerated, quietly hated
- **Trained at:** no formal school; passed in writings and in the Watch-Cantos verses the Caer-Druin sing on dusk
- **Tenet:** the eternity was not rescinded. The Look was a comfort, not a verdict. The Paragon is real but is a SAINT, not a sign of the war's end. To advance is to forfeit the wall's protection. To unify the doctrine around eastward conquest is to invite a worse century than the six.
- **Quiet position:** they are correct, and they suspect the Cantorial Scribes know it. The murders begin here, in the Eternalist correspondence intercepted by the Inquisition.
- **Living standard-bearers:** Archvigil Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost (covert, would deny if asked); the Caer-Druin chorus; the late Confessor Thelos di Carrenost (murdered PD 605, an Eternalist sympathizer).
- **Throughline weight:** TEST 6 (the official story is curated — they REMEMBER the official story was edited and have begun to count the cuts)

##### E. The Schism in Motion (PD 606)

The Eternalist / Triumphalist schism is the **present-moment political fact** of Sebastopyr's theology. Pyric Cathedrate and Almonine sit between, alarmed in different directions. The Vesperine Loyalty Tally — the secret Vesperine-clergy purge-list prepared by Hierarch Cassian Aurriste's secretary Marent de la Pyrille — is the FIRST chancery instrument that crosses the line from licensed dispute to enforced orthodoxy. If it is published, the Eternalists become heretics overnight. The chancery has not decided whether to publish.

---

#### IV. THE DIVINE AND THE WAR

The Cathedrate's war-theology is the **Doctrine of Operative Witness** (PD 312, amended PD 589):

> *"The Enduring One does not fight. The Enduring One ENDURES, and FUNDS the enduring. The hand on the wall is the soldier's; the Grace in the hand is God's; the choice to spend is the soldier's; the cost of the spending is the soldier's; the witness of the spending is God's."*

This is doctrine carefully phrased to absolve the Divine of complicity in any specific death and to throw the moral weight of every wall-defense onto the SOLDIER and the CHANCERY that rations the Grace.

**Operational consequences for the war:**

1. **God does not pick winners.** Grace is granted by rite, not by righteousness-of-cause. The Hordes have no Grace; the Cathedrate does. This is *given*, not *proved*.
2. **God does not heal indiscriminately.** Battlefield healing is rite-bound and metered. The Cathedrate has never confessed that the Divine could end the war and is choosing not to; the Eternalists have suspected it, and have been quiet about suspecting it, because the alternative (God CANNOT) is worse.
3. **The Paragon is the war's only known exception.** The Look was unilateral. It was not solicited. The Cathedrate has spent twenty-three years TRYING TO REPRODUCE THE CONDITIONS of the Look (the *Vocatio Aurriste* chant exists; it has been performed nine times since PD 587; nothing has happened). The doctrinal position is that the Look "is given when it is given, and is not coerced." The Custodes Numeri's position is that the Look is given **when the count permits** — which is a heresy in its own house.
4. **The war FUNDS the doctrine.** Every dawn the Hordes break against the wall, and every dawn the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity needs a Paragon for the Hordes to be breaking *against*. If the Paragon falls, the doctrine falls; if the doctrine falls, six centuries' worth of accumulated theological certainty about what the Divine is and is not falls with it. The chancery's interest in the Paragon's continued existence is therefore not merely sentimental.

**The war is theologically what the Bargain is personally.** Power-now-paid-in-price-later, both at the scale of the soldier and at the scale of the kingdom. The Cathedrate has not noticed it has confessed this; the Cantorial Scribes have, and have made it a matter of working policy.

---

#### V. HERESIES (AND WHICH MIGHT BE RIGHT)

Six heresies are NAMED in the *Index Haeresium Sebastinarum*, the chancery's working schedule of error. Every one of them might be correct. The DM should treat each as both a doctrinal threat AND a potential live wire.

##### A. The Heresy of Multiplied Paragons (Numeralism)
- **Claim:** There have been many Paragons before Halidan. The doctrine of singularity is a lie of curation.
- **Adherents:** the Brothers of the Cinder Hand (Hester Brunn, Tomas Reyes, Skar Slag-Hand); four defected Inquisitor-Vested; possibly Postulant Liturge di Carrenost; the Caer-Druin chorus quietly.
- **Probability of correctness:** **HIGH.** Per the Audit-Below, 73 named + 48 nameless = 121 suppressed paragon cases between PD 51 and PD 583. The Cantorial Scribes' closed sheets are the evidence. The chancery's response is to call the heresy "the Numeralist error" and the heretics "Cohort-counters" — pejoratively, because counting is the chancery's own sacrament.
- **Why it has not won:** because **Halidan himself does not know**. If the Mournwing Letter is ever answered, the heresy is canon.

##### B. The Heresy of the Empty Look (Visional Nihilism)
- **Claim:** The Look that found Halden Orriste was not the Enduring One. It was the Quartermaster of Tongues' second offer, accepted in the moment of refusal.
- **Adherents:** an unmapped cell; the heretic-broker Asperine Vesselain has used the formula in three contracts; the Mournwing intelligence files contain unattributed copies.
- **Probability of correctness:** **UNKNOWN, AND THIS IS THE POINT.** Halidan himself has not been certain for twenty-three years. The Cathedrate's official position is that the heresy is "psychologically explicable as the Paragon's humility, doctrinally untenable." But the account is OPEN in hell's Long Ledger, and no one knows what it means that it is open.
- **Why it has not won:** because there is no proof either way, and the doctrine cannot afford the test.

##### C. The Heresy of the Operational God (Mechanism)
- **Claim:** The Enduring One is *exhausted as fuel.* Grace is real but the source is depleting, not deferred. The Vas Halidani's increased drainage is evidence. The war will end not in victory but in the Grace running dry.
- **Adherents:** Brak Iron-Eye (Ferrenkin smith, keeps a private tower-count and a private Grace-reservoir ledger); Bera Quist (the translation-shock physician, who has noticed the rite-Grace is harder to administer per soul each year); fragments of the Order's quartermaster corps.
- **Probability of correctness:** **PLAUSIBLE.** The chancery's three quiet recalibrations of the aspersoir clinical-concern threshold AND the Grace-cistern drainage curve are the data, and the data has not been published.
- **Why it has not won:** because to admit it is to admit the war is unwinnable, and the kingdom is built on the war being winnable.

##### D. The Heresy of the Indicative Speaker
- **Claim:** The Enduring One is not *Qui Stetit* (past tense). The Old Tongue's lack of liturgical future is not God's grammar; it is the founders' theology imposed onto grammar. God speaks in the *indicative present* and has been doing so all along, and the seventh address has a USER, and that user is in Carcer cell eight, and what he is saying in pre-Fall Saemurian indicative is what the Divine is saying right now.
- **Adherents:** unknown. The Indicative Speaker himself has not been visited in eleven years. The Veriarch who attends his cell is a deaf Almonine who cannot understand him.
- **Probability of correctness:** **UNKNOWN, AND DEEPLY DANGEROUS.** If true, the entire liturgical apparatus is grammatically wrong, and the past-tense Divine has been an artifact of doctrinal grammar for six centuries.
- **Why it has not won:** because no one alive speaks pre-Fall Saemurian. The translation requires the Caer-Druin elder Brigith's-niece-twice-removed, and she has not been asked.

##### E. The Heresy of the Demonic Mercy (*Misericordia Infernalis*)
- **Claim:** Hell offers *sentimental* mercy — uncalculating, uncosted-at-the-moment-of-offer — while the Cathedrate offers only *operational* mercy. Therefore, in the moment of offer, hell is the kinder party. This is sealed-doctrine in the Cathedrate, quietly known, and NEVER preached, because the laity would believe it.
- **Adherents:** the Sixth Notary's clients; the Lampbreaker's clients; everyone who has ever lost a child in the Quietus Ward and been offered a brimstone-shard by the Galiethrin's intermediary.
- **Probability of correctness:** **TRUE AT THE MOMENT OF OFFER, FALSE OVER TIME.** The Cathedrate's theology of *misericordia operativa* holds that hell's mercy is real *in the instant* and catastrophic over the ledger, which is the most Constantine doctrinal position in the entire confession. The heresy is calling true what the Cathedrate has CONFESSED IN PRIVATE for centuries and has refused to confess in public.
- **Why it has not won:** because to preach it is to admit that the Cathedrate's mercy is harder than hell's, and the parish would walk.

##### F. The Heresy of the Withheld Saints (Suppressionism)
- **Claim:** Specifically: the Cantorial Scribes have CURATED the saint count. The Plate of Sebastian is not "blessed unnamed"; it is the bone-layer of saints whose canonization was revised because their existence undermined a later doctrine. The 143-saint plateau is an artifact of editing, not of God's slowed gift.
- **Adherents:** Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde (silently); Postulant Liturge di Carrenost (closing); the Mournwing chorus-keepers (in their own martyr-rolls).
- **Probability of correctness:** **CERTAIN.** The evidence is the Audit-Below itself. The reason it is still a heresy is that the evidence is sealed.
- **Why it has not won:** because no one has been able to walk out of the Audit-Below with the evidence. The bone-handled scalpels of the Cantorial Scribes ensure this.

---

#### VI. THE PARAGON'S THEOLOGICAL STATUS

> *"He is real. The miracle is real. The Look was real. Everything around him is curated."*
> — the operative throughline, in the words a DM should hold in mind

##### A. The Sanctioned Status: ASPIRANT

The Concilium Sebastinum of PD 587 invented the rank of **Aspirant** specifically and exclusively for Halidan Aurriste, because canonization is reserved for the dead and the Cathedrate had no precedent for a living saint. The Aspirant is held to be:

- a soul **looked-upon** by the Enduring One
- a soul **operationally saintly** (Grace-pool above 1000, miracles attested, no measurable Stain in 23 years of daily reading)
- a soul **not yet canonized**, pending death

The Aspirant rank is itself a doctrinal HEDGE. It permits the Cathedrate to venerate Halidan without committing the dangerous theological claim that a saint walks the kingdom. It also permits the chancery to withhold canonization indefinitely, which it has been doing for 23 years.

##### B. The Buried Status: WEARY, REAL, INHERITOR OF A CURATED LIE

Halidan is genuinely a holy man. The miracle was real. His daily Stain-readings come back CLEAN because there is nothing to find. The danger is not that he is corrupt; the danger is sevenfold:

1. **He stands on a curated singularity.** The doctrine of "the first in living memory" was already a lie when it was promulgated. The Audit-Below holds at least 73 named prior Aspirant-cases.
2. **His surname is a polished accident.** "Orriste" was polished to "Aurriste" by chancery clerks in PD 588. The Aurriste keel-throne in the Cathedral was installed in PD 73, four centuries before Halden Orriste was born. The two facts have never been cross-referenced. The chancery clerk who would have flagged it had a stroke in PD 602.
3. **His Grace is declining.** Chancery records show ~73% of peak. Projected to reach minimum-operational threshold in 11 years. The Cathedrate has not informed him.
4. **He has an OPEN ACCOUNT in hell's Long Ledger.** The Quartermaster of Tongues offered him a bargain on the night of the Standing. He refused. The account is still open. He has never been certain the Look that found him moments later was the Enduring One's and not the Quartermaster's second offer accepted unknowing. He has not asked.
5. **His confessor reads him clean and does not know why.** Confessor-Ordinary Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost has filed 23 years of CLEAN readings on a 51-year-old Aspirant whose Grace expenditure is at a level that should produce *some* anomaly *somewhere*. Mauritz has filed the suspicion to no one. He suspects he is filing a curated reality, and he is.
6. **His daily reality is filtered by Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind, in the city, for 23 years.** What reaches the Paragon from the chancery is what Mortane decides reaches him. What reaches the Sebastopater from Ferrostat is what Mortane decides reaches HIM. The dual-Vesperine filter is two devout men editing the truth in love.
7. **He has begun to ask.** The Mournwing Letter of PD 605 asks the chancery "how many saints have there been." Intercepted by Mortane. Filed without answer. The chancery has not decided what to do if he asks again.

##### C. The Three Possible Futures of the Paragon (theological, not dramatic)

| Future | Doctrinal consequence |
|---|---|
| Canonized in death without his question being answered | the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity is preserved; the Crown's keel holds; the lie is sealed for another century |
| Receives the answer to his question (he is not the first) | the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity collapses; the Eternalists are vindicated; the Cathedrate must theologically restructure |
| The Quartermaster of Tongues' account is collected | the singular living miracle of the kingdom is revealed (rightly or wrongly) as a demonic bargain; the kingdom does not survive the revelation |

The DM should hold all three as live.

---

#### VII. SAINTS, MARTYRS, BEATIFIED FIGURES — The Sanctioned Roster

The Cathedrate confesses **143 saints** in the plateau-count (no new canonizations in 81 years). The list below is a working catechism — the saints lay Pyrians actually know — not the full roster.

##### A. The Patriarch-Saints (the Five Pillars)

| Saint | Liturgical name | Feast | Domain | Polished story | Buried complication |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Saint Sebastus the Enduring** | *Sebastus Aeternus, the Arrow-Stander* | Octave of Triumph (PD 583 anniversary) | endurance, walls, the wall-watch | the founding saint; shot through with arrows, stood; was martyred a second time by clubbing | the city's name encodes both the standing AND the futility of the standing; the founders chose the name knowing |
| **Saint Severa di Pyrigorne** | *Severa Numeratrix, Reader-of-the-First-Numbers* | Reading of the Numbers (PD 47) | counting, sacred numeracy, the Inquisition | martyred for completing the first Count of the Saved; her tongue cut out and her hand spared so she could continue counting | the Numbers she counted included a saint-name the chancery later removed; her Audit-Below stratum is sealed |
| **Saint Halidan-not-yet** | *the Aspirant* (provisional) | NO FEAST (canonization withheld) | the living Look | the only living entry on the roster | he does not know he is on it; the Aspirant-rank IS the feast-substitute |
| **Saint Quietus of the Wall** | *Quietus-of-the-Wall, the Stiller of Bargains* | the Held Breath (dawn rite, daily) | refusal of demonic offers in the moment of crisis | refused the Long Ledger at the wall and held the line; the dawn breath of silence across the city honors his refusal | his refusal cost the eleven souls of his cohort; the chancery teaches the refusal as triumph and edits the eleven |
| **Saint Brigith of the Drowned Song** | *Brigith Halloran, the Singer-Drowned* | Vespers of the Drowned (PD 312 anniversary) | Caer-Druin liturgy, the Watch-Cantos | a Caer-Druin singer whose songs warded the high places; drowned in the holy-mouths reversal of PD 312 | she was DROWNED BY THE CATHEDRATE; her songs were taken; the Caer-Druin remember and do not say |

##### B. The Lesser Martyrs (selected, for parish use)

- **Saint Asperine of the Lamps** — Lampwarden of Lamplost, burned in the Cinderbelow fire of PD 391, patron of under-ward parishes and of any soul who tends a flame they cannot afford. Feast: the Last Lamp (variable, set by Almonine reckoning).
- **Saint Velim Aurriste-the-Elder** — NOT the living Cantor-Magisterial; a Vesperine confessor canonized PD 412 for refusing the Cathedrate's order to break the seal of a heretic's confession. Feast: the Sealed Mouth. *Note: the living Velim Aurriste was named for him and may be his deliberate doctrinal opposite, which the Cantor-Magisterial has never publicly addressed.*
- **Saint Mauritz Veillarde of the First Mire** — first reclamation-saint, died in the early Ferrostat outpost in PD 590, patron of the Reclamation Corps. Feast: the First Mire.
- **Saint Liturge of the Counted Children** — Almoner of Quietus Ward, kept the parish ledger of the children of the plague-year PD 471 so that none would die uncounted; canonized PD 489. Feast: the Counted (variable).
- **Saint Thelos di Cinderost** — NOT the living Veriarch of Lamplost; a Cinderbelow priest of PD 502 who is the Veriarch's chosen patronymic-saint, canonized for printing a missal in vulgar Vespertine so the under-ward could read the rite. The Reflected printer's press is the Veriarch's continuation. *The Inquisition has not connected the names.*

##### C. The Beatified (Not Canonized)

Beatification is the Cathedrate's holding-rank — souls whose sanctity is attested but whose canonization is pending. There are **2,389 beatified figures** on the chancery roll. The vast majority are Reclamation-era frontier dead. The chancery has not canonized any of them in 81 years.

**Why not.** Each canonization would require theological assertion of God's continued issuance of saints, which would complicate the doctrine of the Paragon's singularity. The Triumphal school resists. The Pyric Cathedrate has begun to push. The Almonine has stopped asking.

**The Beatified Aspirant-Adjacent Cases (sealed, in the Audit-Below).** Within the 2,389 are 121 cases whose beatification records carry the marginal note *Aspirantis Cognatio* — "Aspirant-adjacent." These are the suppressed Paragon-cases. The Cantorial Scribes have moved them from "candidate-canonization" to "candidate-beatification-only" to "sealed pending review." The review has been pending for between 23 and 555 years.

##### D. The Plate of Sebastian (the Buried Count)

Beneath the Cathedral, a 40-foot stratum of **fused saint-bone, slag iron, and consecrated mortar** — the lowest reinforced course of the Sanctuary Ring's foundation. The chancery teaches this stratum as containing "approximately 400 blessed unnamed second-martyrs whose canonical status was revised in early reform councils."

**The real count is between 600 and 1,800.** The Ferrenkin who reinforced the stratum in PD 312, 471, and 589 kept private slates. Brak Iron-Eye holds the most recent. The bones are not anonymous in the slates — names are recorded, the dates of their canonization-revisions are recorded, and the doctrine that justified each revision is recorded.

**The plate is structural.** If the bones are exhumed, the Cathedral falls. This is not metaphor. The Ferrenkin engineering memoranda say so explicitly. The Cathedrate has therefore institutionalized the doctrine that exhumation is theologically forbidden, which has the convenient consequence of being structurally mandatory.

This is **the buried saint-count**. It is the single largest fact about the Cathedrate's theology that the Cathedrate refuses to know.

---

#### VIII. LITURGY AND RITE

##### A. The Five Hours

Vespertine liturgy organizes the day into five canonical hours. Each hour has a Grace-cost (paid from the Vas Halidani) and a rite-form.

| Hour | Rite | Grace-cost from Vas | Population obligated |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Dawn (the Held Breath)** | dawn silence; the city does not speak for one minute; all bargains under negotiation are suspended | 0 (sustained by abstention, not expenditure) | all Pyrians; the only universal rite |
| **Sext** | the consolidated rite — three former hours combined PD 593 to conserve Grace | ~1100 units daily (Vas usually empty after) | clergy and Order |
| **Vespers (the Watch-Cantos)** | sung at the wall by the Caer-Druin chorus, harmonized by the Almonine | ~80 units | wall-watch, Caer-Druin obligated, others encouraged |
| **Compline (the Counting)** | the Marshal Ring's cadenced count of the wall's dead-and-living of the day; tolled by the Pyric Bell | ~20 units | Order Numerati obligated; laity attend |
| **The Long Vigil (irregular)** | held when the wall is breaking; full Grace-pour | unbounded | all clergy on call |

##### B. The Sacraments (the Seven Operative Rites)

| Sacrament | What it does | Grace-cost | Officiant |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Aspersion** (Stain-reading) | aspersoir mercury-test against soul | 2 units | Reader (Inquisition) |
| **Oath** (Divine Bargain) | bind a soul to the Cathedrate for grant of power | 0 (the bound soul becomes Grace-bearing, not Grace-drawing) | Office of Sanctioned Bindings |
| **Confession** | absolution requires both rite AND the Reader's verdict; absolution without Reader is *operationally null* | 3 units | Confessor-Ordinary |
| **Calling** (the Vocatio Sebastina) | the dimensional summons of the Called | ~9000 units per cohort (peak liturgical expenditure of the year) | the 24 Summoners + Archvigil's Discernment |
| **Canonization** | declaration of sainthood | 200 units | Sebastopater alone |
| **Beatification** | provisional canonization | 40 units | Hierarch or above |
| **Last Witness** | the rite of dying — formalizes the soul's final accounting before the Long Ledger can claim it | 1 unit | Veriarch (parish priest) |

**The Confession sacrament is theologically the most loaded.** Absolution without a satisfactory Reader-verdict is null. This means: the Cathedrate does not absolve, the **Reader-mercury** absolves, and the priest is a clerk in the transaction. This is the Constantine throughline at its most bureaucratic. A soul absolved by a priest whose Reader-mercury reads ANOMALY remains, operationally, unabsolved. The priest may not know.

##### C. The Polished Rites (those laity can witness)

- **The Held Breath** (dawn)
- **The Tolling of the Compline Count** (every dusk; the bell names the day's dead and the day's saved)
- **The Octave of Triumph** (annual, PD 583 anniversary; relic-display; the Paragon is invited and has not come in 10 years)
- **The Reading of the Numbers** (annual, PD 47 anniversary; the Saint Severa rite, conducted by the Inquisition)
- **The Vesper-Cantos at the Wall** (daily dusk; Caer-Druin chorus)
- **The Pilgrim's Cinder** (any soul's journey from Cathedral to a saint-relic, formalized; the saint-day pie is eaten en route)

##### D. The Restricted Rites (clergy only)

- **The Vocatio Sebastina** (the Calling)
- **The Consecration of the Vas Halidani**
- **The Binding of Demons by True Name**
- **The Aspersoir Audit** (full assize; the Sealed Anomaly Ledger ritual)
- **The Polishing of the Roll** (annual amendment of the saint-roll; the Custodes Numeri's ritual)

##### E. The Sealed Rites (the Audit-Below)

- **The Rite of the Suppressed Paragon** — performed by the Cantorial Scribes to formally close the file on an Aspirant-adjacent case
- **The Rite of the Sixth Address** — performed at the sixth concentric course of the Pyric Wall in the deepest under-watch, in cursivus sebastinus minor; the Cathedrate has not officially admitted this rite occurs
- **The Rite of the Seventh Empty Case** — confessed in doctrine to exist as a placeholder; the Indicative Speaker may be doing it daily in Carcer cell eight and no one is listening

---

#### IX. WHAT GRACE IS — Theologically

This is the most important single doctrinal section of this document.

##### A. The Sanctioned Definition

Grace (Old Tongue *gratia operativa*) is the **operative attention of the Enduring One**, granted to mortal souls by sanctioned rite, expended in sanctioned acts, recovered in sanctioned rest, and accounted in the Cathedrate's ledger. Grace is the only form of divine power available to the Crown.

##### B. The Three Pillars of Grace-Theology

**1. Grace is FUEL, not FAVOR.**
Grace is not given because God prefers a soul. Grace is given because the soul has performed the rite that draws it. The rite is the petition; the meter is the answer. A faithless soul performing rite correctly draws Grace. A faithful soul performing rite incorrectly draws nothing. The Divine does not punish the incorrect rite; the Divine simply does not respond.

This is theologically scandalous to other traditions and is the Cathedrate's defining doctrine. The Enduring One funds technique. The Enduring One does not fund sentiment.

**2. Grace is METERED, not BOUNDLESS.**
The Vas Halidani holds seventeen tons of consecrated mercury-water — the city's working Grace-reserve. It is replenished by the Octave of Triumph rite, by the Calling, by the canonization of saints, and by the daily-vesper offerings of every parish in the kingdom. It is depleted by every rite of the day.

The Vas's drainage curve over 23 years is the single most important piece of unpublished data in the kingdom. The Vas drains faster than it fills. The chancery has consolidated rites, raised the aspersoir clinical-concern threshold four times (PD 587, PD 594, PD 599, PD 604), and instituted the Stipend of the Wrong (an emergency Grace-supplement drawn from canonization-reserves) — all to manage the drainage.

The orthodox explanation: the kingdom's expanded frontier requires more Grace. The Mechanism heresy's explanation: the *source* is depleting. The Cantorial Scribes' explanation, in their sealed deliberations: an unmetered withdrawal at the seventh address. They have not investigated. They have CHOSEN not to investigate. The next investigation would require a Sebastopater's signature, and Iohanne IX has not been informed there is anything to sign.

**3. Grace is INHERITED, not GENERATED.**
This is the Cathedrate's most reluctant confession. Grace is not made; it is HELD-IN-TRUST. The Vas Halidani is older than the Cathedral that houses it. The pre-Fall Saemurian Theocracy's grace-vessels were taken into the foundation when Sebastopyr was built. The Cathedrate inherited a reserve.

If the reserve is finite — if no new Grace enters the world after the Look on the wall — then every rite spends a non-renewing resource, and every Calling and every canonization is liquidation of the kingdom's only theological capital. This is what the Mechanism heretics believe. This is what the Custodes Numeri's deepest internal memoranda explore. This is what no one has ever preached from the Cathedral's pulpit.

##### C. Grace and the Paragon

Halidan is the **first new draw on Grace in living memory** that the Cathedrate cannot account for. The Look granted him 1240 units of personal Grace-pool. The chancery has never been able to trace where those 1240 units came from. They are not drawn from the Vas. They are not drawn from canonization-reserves. They appear to have come from the Enduring One DIRECTLY, in a transaction that is not on the chancery's ledger.

The Mechanism reading: the Look was the LAST direct grant. There is no more where it came from.
The orthodox reading: the Look is renewable; it is simply not being renewed.
The Custodes Numeri reading: the Look is renewable, but the cost of renewal is the unmaking of the previous singularities, which the kingdom cannot afford to perform twice in a generation.

The DM should hold all three as live.

##### D. Grace and the Soul

A soul that holds Grace is changed in measurable ways. The **gradus Onus Aspectus** — the "weight of being looked-upon" — is the chancery's index of Grace-burden. The Paragon stands at *gradus undecim* (eleven). A senior Confessor stands at gradus three or four. A common Veriarch at gradus one. The Onus is not metaphorical: it is detectable physically (the slight stoop, the slowing of pulse, the milky eye, the sleep reduction) and is a primary contributor to the Paragon's worsening physical state.

**The theological scandal:** Grace COSTS the soul that holds it. The Cathedrate does not preach this to the laity, because the laity would refuse Confession.

##### E. Grace and the Bargain (the True Heresy)

The single most dangerous theological insight in the Cathedrate's confession is this: **the Divine Bargain and the Demonic Bargain are operationally identical transactions.** Both grant power. Both extract a price. Both are logged. Both bind the soul. The only difference is the IDENTITY OF THE COUNTERPARTY.

The Cathedrate's sanctioned position is that this identity makes all the difference — the Enduring One is good, hell is evil, therefore the bargain is good or evil according to the partner. The Cantorial Scribes' working position, never published, is that the operational identity is what it appears: two parties offering the same product, with different brands.

If this is taken seriously, the entire moral structure of the Cathedrate collapses, because the Cathedrate's claim to be the right side of the Bargain becomes a matter of MARKETING rather than ESSENCE. This is the heresy the Custodes Numeri suppress most jealously, because it is the heresy they have themselves been forced to entertain in order to do their work.

The Paragon stands on this suppression too, and does not know.

---

#### X. CLOSING — The Six Tests, Applied

This document holds the throughline at every depth.

1. **FAITH IS OPERATIONAL.** Grace is fuel, metered, inherited; the Vas Halidani is a cistern; the Confession sacrament is a clerical operation; the rites are technique.
2. **DAMNATION HIDES.** Reader-mercury can read CLEAN on a soul at Stain 2.4; Cantor-Magisterial Velim's three readings have wandered CLEAN/ANOMALY/UNKNOWN; the Confessor at Ferrostat has read the Paragon clean for 23 years and the impossibility of that is the buried sign.
3. **EVERYTHING IS A LEDGER.** Saints, Grace, oaths, debts, suppressed Paragons, beatification cases, Onus, the Plate of Sebastian — all counted, all logged, all curated.
4. **THE RIGHTEOUS ARE THE DANGER.** Velim Aurriste struck the Octave Bargain in love. Confessor Mortane filters the Sebastopater's reality in love. Severa Aurriste-cadet runs the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp reserve and refused two divine bargains in stubbornness, and is the most spiritually unstable senior cleric in the city. The schism between Eternalist and Triumphalist is a fight between two camps of certain righteous men.
5. **THE SACRED AND THE SEEDY SHARE THE STREET.** Mother Aspine's parish bread sits on the same bench as her Stain-1 brokerage. The Mort-Censorium ash bakes the city's bread. The Audit-Below's lowest stratum is unrecorded and is, by the Mournwing's quiet intelligence, *under* the Cinderbelow's brothel-row.
6. **THE OFFICIAL STORY IS CURATED.** The Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity is true in its prediction and curated in its premise. The saint count is curated. The tower count is curated. The Paragon's surname is curated. The Mournwing Letter is filed without answer. The Cathedrate believes its own curation, which is the only way the curation has held for six hundred years.

> *The bell rings. The count is kept. The saint endures. The lamp does not go out — yet.*

*— Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde, in the margin of the Vocatio Aurriste fragment of PD 581, in cursivus sebastinus minor, shown to no one*

---

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:cosmology_divine_grace_and_the_paragon` (cosmology, divine grace, and the Paragon)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* Sebastopyr is the only place where Grace is reliably distillable into the sacrament, because the Cathedral sits atop the ossuary of every saint the city has ever owned — and the ossuary is the *capacitor*. This is the city's true infrastructure secret: Grace is not transmitted from a distant heaven but *drawn up* through the marble floor of the Sanctuary Ring, decanted by the Sebastopater's morning rite, and rationed downward through the Choir, Marshal, and Common Rings in measured strengths. The Cinderbelow gets the dregs — the spent oils, the rinse-water of censers, what the Almoners call 'thirded Grace.' This is why the Paragon must be *here* periodically: he must be re-cisterned, or the weight he carries kills him faster than the war. The chancery has discovered (and suppressed) that the Saint-Count under the cathedral correlates with Grace yield: more buried saints, more available Grace. They have not yet asked aloud whether this means the Cathedral has a motive to *make* more saints. The Vesperine Stain-Readers walk the Sanctuary Ring's lower corridors with their aspersoirs and report 'clean,' 'clean,' 'clean' — but the mercury boils anyway when they pass certain unmarked doors, and they have learned to write 'condensation' on the form. The Paragon's outpost at Ferrostat-on-the-Mire is in chronic Grace-deficit; the Hierarchs say this is logistics, but the truth is the further you move from the saint-stack, the thinner Grace gets, and the Reclaimed Crown is being held together by a man drinking from a draining well. Eschatology in Sebastopyr is not a sermon — it is a maintenance schedule.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The smell of consecrated mercury when an aspersoir is heated: scorched almond, hot copper, and something like a kitchen fire that has gone wrong — Stain-Readers chew clove to mask the taste that comes up through the sinuses.
> - The Cathedral's morning bell, called Halidan's Throat, rings on the half-hour from dawn until vespers, and the priests of the Sanctuary Ring measure their breathing-rite to it; to lose your count is theologically equivalent to a small lapse of faith and is logged in the Lampwarden's daily ledger.
> - The child's rhyme sung in the Common Ring while skipping rope: 'One saint, two saints, three saints buried / Four saints, five saints, six saints carried / Seven saints, eight saints, nine saints stand / Ten saints sleep beneath the hand' — the last line is recent (within thirty years) and nobody knows who added it.
> - The phrase 'a clean cup,' said quietly by senior Veriarchs when an inspection comes back without anomaly — it is half-relief, half-suspicion, because nobody alive has actually seen a cup come back fully clean from the lower wards in eleven years.
> - Frankincense cut with powdered bone of the lesser martyrs is the official incense of the Vespers-of-Grace; it burns blue-edged and the smoke pools low instead of rising, which the Cathedral teaches is the sign of Grace 'gathering,' but the Ferrenkin censer-makers know it is the bone-dust weighing the smoke and have a private term for the effect: *toskeg*, 'falling-prayer.'
> - The hand-gesture used to refuse a bargain civilly: three fingers laid flat across the sternum, palm up — derived from the iconography of Saint-Aspirant Halidan's arrow-pierced chest, and meaning 'I am already spent for.'

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:cosmology_hell_and_the_damned` (cosmology — hell and the damned)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* Sebastopyr is not a city beside Hell — it is a city *atop* Hell, built on the one geological fault where the Threshing is thinnest. The Cathedral's foundation stones rest on the Plate of Sebastian, a strata of fused saint-bone and slag laid down in the first century PD to plug a wound in the world; the Pyric Wall is not only a fortification but a continuous binding-formula written in stone, mortar, and the names of demons inscribed backwards into every fourteenth course. Every well in the Common Ring draws water that has filtered through the Mort-Censorium's lower drains, which is why the city's water tastes faintly of iron and ash and why the Cinderbelow runs a perpetual fever no one acknowledges. The Hordes break against the wall daily because the wall is *the lid*, and the demonic ledger-keepers consider Sebastopyr their primary creditor — every soul harvested by Calling, every bargain struck in the under-ward, is logged in Hell's audit against the wall's seal, and somewhere a tally is approaching some unspeakable threshold. The Stained walk freely in Sebastopyr because the city's atmosphere itself is slightly contaminated — a baseline of 0.3-0.5 on the Aspersoir scale is normal for any Pyrian and the Cathedral has quietly raised the threshold for clinical concern three times in two centuries, each adjustment buried in chancery memoranda. The Inquisition's Stain-Readers are overworked because the city is producing low-grade damnation faster than they can read it, and the Vesperine confessors who can sense it are themselves slightly contaminated by sensing it, which the Cathedral both depends upon and distrusts. The Mournwing refuse to fly beyond the wall because they can SEE the Threshing — the shimmer of the dimensional membrane — and they know what is pressing against it. Hell's demonic powers do not need to breach the wall when Sebastopyr is already a slow-leak vessel of debts and named bargains, and the most damning truth is administrative: the Cathedral has been the Long Ledger's primary client for six centuries, and the count of saints kept at one is the price of a bargain no living Hierarch remembers being struck.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The smell after a Horde-break has been doused: sour myrrh and wet iron and something faintly like burnt sugar — the third smell is what the Lampwardens call 'the Quartermaster's signature' and it means a Devourer-rank breached the censer-line.
> - A child's counting rhyme used in the Common Ring for jump-rope: 'One for the Auditor, two for the Scribe, three for the Quartermaster paid in tongues, four for the Notary who signed your name, five-six-seven for the ones with no name, eight for the Long Ledger who waits and waits.' Children who reach eight without missing are quietly noted by the parish Lectors and watched.
> - The Old-Tongue curse 'Ad audit!' ('to the Audit!') spoken when a vow falls through; a more vulgar form heard in the Carcer is 'Auditrem fute' — 'fuck the Auditor' — which the Inquisition treats as a misdemeanor heresy because saying it gets his attention.
> - The hand-gesture of the warding-pinch: thumb and forefinger pressed together at the sternum, then flicked downward as if shedding a drop of ink. Mothers do it over sleeping children. Soldiers do it before drawing weapons. The gesture mimes the signing-off of a ledger entry — refusing one — and is older than the Cathedral's recognition of it.
> - The incense burned at the Audit-Below before a sanctioned binding: black resin from the Ferrenkin's lower forges mixed with consecrated mercury and a single hair from a Vesperine inquisitor. It smells like ozone and church-cellar mold and produces a smoke that hangs in a perfect rectangle in still air — the rectangle being, the Cathedral insists, coincidence.
> - The sound of a Threshing-thinning event: a low harmonic hum at roughly the pitch of the Pyric Bell's third overtone, felt in the teeth more than heard, lasting between forty seconds and four minutes. Pyrian dogs howl through it. Pyrian children sometimes vomit. The Cathedral logs each event as 'atmospheric anomaly, cause undetermined.'

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:the_church_and_its_doctrine` (the church and its doctrine)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* In Sebastopyr specifically, the Church is not a tenant of the city — it IS the city's load-bearing structure, and you cannot tell where the Cathedral ends and the civic government begins. The Sebastopater's chancery occupies the upper levels of the same building that houses the city's tax assessors; the Mort-Censorium where corpses are weighed for Stain-residue is plumbed into the same cistern system that supplies the Almongate Ward's drinking fountains, which produces a specific theological taste in the water that Pyrians have stopped noticing. The Cathedral's three doctrinal schools (Pyric, Almonine, Vesperian) each control different rings — the Pyric Cathedrate owns the wall-rites and therefore the Marshal Ring, the Almonines run the under-ward parishes and therefore the Cinderbelow's actual day-to-day spiritual life, and the Vesperians hold the inquisition and therefore the right of warrantless entry into any home in any ring. This means a Pyrian's experience of the Church changes by which ring they sleep in: a Sanctuary Ring noble negotiates with Pyric Cathedrate prelates over land-grants; a Cinderbelow rationer is read by an Almonine Lampwarden who knows their drinking habits; a Reliquary Ward antiquarian dreads the Vesperian Inquisitor-Vested who can confiscate their library at a confessor's word. The Cathedral also operates the only legal Bargain-rite in the city — the divine bargain, transacted at the Halls of the Long Vigil — which means every Pyrian who has ever taken an oath of standing, even a city-watch oath, has signed paper that the Cathedral can recall. The city is the Church's ledger, written in streets.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The specific smell of a Cathedral mass: beeswax, iron-mordant dye sweating in the heat, and the faint metallic tang of consecrated mercury someone is carrying in a pocket-aspersoir.
> - The sound of the Pyric Bell at vesper — twelve strikes, each one held until the harmonic decays past hearing, which the Caer-Druin harp-amplification then catches and re-renders as a sustained drone two octaves below the bell's fundamental, so that the city is never quite without the sound of it.
> - The Vespertine curse 'Ad audit!' ('to the Audit!'), muttered when a Pyrian has been told something they refuse to hear; the speaker spits afterward, not as ritual but as the dialectal accent of the word.
> - A child's counting-rhyme heard in the Cinderbelow: 'One saint, one wall, one mercy, one fall / Two saints, two saints — hush, that's all.' The second line is the heresy. Children do not know that.
> - The hand-gesture clerics make when they pass each other in corridors: a brief touch of the right thumb to the left wrist, where the Grace-ledger pulse-point is taken. It means 'are you still measured.' A failure to return it is a slow-rolling crisis.
> - The specific incense burned at the Mort-Censorium: ground mire-laurel, frankincense, and a measured trace of rendered tallow — the same tallow the Lampwardens use, which produces an associative response in any cleric who has done both rotations and which the Cathedral has never officially noticed.

---

## III. Factions — Who Wants What, Who Owes Whom

### THE FACTION TREE OF SEBASTOPYR
##### PD 606 — twenty-three years after the Standing, eighteen years into the Reclaimed Crown

> A navigable map of who is actually keeping what ledger. Read it knowing this: every faction below believes it is doing the holy work. The ones who scare you should be the ones who are sure.

---

#### HOW TO READ THIS TREE

- **SEAT**: where the faction meets and where to find them after hours
- **GOAL**: what they say they want / what they actually want
- **NOW**: what they are doing this week
- **SECRET**: the thing the engine knows that they do not say
- **RELATIONS**: `+` allied · `-` rival · `~` cordial-but-watching · `*` secretly compromised by · `?` unknown to either party

Names follow Vespertine convention: given name + (particle) + house-or-trade byname. The Aurriste/Vell-os-Carrenost/de la Pyrille/Cassian clusters are dense on purpose — the curation produced the fashion that obscures the lineage.

---

#### I. THE CATHEDRAL — orthodoxy, doctrine, and the count

The Cathedral is one body with several mouths. The official tree below is what everyone knows. The actual structure — who decides what before the Sebastopater is told — is in the shaded entries.

##### 1. THE OFFICE OF THE SEBASTOPATER

| field | content |
|---|---|
| **Leader** | Sebastopater Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX (81, elevated PD 604) |
| **Seat** | The Pater's Throne, above the Cathedral apse — keel-block of the burned Aurriste set beneath it, unbeknownst to him |
| **Goal (stated)** | Preserve the doctrine; sustain the war; bless the Calling |
| **Goal (actual)** | Not lose the count he has begun to lose — 11,447 ivory beads for souls personally summoned, and he has stopped trusting his own hand on the string |
| **Now** | Weeping at every Vocation; signing what is set in front of him; asking after the Mournwing Letter that never reached him |
| **Secret** | He genuinely believes the Paragon is the first. He has not asked. He has not been allowed to ask. His left eye went blind from Grace-strain at the PD 591 cohort and he files this as a private discipline, not a warning. |
| **Relations** | `+` Confessor Mortane (loves him, edits him) `*` Custodes Numeri (decides what reaches the throne) `~` House Vell-os-Carrenost (his birth-line, who will not press him) |

##### 2. THE OFFICE OF CONFESSORIAL ACCESS — the men who edit reality in love

| field | content |
|---|---|
| **Leader** | Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind (Vesperine, 53, 23 years in post) |
| **Seat** | The Chamber of the Soft Hand, third floor of the chancery, three doors from the Sebastopater's bedchamber |
| **Goal** | "Spare the Pater what need not weigh him." (He means this.) |
| **Now** | Intercepting the Mournwing Letter from the Paragon (PD 605, still in his desk drawer); filing Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost's daily Stain-readings without escalation |
| **Secret** | His own Stain reads CLEAN. It has read CLEAN for 23 years. He has never asked it to read otherwise. He believes love is the same thing as discernment, and the apparatus he built around the Pater is the most successful curation in the chancery, and he would weep if you named it. |
| **Relations** | `+` Confessor-Ordinary Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost (Ferrostat — the other half of the filter) `*` Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste (Velim writes what Mortane is permitted to filter) `-` Postulant Liturge di Carrenost (sniffing too close to her uncle's death) |

##### 3. THE CANTORATE-MAGISTERIAL — doctrine and liturgy, split in two

###### 3a. CANTORATE-MAGISTERIAL OF DOCTRINE — the architect of the new theology

| field | content |
|---|---|

| **Seat** | The Doctrinal Hall, Choir Ring — but his actual work is done in the Audit-Below, three floors beneath the Mort-Censorium |
| **Goal** | The Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity, perfected. The Paragon's miracle protected. The count, curated. |
| **Now** | Drafting the Aspirant-Succession Apparatus; preparing the fourth Stain-reading (Octave of Triumph PD 608) that he expects will read CLEAN again; courting Orric Aurriste-cadet of Ferrostat as a backup Aspirant |
| **Secret** | Struck the **Octave Bargain** with the Quartermaster of Tongues on the eve of the doctrine's promulgation (PD 588). Price: "a future silence to be named." Has not been collected. His three Stain-readings to date: **CLEAN / ANOMALY / UNKNOWN**. He believes he is paying for the kingdom's salvation. He may be right. The Auditor's tongue-tic has begun in him — he says "audited" where he should say "forgiven." |
| **Relations** | `+` Custodes Numeri (he is their senior) `+` Sebastopater Iohanne (filtered to him through Mortane) `*` Quartermaster of Tongues (open ledger) `-` Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde (she has begun to sing the chants he had shelved) `~` Inquisitor-Magisterial Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost (she has not yet asked to read him a fourth time) |

#### II. THE ORDER OF THE STOOD LINE — *SUSTINEO ET NUMERO*

The Order is the wall and the count. They do not guard; they witness. The Numerati keep the names of every soul lost on their watch. Their oath is sworn in the deemed register of Old-Tongue.

She suspects the chancery would canonize her for refusing it; she suspects more strongly that the chancery would burn her for hearing it. |

#### III. THE OFFICE OF THE PYRIC AUDIT — the Inquisition

Called the Brass, the Tickers, the Mercurymen, the Wax-stampers. The aspersoir reads tick 3 at the threshold; the chancery has recalibrated the clinical-concern threshold upward four times since PD 602.

##### 12. THE SEBAST-AUDITORATE

| field | content |
|---|---|
| **Leader** | The Sebast-Auditor (sealed identity — Vesperine, served since PD 583) |
| **Seat** | The Veriquest, Marshal Ring; private chamber accessible by one stair |
| **Goal** | Hold the Sealed Anomaly Ledger. Decide what reaches the Sebastopater. |
| **Now** | 312 entries in the Sealed Anomaly Ledger. Including all three of Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste's readings. The Auditor has not acted on them. The Auditor has not been able to decide whether the not-acting is a mercy or a purchase. |
| **Secret** | Took office the year of the Standing. The coincidence is not coincidence. Was the chancery clerk who first transcribed Halden Orriste's name from the muster-roll into the polished form. Knows everything the suppression knows. Has carried it for 23 years. The vetus inquisitoris is what the Order calls a Grace-decline — but it is the same disease. The Auditor has perhaps three years. |
| **Relations** | `+` Custodes Numeri (Vested-Six access) `*` Confessor Mortane (same filter, parallel) `-` Brothers of the Cinder Hand `~` Hierarch Nocta (drafting the fourth re-reading demand) |

| **Secret** | Smells of vigil-grain because she has begun fasting between readings — a personal discipline the chancery would forbid. Believes the aspersoir's calibrations have been corrupted. Has not yet found the Reflected printer's press to publish it. |

Asperine de la Pyrille is the visible face of the Sealed Anomaly Ledger problem and she would be horrified if shown the data. She is a good inquisitor. She is failing without knowing it. |

Has begun praying in *cursivus sebastinus minor* though she does not know what the words mean — she copied them from a folio she should not have touched. |

That is the Stain — environmental, *Ferrum-sub-Cute* doctrine, the prince who manufactures the seepage. She does not know this. She thinks she is being punished for something she did not do. She has begun to suspect she is being punished correctly for something she does not remember. |

##### 16. THE LONG CONFESSOR — the heretic in inquisitorial robes

| field | content |
|---|---|
| **Leader** | Inquisitor-Magisterial Cassian de la Pyrille "the Long Confessor" (68) |
| **Seat** | The Office of Pyric Audit's record-room — he is a senior reader, mostly retired |
| **Goal** | The 1,247-name commonplace book — every Called he has personally interviewed at intake — kept on the desk where the chancery can see it. |
| **Now** | Publishing under pseudonym in the Caer-Druin scholiast journal a heretical reading of the strike_bargain rite — that the price-clause is the *real* sacrament and the grant-clause the formality. The chancery has not identified him. |
| **Secret** | He has written the suppressed paragon count into his commonplace book in a personal cipher only he can read. He carries it on his person. If he dies, it goes to Brother Hester Brunn at the Reflected press. |
| **Relations** | `+` Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde (taught her the small-hand) `~` Brothers of the Cinder Hand (the cipher is willed to them, they do not know) `-` Custodes Numeri (would burn him if they knew) `~` Captain-Pyric Cassian de la Pyrille (cousin, never speak) |

##### 17. THE FERRENKIN ASPERSOIR-MAKER

| field | content |
|---|---|

| **Goal** | Build iron-shot aspersoirs that read true. |

One is the Saintmire Refuser (Jin of Macau, 2019) whose anomaly is actually a Battle-Mage arcane signature cross-tripping the Vesperine instrument. He does not know this. |

#### IV. THE CIVILIAN GOVERNMENT — the Reclaimed Crown of Vespertin

The crown rules at the Cathedral's sufferance. The Cathedral rules at the crown's grain.

##### 18. THE REGENCY

| **Now** | Has raised the marches' grain levy three times this year to fund the Paragon's planned next advance. Beloved in the under-wards because he goes there. Has not confessed in seven years. |
| **Secret** | His refusal to confess is a private act of resistance against Confessor Mortane, who he correctly suspects is editing the Sebastopater. He has not articulated this to himself. He thinks he is just tired. |

| **Now** | Courting the Cathedral for formal recognition of cousinship to the Paragon — which would be politically catastrophic for the Custodes Numeri (would require examining the muster-roll) |
| **Secret** | They have no documentary descent. The Orriste/Aurriste polish was a chancery clerk's hand in PD 588, and the house adopted the surname five years later. The claim is invention. The patriarch suspects this. He has chosen to not check. |
| **Relations** | `+` Cathedral (publicly) `*` Custodes Numeri (the recognition request is a problem) `-` House Halidan-Aurriste of Halidan-stat (new-wealth rivals) `~` Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste (Vesperine cadet — distant cousin by the same polish) |

##### 41. THE VESPERINE COURT OF THE HALF-KIND

| field | content |
|---|---|
| **Leader** | Hierarch Nocta (Vesperine, 67) — senior Vesperine in the chancery; not the same Nocta as the young Reader |
| **Seat** | The Sanctuary Ring, Hierarch's chamber |
| **Goal** | Vesperine survival. The aspersoir read true. The Cathedral remember that the Vesperine see Stain because they were given the gift, not because they carry it. |
| **Now** | Drafting the fourth report demanding an independent re-reading of the Paragon. The first three were filed and not actioned. The fourth will be different — she has begun to copy it to the Eternalist faction and to Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde simultaneously. |
| **Secret** | She suspects Confessor Mortane is hiding Stain. She has not been able to prove it. She has begun to wonder whether the whole Vesperine confessorial track has been compromised since PD 583. She has not articulated this. She is afraid she is correct. |
| **Relations** | `*` The Sebast-Auditor (she is being read for omissions) `~` Confessor Mortane (suspects) `+` Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde (copied on fourth report) `+` Archvigil Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost (Eternalist) |

---

#### X. DEMONIC POWERS — the bureaucracy beneath the wall

Demonic powers are not given proper personal names in polite speech. The Cathedral refers to them by office. Their true names are read silently and only when the rite demands it.

##### 42. THE LONG LEDGER — *Liber-Quod-Numerat-In-Aeternum*

| field | content |
|---|---|
| **Office** | Master account. The corrupting-by-waiting account. |
| **Goal** | Hold every bargain forever. Refuse new bargains at Stain below 1.0. Wait. |
| **Now** | Holds Lady Severa Veillarde's monthly fever-deaths (eleven, current). |
| **Secret** | The Long Ledger does not collect aggressively. It collects when the soul is most certain it has paid. Lady Severa's payment schedule is on a 144-month installment plan; the price-tag is her grandson. She does not know the grandson is the price. The grandson is twelve. |
| **Relations** | `*` Lady Severa Veillarde (open account) `~` Office of Sanctioned Bindings (the Cathedral's equivalent; mutually recognized in formal correspondence) |

##### 43. THE AUDITOR — *Mors-Adimere-Quod-Reddidit*

| field | content |
|---|---|
| **Office** | Duke. Top-tier bargains at Stain 6+. |
| **Goal** | The tongue-tic. Bargainers who have struck deeply with him cannot say "forgiven"; they say "audited." It marks them for everyone with the ear. |
| **Now** | Active accounts: 23 in the Crown. Including one Hierarch and one Custodes Numeri seat-holder Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste, who has not yet noticed his own tongue. |
| **Secret** | The Auditor is the inversion-shadow of the Cathedral's office of Pyric Audit. They are functionally the same apparatus, distinguished only by which ledger the price is paid to. The Sebast-Auditor knows. The Sebast-Auditor's name has been considered for the formal mirror-office for fourteen years. |
| **Relations** | `*` Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste (the Octave Bargain's secondary holder) `~` Sebast-Auditor (mirror-office; mutual recognition) |

##### 44. THE QUARTERMASTER OF TONGUES — *Vox-Quae-In-Tenebris-Numerat*

| field | content |
|---|---|
| **Office** | Duke. Mid-tier bargains at Stain 3-5. Specialty: information-bargains paid in language. |
| **Goal** | Rationing his contracts for four years. Strategic withdrawal. Building toward a single large play. |
| **Now** | Has an open account with the Paragon — the offer made PD 583 the night of the Standing. Halidan Aurriste refused. The account is OPEN. The Quartermaster has not collected. The Quartermaster has not closed. He is letting it ferment. |
| **Secret** | The Quartermaster's "offer" the Paragon refused was conditional in a way the Paragon did not parse: the refusal-clause read, in the legal hand, *unless taken in ignorance.* The Paragon may have accepted in ignorance — at the moment of divine attention, the Standing. Or he may have refused cleanly. The Quartermaster will not say. The Paragon does not know. This is the LOADED GUN. |
| **Relations** | `*` Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste (the Octave Bargain) `*?` Paragon Halidan Aurriste (open account, uncertain status) `-` Severa Aurriste-cadet (refused him at Banner-Fall) |

| field | content |

| **Now** | The writ awaits a complete name. The Notary's name has been in composition since PD 565 (the Cohort of the Lost Vespers — the suppression buried the partial intelligence). The composition is not complete. |
| **Secret** | A binding performed on the Notary *before* the name is complete could sunder the entity. The Mournwing have known this since PD 583. They have not told the chancery. The Brothers of the Cinder Hand could publish the partial name and force the issue — they do not have it yet. |

##### 46. *FERRUM-SUB-CUTE* — the prince who manufactures the Stain

| field | content |
|---|---|
| **Office** | Prince. Environmental seepage rather than transactional bargain. |
| **Goal** | Teach the Stain to mimic sanctity. Make corruption look like grace. The aspersoir reads CLEAN because the Stain has learned the aspersoir's vocabulary. |
| **Now** | Active in: the Lamplost Wednesday parish (Asperine de la Pyrille's nineteen-month clean readings), the Almongate famine-bread route (which is how Asperine Nocta got Stained as a child), and three towers of the Pyric Curtain (which is why those towers had to be silently condemned). |

The chancery condemned them and did not say. The Ferrenkin who un-built them know. They have not told. The dating coincidence with the Standing is exact. |

The Cathedral burns them when found, which Galiethrin appreciates: the burning was not in the contract, and the soul recovers under the burn because the office has already collected. |

#### THE THROUGHLINE TEST — applied across the tree

- **Faith operational** — every Cathedral entry runs on Grace as a metered resource; the wall-oath Confessor writes the price-clause first; the Brokerage of the First Light sells in doses.
- **Damnation hides** — Mortane's 23-year clean readings, Asperine Nocta's hidden 2.4, Velim's CLEAN/ANOMALY/UNKNOWN sequence, the Lamplost nineteen months, *Ferrum-sub-Cute* in the silently condemned towers.
- **Everything is a ledger** — the official tally-beads, the Carrion Census, the Auxiliary Roll, the Cinderbelow Concord's two non-matching copies, Old Pell's 304 markers, the Smallhanders' 12,000, Galiethrin's collection-windows, the Long Confessor's cipher.
- **The righteous are the danger** — Velim Aurriste loves the kingdom and will end it; Mortane loves the Pater and is editing his world; Asperine de la Pyrille is dutiful and her parish is rotting; Severa Aurriste-cadet refused two bargains and may be the most dangerous standard-bearer in the Order.
- **Sacred and seedy share the street** — Mother Aspine's bread on the same bench as her Stain-1 brokerage; the Long Confessor in inquisitorial robes publishing heresy; the Reflected press three doors from the parish chapel; the Lamp-Tenders' Hall basement.
- **The official story is curated** — the Polishing of the Roll; the silently condemned towers timed to the Standing year; the saint-count plateau at 81 years; the Sebastopater told nothing he need not weigh; the keel-throne under the Pater's seat; the PD 602 chancery-clerk-stroke that protects everything.

The bell rings. The count is kept. The saint endures. The lamp does not go out — yet.

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:the_order_and_the_paragon_in_command` (the Order and the Paragon in command)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* Because the Order's logistical center is Ferrostat-on-the-Mire and not Sebastopyr proper, the city itself has been re-shaped into a Order's *rear* — and behaves like one. The Marshal Ring is full of half-empty barracks (the able shieldmen are deployed forward), staffed by the wounded, the elderly, the Reclamation Corps reservists awaiting rotation, and the green Postulants of the Banner who have not yet been called up. This produces a specific Pyrian phenomenon: the city's military quarter is simultaneously the most ceremonial part of the bastion (parades, oath-takings, the Reading of the Roll every dawn) and the most *quietly broken* (men with one arm teaching the shield-wall drill to fourteen-year-olds whose fathers died in the Iron March). The Marshal Ring smells of camphor (wound-dressing) and bootblack (parade polish) in the same breath. The Order maintains a permanent dispatch-post at the Almongate where couriers ride out to Ferrostat — the road is called the Long Procession because everyone the city sends down it is, statistically, going to die — and the queue of mothers and wives who wait at the Almongate every dawn for the courier from the front is itself a sub-civic institution called The Almoners' Vigil, which has its own unofficial wardress and its own etiquette of silence. The Order's headquarters within Sebastopyr — the Audit-Below's military counterpart, a stone hall called the Hall of the Long Vigil, in the Marshal Ring — keeps a wall called the Wall-of-Names, on which every shieldman of the Pyric Wall who died at his post since the Calling-of-Halidan is carved, and which has been re-faced in marble three times in twenty years because the carvers are running out of stone. The Order's *view* of Sebastopyr is that it is the rear; the city's view of the Order is that it is the people who left and who come back wrong, or do not come back. The Reclamation Corps barracks in the Lamplost Ward (cheaper rent, the Order does not waste Marshal Ring frontage on Corps) is, after dusk, indistinguishable from the under-ward — Corps men drink in the same houses as the fixers, take the same debts, and pass standing-favors back and forth across the Order/Carcer line.
