This is the holy-noir specific to Sebastopyr's military arm: the shield-wall doctrine is preserved with monastic rigor in the Marshal Ring's drill-yards while in the Lamplost the Corps is borrowing money from the same broker who sells forbidden things three doors down.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The sound the Order makes on parade is not a march-cadence — it is the Counting, a slow numerical recitation in Old-Tongue ('unum, duo, tres, quatuor...') called out by the file-leader as the column moves, marking each step against the count of the dead. A column on the move sounds like an abacus walking.
> - The smell inside the Hall of the Long Vigil is camphor and old bootblack and the specific iron-tang of a Ferrenkin censer that burns a resin called *aurigan* — used to clean the air of any lingering Stain-trace a returning shieldman might carry. Every wall-veteran who enters the Hall is censed at the door whether they ask for it or not. The censer-smoke leaves a faint orange residue on the lintel and on the shoulders of the censed; veterans wear it as a mark of having come back at all.
> - The Order's parting blessing, said by file-leaders to their files at the gate before a sortie, is not a prayer — it is the phrase 'Sustineo, et numero te' ('I endure, and I count you'). The men reply 'Numerati' ('counted'). It is older than the doctrine and older than the Cathedral's hold on military rite; the chancery has never been able to suppress it and has stopped trying.
> - Children in the Marshal Ring play a clapping-rhyme called Halidan's Hand that goes: 'One arrow, two arrow, three in the shield / Four arrow, five arrow, six in the field / Seven in the soldier, eight in the saint / Nine in the wall and the wall does not faint.' The rhyme stops at nine deliberately — the tenth arrow is the one that killed him in the second martyrdom, and the children are taught (without being told why) not to say it aloud.
> - The Reclamation Corps wears a deliberately ugly grey wool over its scale, dyed with bog-iron from the Mire March, that fades to a sick yellow-green after eight months in the field. Veterans call this color 'Corps-rot' and refuse to wash it; a Corps man whose coat is still grey is a man who has not been out long enough to be trusted.
> - The Order's curse for a battle going wrong is 'Ad numerum!' — 'to the count!' — meaning the dead are about to be tallied and you will be on the list. A file-leader who shouts 'Ad numerum!' is reporting to his men that the action has failed and the only honor left is to die well enough to be counted accurately.

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:the_inquisition_and_the_unreadable` (the Inquisition and the unreadable)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* Inside Sebastopyr, the Inquisition occupies the Reliquary Ward's southern arc — the Audit-Below, a basilica-and-warren complex where the Stain-readings are taken. A citizen entering the Choir Ring at certain hours will pass under a Listening Arch (a Ferrenkin-cast lintel that hums when a Stain over 4 walks beneath it) and not know they were read. Every Pyrian household above the Common Ring keeps a Vestibule Chit — a small wax tablet stamped by their parish Veriarch quarterly to confirm a clean reading; the chit is required to enter the Sanctuary Ring, to take communion at high mass, and to hold any chancery post. Loss or forgery of the chit is a Carcer matter. The Inquisition also runs the city's only legal mercury (consecrated, for aspersoirs) and the only legal supply of Caer-Druin tear-resin, which means the holy economy and the underworld economy meet at the Inquisition's loading dock in Lamplost Ward — fixers buy expired tear-resin from venal Lectors because it still works to mask a Stain at parish-grade readings, and the Inquisition has known about this leak for eleven years and not closed it because closing it would mean admitting the leak exists. The Mournwing couriers refuse Inquisition contracts after the Drumeth Affair of 597 PD (a Reader hired three Mournwing to fly an asset to Ferrostat; only the asset's coat returned), so all inter-Hold inquisitorial traffic goes by Long Procession road, which is slower and gives suspects time to either flee or arrange their cleansing. Most particular: in Sebastopyr the Reader and the suspect both bring witnesses, both are entitled to a Cantor's silent minute before the reading begins, and the Reader pays a small ritual fee from their own purse for every false-positive — which means the entire Inquisitorial salary structure is bent around the unsayable assumption that they get things wrong often enough for the fee-out to matter. The Stipend of the Wrong, they call it. No one will say what they call it in the under-wards.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The smell of an Inquisitorial chamber after a long reading: hot brass, consecrated mercury (which smells faintly of broken eggs and old altar wine), the cold-iron tang of a censed Ferrenkin weight, and under all of it the specific dry-paper scent of a freshly-stamped Vestibule Chit cooling on its rack.
> - The sound a brass aspersoir of consecrated mercury makes when it goes off: not a boil but a small, patient ticking — like a clock running too fast, then too slow, then too fast — that the trained ear learns to count against the Reader's own heartbeat. Untrained witnesses describe it as 'a watch going wrong inside a cup.'
> - The phrase Readers use, formally, to close an ambiguous session: 'The reading is held in vigil' — meaning: not clean, not condemned, the file stays open, the suspect walks out under a wax-tag they must show at every Listening Arch for ninety days. Vespertine slang shortens this to 'tagged for ninety,' and a tagged person is treated, socially, as if they had a contagious cough.
> - Children in the Common Ring play a clapping-rhyme called 'Halidan Knew,' the final couplet of which goes: *Reader Reader at the door / count to six and not to four / count to six and turn away / Reader Reader, what'd I pay?* No adult is sure where it came from and the Inquisition has formally declined to suppress it three times.
> - The hand-gesture an Inquisitor-Vested gives to dismiss a parish Lector after a joint reading: right hand, thumb folded under, three fingers tapped against the sternum in the rhythm short-short-long — the cadence of *sus-ti-NE-o*. It means 'go,' it means 'you did adequately,' and in the wrong context (made with the index finger extended instead of folded) it is a private signal that the reading was rigged.
> - Reader's incense: not the cathedral's frankincense-and-tallow blend, but a darker compound called *vigil-grain*, made from Caer-Druin hill-resin, ground iron filings, and a trace of distilled tear-resin. It burns black and sticks to the throat for an hour. Veteran Readers can smell it on each other across a crowded room and use this to find one another at parties without speaking.

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:the_kingdom_and_secular_power` (the kingdom and secular power)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* In Sebastopyr specifically, secular power lives in the LIMINAL RINGS — the Marshal Ring and the upper Common Ring — physically wedged between the Cathedral's Sanctuary Ring above and the Under-Wards below. The Crown's seat, the Audit-House of Vespertin, was deliberately built three streets DOWNHILL from the Cathedral's south gate so that any procession of the Sebastopater would always be seen descending TO the Crown, never ascending. The kingdom's currency, the Pyric mark, is struck with the Paragon's silhouette on the obverse and the Cathedral's bell-tower on the reverse — meaning every transaction in the city is a small daily reminder that civil money is backed by holy victory. The noble houses' townhomes cluster along the Aurriste Road in the Marshal Ring, but every house keeps a SECOND residence in a deconsecrated chapel-shell within the Choir Ring, paying the Cathedral a 'votive lease' that is, in plain language, a tax on proximity to grace. The Cinderbelow district, where the Crown has no writ at all, is where the new-wealth Reclamation Concession operates the bonded warehouses that hold confiscated Horde-territory salvage — gold cooled out of slag-pits beyond the wall, which the Crown claims by reclamation-right and the Cathedral claims by sanctification-right, and which in practice is split 60/40 by an unsigned arrangement called the Cinderbelow Concord. Most particularly: in Sebastopyr, the secular Crown DOES NOT HAVE ITS OWN BAILIFFS. Civic enforcement is leased from the Order's lay arm. The kingdom's law has no hands but the Church's, and every arrest is therefore a small humiliation the Crown has decided to call cooperation.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The smell of the Audit-House antechambers: cold beeswax, ink-iron, and the faint vinegar tang of the rag-soaked sponges the chancery uses to lift signatures from rejected drafts before re-pressing the parchment.
> - A merchant's curse muttered when a Cathedral inspector raises the tithe-rate mid-quarter: 'Per Sebast, they audit even the audit.'
> - The bell at the Audit-House does not match the Cathedral's tone — it is a half-step flat, deliberately, so the civilian hours can be told apart from the liturgical. Old Pyrians can tell which clock is striking with their eyes closed; tourists from the Holds cannot, and miss appointments by it.
> - The children's rhyme heard in the Marshal Ring courtyards: 'House of arrows, house of stone, / house of coin you call your own, / house of nothing keeps the wall, / house of nothing pays for all.' (Pyrian parents do not always know that 'house of nothing' is the working-class slur for House Halidan-Aurriste, the upjumped cadet branch.)
> - The mid-summer Concord Procession: a single bondsman from the Reclamation Concession walks from the Cinderbelow to the Cathedral's south gate carrying a sealed iron box, in absolute silence, while the bells of both the Cathedral and the Audit-House are deliberately stilled. The silence lasts exactly the length it takes a tallow-candle of a fixed weight to burn down. The box's contents are never publicly disclosed.
> - A specific incense, *fumum civile* — burned in Crown chambers only, never in chapels — a blend of resin, dried bog-orange, and a trace of brimstone-shard from beyond the wall. It is meant to mark a room as secular ground. The trace of brimstone is a fashion that started among House Veillarde and the chancery now considers unwise but cannot rescind without admitting it was ever a fashion.

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:the_bargain_economy_and_its_brokers` (the bargain economy and its brokers)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* In Sebastopyr specifically, bargains are not back-alley sin — they are a regulated industry with public hours. The Cathedral's Office of Sanctioned Bindings sits three doors from the Carcer in Quietus Ward, and on the same street as the Lampgate Discounts Bench where the under-ward's most respectable demon-broker keeps office hours stamped beside a parish almoner's. The Pyric Wall economy has produced a strange specialty: brokers who only deal at the wall itself, where Grace-prices are inflated by tactical urgency and where the chancery's audit-clerks turn deliberately slow. The under-ward Cinderbelow has a real ledger building — the Audit-Below — staffed by mortal clerks who keep mortal-debt books because the demonic Long Ledger refuses to register debts under three Stain, and someone must track the small graft that runs the city's daily work. Sebastopyr is also the only place in the Reclaimed Crown where the divine-bargain (oath) and the demonic-bargain (Stain) are written in the same Old-Tongue formula by tradition — the Cathedral copied the binding-clause from a confiscated heretic-broker's ledger in 712 PD because it was theologically superior, and the chancery has been quietly pretending otherwise for three centuries. The pricing conventions visible inside Sebastopyr right now (Vespertin's twentieth year of victory): a Stain-1 demonic bargain costs roughly one favor-from-a-priest's worth of leverage; a Stain-3 bargain has been inflated by frontier desperation and now goes for what used to buy Stain-5 (the Quartermaster of Tongues is rationing); an Order-binding oath has six standard durations from "one bell" (a single tactical hour) to "until the canonization that will not come"; and a mortal favor in the Cinderbelow this week is worth three rationed Grace-doses or a forged transit-letter through Almongate, whichever the broker fancies. The single most Sebastopyr-particular fact: the city's three ledgers (Grace, Stain, Debt) are believed by the chancery to be sealed from each other, and are not — the Vesperine half-kin clerks who staff all three departments are the same families, the brokers know it, and what walks between the ledgers is the city's actual economic life.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The under-ward smell of cold incense and brass shavings — the residue of unmaking a binding — which clings to anyone who has just walked out of a broker's parlor and lasts for two days no matter what you wash with.
> - The hand-gesture for 'I will not contract with you' is a closed fist held at sternum height with the thumb tucked inside the fingers — a knuckled refusal, said to mean 'my name stays in my mouth.' Refusing a broker without it is considered a tacit yes.
> - The Cinderbelow expression 'paying in Mondays' — taking on a mortal debt that comes due every week forever in small increments, the worst kind because it never matures and never closes. A man can be paying in Mondays his whole life and the broker still hold the original favor.
> - The sound a strike_bargain copper-needle makes when it pierces the contract-vellum: a small, definite *tik* — a sound clerks call 'the swallow,' because the ledger has swallowed the deal. No bargain is real until the swallow.
> - A child's rhyme from Almongate Ward: *Three knocks for grace, two knocks for debt / One knock means the Auditor's met / Don't open, mama, don't open the door / She paid in Mondays, she'll pay some more.*
> - The curse word 'sub-numerat' — literally 'it is being counted-under' in Old-Tongue, used when something small and bad has happened that the speaker knows will be tallied against them somewhere they cannot see. ('I dropped the censer, sub-numerat.')

---

## IV. City Districts — Sebastopyr Ward by Ward

#### SEBASTOPYR — DISTRICTS AND KEY LOCATIONS

##### A Walking Tour of the Bastion-City, PD 606

> *"You do not walk Sebastopyr. You descend through it. Each Ring lower is one degree colder, one shade dimmer, one debt deeper. The Cathedral sits at the apex; hell breathes through the Cinderbelow grates at the base. Between them, a city of ledgers."*
> — Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde, marginalia, unpublished

---

#### I. THE RINGS — How Sebastopyr Is Structured

Sebastopyr is mapped by **RING** (concentric, descending in elevation and standing) and **WARD** (radial, named for old gates or functions). The Pyric Wall is the outermost course — seven concentric battlements descending from the Cathedral apse outward. A native Pyrian gives directions by Ring + Ward + landmark: *"Choir Ring, Reliquary Ward, behind the Brass Pelican."* Outsiders get lost in the first hour. By tradition, you do not ascend a Ring without sanction; you may descend any Ring you have business in, and the Cinderbelow is open to all who have a reason and a reason that will hold.

The six Rings, top to bottom:

| Ring | Elevation | Character | Who Lives Here |
|------|-----------|-----------|----------------|
| Sanctuary Ring | apex | Cathedral, Aspirant's Lodgings, the Plate of Sebastian beneath | Sebastopater, Cantor-Magisterials, the Vested Six, two Caer-Druin reliquary-singers, the Paragon (when he comes, which is no longer) |
| Choir Ring | upper terraces | Chancery, Vocation House, archive offices | Postulants, Lectors, the cursivus-fluent, the chancery clerks, Confessor Mortane |
| Marshal Ring | upper-mid | Order garrisons, Inquisition's Veriquest, Hall of the Long Vigil | The Order, the Brass (Inquisition), Vexillarius Severa Aurriste-cadet, the bonded confessors |
| Common Ring | mid | Great Market, Reliquary Ward, Mort-Censorium, theaters | Pyrian merchants, guild-masters, the working faithful, House Marent's beeswax sheds |
| Under-Ward Ring | lower | Lamplost, Quietus, the Carcer | Lampwardens, censer-tenders, the funeral trades, prisoners, almoners, Mother Aspine |
| Cinderbelow | lowest, hell-adjacent | Brokerage of the First Light, Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp, Audit-Below registry | Ferrenkin forges, the Smallhanders, brokers, the Conscripted League at new moons |

Beneath the Cinderbelow: **the Audit-Below archive proper** (nine descending strata under the Cathedral, accessed only through the Mort-Censorium's lower passage via the Cantor's Stair). Beneath the Audit-Below: the Plate of Sebastian. Beneath the Plate: silence, and hell.

---

#### II. THE DISTRICTS

##### 1. THE SANCTUARY RING — *Where the Bell Lives*

**Character:** Hushed, vertical, smelling of vigil-grain incense and old stone-dust. The light comes through stained glass aged to honey. Bells govern the day; the Pyric Bell tolls for every soul's last Grace-spending and the Sanctuary hears every toll undampened.

**Who lives here:** Sebastopater Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX (81, eighteenth year of tenure, blind in left eye, weeps at every Calling); the two senior Cantor-Magisterials (Velim Aurriste 45, Asperine os Veillarde 62) in adjacent chancery-cells; two Caer-Druin reliquary-singers permitted to keep their harps within the Cathedral aisle; the Vested Six (the senior Inquisitorial council with read-access to the Sealed Anomaly Ledger); the **Aspirant's Lodgings** — the Paragon's residence, kept by three Lay-Sisters of Vigil who light a lamp at dusk and snuff it at dawn for a man who has not slept in those rooms in ten years.

**Key buildings:**
- **The Cathedral of the Enduring One** — six-century structure, seven naves, the Sebastopater's keel-throne (carved from the bow-block of the burned ship *Aurriste* sunk in port PD 41 — the connection no one has reconstructed since the PD 602 chancery-clerk's stroke)
- **The Aspirant's Lodgings** — a four-room suite, the bed dressed weekly, ceremonial regalia hanging on a black silk hanger
- **The Cantor's Stair** — the only sanctioned descent to the Audit-Below; gate of riveted iron, manned in three-shifts by Sworn Lectors who have taken the Oath of Numeration and the Oath of Silence-Beneath

**Atmosphere:** The Sanctuary smells of cold candle, old wood, vigil-grain. The flagstones are worn into prayer-shaped depressions before the high altar. There is a place on the lower transept where the Mournwing couriers land at dusk and unwrap their wings; their bone-thin shadows on the wall during deposition are a thing to see.

**Who the cohort meets:** Sebastopater Iohanne if granted audience (rare, three-day fast required, the audience itself eleven minutes by chancery tradition); Cantor-Magisterial Asperine in the lower transept after vespers, often alone, often humming fragments of music she should not know; the Sebastopater's Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind (Vesperine, 53, master of access, the man whose silence has filtered the Sebastopater's reality for 23 years); the Lay-Sisters of Vigil if they ask after the Paragon (they will not).

---

##### 2. THE CHOIR RING — *Where the Records Are Kept (and Edited)*

**Character:** Administrative dread. Carpeted corridors, oil lamps trimmed twice daily by chancery boys, the sound of beeswax styli scratching cursivus sebastinus minor on slate. Postulants run between rooms with sealed wax-stamp dockets; nothing is spoken above a chant-low murmur. The light is the cold light of north windows.

**Who lives here:** Chancery clerks (147 on the active roll, 23 in the closed-list), Postulants and Lectors (the lower clerical ranks), the **Office of the Pyric Audit**'s administrative wing, the **Curiate Vincula** (Office of Sanctioned Bindings), the **Office of the Cantorial Scribes** (formal name; self-name Custodes Numeri), Postulant Liturge di Carrenost (22, fluent in cursivus sebastinus minor, asking the wrong questions about her uncle's death).

**Key buildings:**
- **Vocation House** — where the Calling rite is performed by the 24 summoners under the Vocatio Sebastina, Archvigil Severa di Mauritz makes the nine-second Discernment that routes the new Called by prototype, and the translation-shock dead are removed by an iron-wheeled cart down a back stair to Bera Quist's tally-room
- **The Mirror Audit** — the chancery's own internal audit office that has known the Cinderbelow Concord's two non-matching copies for fourteen years and not reported
- **The Hall of the Cursivus** — the script-room where cursivus sebastinus minor is forged on warmed beeswax tablets, then transcribed to slate; access by appointment, oath required at the threshold
- **The Walker-Beyond-the-Wall Succession Apparatus** — a working office, not yet activated, run by three clerks who do not know what they are preparing

**Atmosphere:** The Choir Ring smells of beeswax (House Marent's monopoly), of oil-trimmed lamps, of paper-dust and the very faint mercury-smell from the Veriquest aspersoirs being calibrated downstairs. The clerks pad in felt slippers; a hard heel-strike in the Choir Ring would mark you as foreign.

**Who the cohort meets:** Postulant Liturge di Carrenost in the Hall of the Cursivus, mistaking the cohort for distant cousins of someone she should know; Confessor Mortane gliding past with a leather portfolio (he keeps three; the cohort will not know which one matters); a chancery clerk willing to lose a document for a Stain-1 favor if approached after seventh bell; Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste only by sanctioned appointment, only at the Veriquest threshold, never in his Audit-Below office.

---

##### 3. THE MARSHAL RING — *Where the Order Counts the Dead*

**Character:** Garrisoned, swept, ordered. The cobbles ring with iron-shod boots — Order Numerati pacing the Counting cadence (one-two-three-rest-name, marking every step with a name from the morning's casualty roll). Banners hang along Marshal Boulevard, each one a Pyric File's standard, each one with an embroidered tally of its honored dead. The Hall of the Long Vigil's brass-rimmed clock is audible from three streets in any direction; the Marshal Ring tells time by the Hall.

**Who lives here:** Order officers, Inquisitor-Vested ranks, Marshal-Vested Severa Aurriste-cadet (41, Vexillarius, the Paragon's voice here), the **Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp** off-hour pour, the bonded confessors of the Order, retired File-Leaders who have taken the Stipend of the Wrong (pension for those whose files broke during the Reclamation and were not officially listed as broken).

**Key buildings:**
- **The Hall of the Long Vigil** — Order's principal chancery, the Vexillarius's standard chained to its keel in the lower hall, the Wall-of-Names re-faced four times (the canon-historical fact the Order does not discuss)
- **The Veriquest** — the Office of the Pyric Audit's operational wing; aspersoirs calibrated here, readings filed here, the Sealed Anomaly Ledger kept in the Sebast-Auditor's vault (sealed identity, served since PD 583)
- **The Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp** — Order pub, third bell to dawn, hosts the Brokerage of the First Light's off-hours; Vexillarius Severa runs the Grace-reserve from a back table
- **The Garrison of the Tenth File** — north Pyric Wall barracks; File-Leader Nera Slag-Hand the Younger keeps her bunk-slate hidden behind a loose stone

**Atmosphere:** Iron, sweat, vigil-grain, the metallic tang of bell-grease. The Marshal Ring smells of clean steel kept oiled and of bodies kept disciplined. After tenth bell the pubs open and the smell shifts to spiced beer and resin-smoke; after midnight, to the slow exhausted sweetness of men and women who have spent their Grace and have nothing left.

**Who the cohort meets:** Vexillarius Severa Aurriste-cadet in the Hall (cool, courteous, refused two divine bargains, will offer the cohort a clean read of their standing if they ask correctly); File-Leader Nera Slag-Hand the Younger on the Drinkings' back step at any off-hour (she will not speak of her mother); Inquisitor-Magisterial Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost (51, the Office's best Reader) in the Veriquest if a reading is required — soft-spoken, smells of vigil-grain, may read the cohort's Stain if she has cause, will not report a minor anomaly without consultation.

---

##### 4. THE COMMON RING — *Where the City Lives*

**Character:** Where Pyrians actually live. Open-fronted shops, the Great Market on Sextidie and Octidie, balconies with linen drying between them, children playing the Arrow-Counter's Rhyme (truncated; no one knows the full version is canonically truncated). The Common Ring is the only Ring where laughter is the dominant sound.

**Who lives here:** Pyrian shopkeepers, guild members, the working faithful, the Reliquary Ward's relic-mongers, theater companies who play the Long Vigil Plays each Octave (seventeen plays; there is an eighteenth, suppressed; everyone above the Choir Ring knows; no one performs it). The Mort-Censorium occupies the north quadrant; its ash bakes the city's bread, which everyone knows and almost no one says.

**Key buildings:**
- **The Reliquary Ward** — three streets of relic-mongers, finger-bones in glass, splinters of saint-cot, brothels three doors down on Saintwomb Lane (the sacred and the seedy in literal proximity)
- **The Mort-Censorium** — the city's funeral-furnace and registry; case-closure records here cross-reference (or fail to cross-reference) Audit-Below paragon-deaths; the lower passage opens onto the Cantor's Stair via a door no one above the rank of Veriarch has ever seen used
- **The Brass Pelican** — Pyrian Mercantile Guild headquarters; Liturge Marent-Veillarde the guild-master holds personal markers from 35+ officials
- **House Marent's Beeswax Sheds** — beeswax monopoly, the city's lamp-oil, candles, sealing-wax; matriarch Severa Marent has been having private audiences with the Cantor-Magisterial about beeswax-consumption spikes that correlate with no recorded saint
- **The Theater of the Long Vigil** — where the seventeen Plays are performed during the Octave of Triumph

**Atmosphere:** The Common Ring smells of bread (Mort-Censorium ash in the flour), of beeswax (House Marent's sheds), of incense from the Reliquary Ward, of cheap perfume from Saintwomb Lane, of horse-shit and lamp-oil and rain on cobbles. The rain in Sebastopyr is constant; the cobbles are always wet; the gutters carry away ash and prayers in equal proportion.

**Who the cohort meets:** Liturge Marent-Veillarde the guild-master (will lend, owes, collects, knows everyone, will offer the cohort a place to stay and a debt to remember); Severa Marent of House Marent at her beeswax shed (asks too many questions of priests; will ask too many of the cohort); a Reliquary Ward broker who can sell them a saint's tooth (real, blessed, useless) for the price of a story; a Mort-Censorium censer-tender who has been keeping his own markers and is afraid.

---

##### 5. THE UNDER-WARD RING — Lamplost Ward, Quietus Ward, the Carcer

**Character:** Lower, older, narrower. The Pyric Wall's seven courses descend in tight terraces here; you climb stairs to get out of the Under-Ward Ring no matter which direction you go. The light is thinner — fewer chancery oil-lamps, more open-flame Lamplost lanterns whose wicks the parishes trim themselves.

**Who lives here:** The poor faithful, the censer-tenders, the funeral trades, the Lamplost lamp-tenders, the prisoners of the Carcer, the Almoners, **Mother Aspine Vell-os-Carrenost** at her Lampgate parish, the Lay-Almoners under Bera Quist (Ferrenkin, retired forge-worker, runs translation-shock care from a back room).

**Lamplost Ward** is the parish-poor district — three orphanages, six parishes, the Lamp Tenders' Compact under Veriarch Thelos di Cinderost (who also runs the Reflected printer's press the Inquisition has been hunting for nine years). The Wednesday readings by Inquisitor-Vested Asperine de la Pyrille come back clean for nineteen months running; the Almoner has begun a parallel ledger.

**Quietus Ward** is the funeral district — undertaker's row, the Lay-Sisters of the Quiet Procession, the small mortuary chapels for souls who cannot afford the Mort-Censorium proper. The air smells of myrrh and quicklime.

**The Carcer** — single-named, never "Carcer Ward"; the article *the* marks it as the prison-quarter — is a separate keeping. Run by the Order, supervised by the Inquisition, holds the city's heretics, demonics, anomalies, and the Indicative Speaker in Cell Eight (ageless since PD 591, speaks only pre-Fall Saemurian in the indicative case, knows the names of suppressed paragons). Currently holds Jin of Macau 2019 (Battle-Mage Refuser; the Veriarch invented "Aspirant-Reluctant" for her; the Brothers of the Cinder Hand know where she sits).

**Key buildings:**
- **The Lampgate Discounts Bench** — Mother Aspine's bench, Tuesdays and Thursdays third to seventh bell, Stain-1 and Stain-2 demonic bargains via the Sixth Notary, sanctioned by the Cathedral, no one speaks of it above the Choir Ring
- **The Reflected Press** — Veriarch Thelos's printing press, prints *The Refusal* weekly, hidden in a sub-cellar beneath a Lamplost orphanage
- **The Lay-Almoner Tally-Room** — Bera Quist's back room, holds the true translation-shock death count
- **The Carcer's Cell Eight** — the Indicative Speaker; visits by sanction only
- **The Quietus Bell-Tower** — rings for every funeral, hourly during plague-weeks

**Atmosphere:** Smoke. Always smoke — from the censer-tenders' shops, from the Quietus mortuaries' quicklime, from the Lamplost wicks that burn cheaper oil. The Under-Ward Ring smells of incense and old grief and lamp-soot. The rain runs blacker here.

**Who the cohort meets:** Mother Aspine at her bench (kindly, theological, will refer a soul to the Sixth Notary for a small bargain or a small mercy); Veriarch Thelos di Cinderost in his Lamp Tenders' Compact office (carries the printer's ink-stain on his right thumb, will not ask the cohort's business, will offer them shelter if they offer truth); Bera Quist in her tally-room (Ferrenkin, no-nonsense, knows the real translation-shock count, will not say it aloud); Jin of Macau in Cell Eight if access is arranged (refusal in her teeth, Battle-Mage prototype, her arcane signature has been cross-tripping the aspersoir for six weeks); the Indicative Speaker through a wax-stopped grille (he will speak only if the cohort comes with a question in the indicative; in eight centuries he has answered three questions).

---

##### 6. THE CINDERBELOW — *Where Hell Breathes Up Through the Grates*

**Character:** Forge-light and steam. Lowest Ring, hell-adjacent, the air shimmers with heat from Ferrenkin forges and from the venting grates that no one has surveyed in two centuries. The Cinderbelow is not on the chancery map; the chancery's map shows a smooth lower border and a single labeled tunnel ("Service Access"). The Cinderbelow itself maps the chancery, in chalk, on the inside of the Brokerage's back door.

**Who lives here:** Ferrenkin smith-families (the Ironcount, the Slag-Hand, the Slag-Tongue, the Iron-Eye), the Smallhanders (the under-ward registry-keepers), brokers of every stripe, the under-ward poor who could not afford even the Under-Ward Ring rents, the Conscripted League who meets at the Last Lamp on new-moon nights, the Caer-Druin parallel-ledger singers who keep their counter-song in pre-Old-Tongue, Old Pell the Rationer at the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp's back-room tea-house.

**Key buildings:**
- **The Brokerage of the First Light** — Nera Slag-Hand the Elder's office, off the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp, where Grace-rationing and mortal-debt trades are settled
- **The Audit-Below Registry (Cinderbelow location)** — the mortal-debt registry, run by the Smallhanders, distinct from the under-cathedral Audit-Below archive (same name, different building, the chancery tolerates the collision and the Smallhanders prefer it)
- **The Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp** — pub above, tea-house behind, Old Pell's Grace-rationing market in the back parlor
- **The Last Lamp** — heretical chapel at the deepest Cinderbelow level, Conscripted League meetings on new-moon nights, Wren Ashlin presiding
- **The Ironcount Forge** — needle-smithy; produces every copper bargain-needle (the Swallow) in the city; Marent of the Slag-Hand the current eldest
- **Brak Iron-Eye's Forge** — small, hidden, keeps the secret tower-count slate

**Atmosphere:** Heat and forge-smoke and the wet-iron smell of slag-water. The grates breathe out warm sulfur breath; the children who play here speak a whistling-language that no surface scholiast has cataloged. The Cinderbelow has its own clock — the Ferrenkin forges' shift-bell — and Pyrian bells reach here only as distant memory.

**Who the cohort meets:** Nera Slag-Hand the Elder at the Brokerage (67, missing left hand, will broker anything, will not broker a deal she thinks her daughter would refuse); Old Pell at his tea-house back-room (will sell Grace-doses at the current Bench Rate — 1 dose = 1 second-tier favor, this week — will refuse demonic work); Wren Ashlin at the Last Lamp on new-moon nights (former Battle-Mage Called, organizes the Refused, will recruit if cohort shows the right kind of doubt); a Caer-Druin parallel-ledger singer who will sing the cohort their own count in a tongue they cannot understand; Asperine Vesselain the Heretic-Broker in a moveable parlor that changes weekly (six failed Inquisition interrogations, the most dangerous broker in the city).

---

##### 7. THE PYRIC WARD — *The Wall Itself*

**Character:** The Pyric Wall is its own ward. Seven concentric courses, eighty towers on the chancery roll, eighty-four true (four silently condemned in PD 583 — the Standing year). The wall is staffed by the Order Numerati in three watches. The light is the gray light of frontier weather; the wind smells of mire and of the distant Hordes' camp-smoke.

**Who lives here:** Order soldiers on rotation (no one is permanently quartered on the wall; rotations are eighteen days on, six off), wall-priests who perform the daily warding-formulae, Mournwing couriers landing on the upper spires, occasional Caer-Druin who sing the dusk Watch-Cantos.

**Key buildings:**
- **The Pyric Bell** — the great wall-bell, tolls for every soul's last Grace-spending and for every Hordeflesh breach
- **The Mute Tower** — one of the four silently condemned; chancery roll says "under repair, indefinite"; Brak Iron-Eye knows
- **The Vigil-Stations** — eighty manned (chancery), eighty-four true; each station's Lampwarden day-book is kept on a wrist-chain (canon-historical fact)
- **The Outer Cohort's Marching Yard** — where new Order files form up before assignment

**Atmosphere:** Wind, iron, distant horns. The Pyric Ward smells of bell-grease, of wet stone, of the alchemical wash applied weekly to the wall to retard Hordeflesh corrosion. At dusk the Caer-Druin Watch-Cantos rise from the upper terraces; the Cathedral has folded these into the orthodox vesper-mass and now claims the songs were always Vespertine.

**Who the cohort meets:** Marshal-Vested Orric Veillarde of the Lower Pyr (63, wall commander, Pyric hardliner, secretly Sustainist, best wall-commander in living memory, dying — Cathedral infirmary knows, Order does not); a Mournwing courier unwrapping wings at a landing-spire; a Caer-Druin singer at vespers who will not break the song to speak.

---

##### 8. THE ALMONGATE WARD — *The Almoners' Quarter*

**Character:** The Almongate is the ward where the Cathedral's charity is administered — the soup-kitchens, the orphanages, the bread-doles, the libellus gratiae chits distributed to the working poor for sub-clinical Grace top-ups. The Almongate is also where Inquisitor-Magisterial Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost's Almongate Cluster reads parish Stain; her best Reader is also her former student Asperine Nocta who is hiding 2.4 Stain.

**Who lives here:** Almoners, orphans, parish bread-bakers, the working poor who line up at fourth bell for the dole, the Vesperine Lampwardens who administer the libellus chits, the Inquisitor-Vested Mauritz Aurriste-cadet (Vesperine, runs the Almongate's hardline reading).

**Key buildings:**
- **The Almongate Soup-House** — runs by Mother Aspine when she is not at her Lampgate bench
- **The Almoners' Vigil** — Vexillarius Severa Aurriste-cadet's patronage, a weekly vigil for the bread-poor
- **The Almongate Veriquest Sub-Office** — Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost's working office, where she suspects (wrongly) that Asperine Nocta is under-reporting

**Atmosphere:** The Almongate smells of bread (Mort-Censorium ash in the flour) and of vigil-grain incense and of the cheap soap the Almoners use to wash the orphans. The light is kinder here — more south-facing windows, more open courtyards. The cobbles are washed weekly by Almoner-apprentices on hands and knees.

**Who the cohort meets:** Mother Aspine at the soup-house (kindly, theological); Inquisitor-Magisterial Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost in the sub-office (will read the cohort if asked, will not invent a reading); Asperine Nocta in passing — pale, quiet, 27, the cohort may be the first to notice she does not meet the eyes of children.

---

##### 9. THE RELIQUARY WARD — *Where the Bones Are Sold*

**Character:** A radial ward inside the Common Ring; relic-mongers' shops three deep on Saintwomb Lane, with brothels behind them and pawnshops in between. The Reliquary Ward is the canon-perfect Constantine street — incense and cheap perfume in the same breath, a finger-bone in glass beside a card for a brothel.

**Who lives here:** Relic-mongers, certified and uncertified; pawnbrokers; the working women and men of Saintwomb Lane; touts; pilgrims from the marches who come once a year to buy a splinter; the Reliquary Ward's own small Inquisitorial sub-office that mostly looks the other way for a Stain-1 favor.

**Key buildings:**
- **The Hall of Saints** — official relic-house; certified relics with chancery wax-seals
- **Saintwomb Lane** — the brothel street, three doors from the Hall of Saints
- **The Brass Pelican** (also Common Ring) — Pyrian Mercantile Guild HQ, doubles as the Reliquary Ward's informal court of disputes
- **Hester Brunn's last known parlor** — empty, watched

**Atmosphere:** Incense, perfume, lamp-soot, the dry musk of old bone. The Reliquary Ward never sleeps; pilgrims come at all hours, the working women keep their lanterns lit through the watches.

**Who the cohort meets:** A relic-broker who will sell them a real bone of a real saint for a price they can pay or a story they cannot tell again; a Saintwomb Lane keeper who has a back room and a memory; a Brother of the Cinder Hand watching the empty parlor.

---

##### 10. THE QUIETUS WARD — *Where the City Buries Itself*

**Character:** Funeral district, north of the Mort-Censorium. Undertaker's row, the Lay-Sisters of the Quiet Procession, the small mortuary chapels for the souls whose families cannot afford the Mort-Censorium's furnace-fee. The Quietus is hushed even by Sebastopyr standards.

**Who lives here:** Undertakers, the Lay-Sisters, the lay-sextoners, the families of recently dead taking the seven-day Quiet Walk past the chapels.

**Key buildings:**
- **The Chapel of the Quiet Procession** — Lay-Sisters' chapter house
- **The Pauper's Mort** — small mortuary furnace for the unaffordable, ash returned to the families in lead boxes (the Mort-Censorium's larger furnace keeps the ash; the city eats it)
- **The Wall-of-Names (Quietus copy)** — a smaller copy of the Order's wall, here for civilian dead

**Atmosphere:** Myrrh, quicklime, beeswax. The Quietus is the quietest ward in the city. People walk softly. The rain runs cleaner here, somehow.

**Who the cohort meets:** A Lay-Sister of the Quiet Procession who will register a death without questions for a coin and a name (she will keep her own ledger); an undertaker who remembers every face that has been through his door in forty years; the chapel-sextoner who has been counting the unrecorded deaths since PD 591 and has eight thousand on his slate.

---

##### 11. THE FERRENKIN QUARTER (CINDERBELOW SUBDIVISION) — *The Forges*

**Character:** A district-within-a-district. The Ferrenkin do not call their quarter by any Vespertine name; they call it *Erdunost* — "the place-of-the-iron-deep." The chancery map labels it "Lower Industry." The forges run day and night; the Ferrenkin shift-bell is the loudest timekeeper in the Cinderbelow.

**Who lives here:** Ferrenkin smith-families (six major clans, twenty-three lesser), apprentices, the Ferrenkin Numerati who serve in the Order's Tenth File and rotate home between watches.

**Key buildings:**
- **The Ironcount Needle-Smithy** — copper bargain-needles, every Swallow in the city
- **Brak Iron-Eye's Forge** — small, hidden, the tower-count slate
- **The Erdunost Reading-Room** — Korreth Slag-Tongue's private aspersoir-laboratory where the iron-shot aspersoirs are built and the parallel Carcer-intake readings happen (31% anomaly, vs official 99.7% clean)
- **The Ferrenkin Forge-Hall** — communal forge for clan-shared work

**Atmosphere:** Heat. Smoke. The hammer-rhythm that the Ferrenkin time their workdays by. The Ferrenkin Quarter smells of slag-water, of brimstone (the Vell-os-Carrenost monopoly stockpile feeds these forges), of the metallurgical Old-Tongue that the surface scholiasts do not recognize as Old-Tongue.

**Who the cohort meets:** Korreth Slag-Tongue (94, Ferrenkin Reader-Adjunct, will give them a true reading if they sit for it); Brak Iron-Eye (62, will show the tower-slate to someone who has earned it); Marent of the Slag-Hand at the Needle-Smithy (eldest of the Ironcount; will sell a Swallow if the buyer can name the bargain).

---

#### III. KEY LOCATIONS — Spatial-Manage Ready

> Twelve specific rooms, ready for `spatial_manage` district + room generation. Each has atmospherics, who is present at the canonical default time, scene-type, and the throughline-test it serves.

##### KEY LOCATION 1 — THE VOCATION HOUSE INNER CHAMBER

- **Ring/Ward:** Choir Ring, north terrace
- **Scene-type:** Calling Rite / Discernment / first-encounter for newly-Called cohorts
- **Atmospherics:** Domed chamber, 24 summoners ranged in a half-circle on a tiered marble floor inlaid with the Vocatio Sebastina sigils. The air is alkaline with vigil-grain smoke and the metallic burn of summoned trans-dimensional cold. Twenty-four beeswax tapers, one per summoner, flicker in a wind that is not in the room. The floor is stained — pale brown — where translation-shock dead have been removed by iron-wheeled cart down the back stair. The walls are hung with the Vocatio Sebastina embroidered in gold thread on black silk; the embroidery is centuries old and the gold thread is being slowly polished away by every cohort's Discernment.
- **Who is present:** The 24 summoners (Pyric Cathedrate trained, robed in dove-grey vested chasubles); Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde (rehearsing the chant); Archvigil Severa di Mauritz (making the nine-second Discernment, then turning her back to drink water from a brass flask); two Postulants ready with the Auxiliary Roll; the iron-wheeled cart and its handler at the back stair; the new cohort, dazed, on the marble.
- **Throughline tests:** 1 (Calling rite is operational), 6 (Discernment routes Battle-Mages to Auxiliary Roll), 3 (every soul logged at threshold). What the cohort sees and Asperine knows is not the same thing.

##### KEY LOCATION 2 — THE LAMPGATE DISCOUNTS BENCH (MOTHER ASPINE'S BENCH)

- **Ring/Ward:** Under-Ward Ring, Lamplost Ward, Lampgate parish-square
- **Scene-type:** Sanctioned demonic-bargain broker-room
- **Atmospherics:** A worn oak bench in a parish-square under a stone arch. The arch has a Pyric niche with a small lamp (Lamplost wick, parish-trimmed). Mother Aspine sits with a folded leather bargain-book, a beeswax stylus, and a copper Swallow already threaded. The square is half-busy: parish-poor lining up for the Tuesday bread-dole at the next stall over, children playing the truncated Arrow-Counter's Rhyme three feet from where a Stain-1 bargain is being struck. A small chalkboard on the bench-side: *Bench open Tuesdays / Thursdays, third bell to seventh. Stain-1 and Stain-2 only. The Sixth Notary attends.* The smell is bread, beeswax, and the very faint dry-burning-metal scent that the Sixth Notary's attendance leaves.
- **Who is present:** Mother Aspine Vell-os-Carrenost (60s, kindly, theological); a queue of three to five petitioners; one Almoner-apprentice keeping records; the Sixth Notary (invisible to most, present in the form of a faint indentation in the air between Aspine and the petitioner).
- **Throughline tests:** 3 (every bargain logged), 4 (the righteous mother is a tolerated channel for hell), 5 (sacred and seedy share the bench), 6 (the chancery knows and tolerates; the bench has no chancery seal).

##### KEY LOCATION 3 — THE DRINKINGS-OF-THE-LAST-LAMP (BACK TEA-ROOM)

- **Ring/Ward:** Cinderbelow, just below Marshal Ring boundary
- **Scene-type:** Grace-rationing market / mortal-bargain ledger / cohort recruitment
- **Atmospherics:** A back parlor reached through the Drinkings pub's kitchen and down four worn stone steps. Low-ceilinged, smoke-stained, with a single long oak table and one Lamplost lantern. Old Pell sits at the head with a leather day-book and three small clay vials of consecrated water for the Grace-doses he keeps in lead-lined boxes beneath the table. The walls are hung with sailors' nets and a single Caer-Druin harp on a peg (a gift, kept tuned, never played). The smell is tea, lamp-oil, and the very faint sweetness of consecrated water beginning to lose its consecration. The Brokerage of the First Light operates from a side-door off this parlor — Nera Slag-Hand the Elder's office two steps down.
- **Who is present:** Old Pell the Rationer (60s, retired Order quartermaster, refuses demonic work); two regulars (an Order corporal off-duty, an Almoner); occasionally Nera Slag-Hand the Elder coming in through the side-door for a cup; in the small hours, Wren Ashlin if she has business.
- **Throughline tests:** 3 (Bench Rate is canon; debt is logged), 5 (Cinderbelow tea-house at the edge of the Marshal Ring; Order regulars), 1 (Grace as physical resource, doses, vials).

##### KEY LOCATION 4 — THE CATHEDRAL OF THE ENDURING ONE (HIGH ALTAR + KEEL-THRONE)

- **Ring/Ward:** Sanctuary Ring, apex
- **Scene-type:** Audience with Sebastopater / formal rite / climax scene
- **Atmospherics:** A nave of seven aisles converging on a high altar of black basalt and a keel-throne carved from the bow-block of the burned ship *Aurriste*, dark wood polished by six centuries of Sebastopater hands. Stained glass aged to honey; the light at noon is the color of warm cider. The smell is cold candle, vigil-grain, beeswax (House Marent's finest), and the very faint old-fire smell that no one has ever fully identified (the keel-block remembers the burning). The flagstones are worn into prayer-shaped depressions before the altar. A small placard, never replaced, names the keel-block "GIFT OF AN OLD HOUSE."
- **Who is present:** Sebastopater Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX (81, fragile, weeps easily, holds his ivory tally-beads in his right hand at all times); Confessor Mortane standing one pace behind the throne (Vesperine, 53, leather portfolio under his arm, will speak if asked, will redirect if not asked); two Sworn Lectors at the high altar; the Aspirant's empty seat to the throne's left, dust-free, dressed weekly.
- **Throughline tests:** 6 (the keel-throne IS the buried Aurriste connection; the Sebastopater does not know), 4 (Iohanne is genuinely good and genuinely complicit), 2 (Mortane reads clean every Octave; his Stain hides perfectly).

##### KEY LOCATION 5 — THE AUDIT-BELOW (STRATUM FOUR, CANTORIAL SCRIBES' WORKROOM)

- **Ring/Ward:** Beneath the Cathedral, accessed via the Mort-Censorium's lower passage and the Cantor's Stair
- **Scene-type:** Discovery / heist / forbidden access / confrontation with curation
- **Atmospherics:** A low vaulted chamber, fourth descending stratum. Slate-floored, slate-shelved. Bone-handled scalpels in a velvet tray on a long oak table. Beeswax tablets, warmed in palm, scattered. A small forge for warming the wax. The cursivus sebastinus minor flows in dark ink on slate; the older entries are tarnished to near-illegibility. Seven stools at the long table — one empty, the murdered Confessor Thelos di Carrenost's. The smell is old beeswax, ink-iron, slate-dust, and the faint corpse-cold smell of stone that has not seen sunlight in centuries. Three small shelves hold the SUPPRESSED PARAGON SHEETS — seventy-three named, forty-eight nameless, the slate slightly darker.
- **Who is present:** Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste (Vesperine, 45, working at the head of the table); two other Cantorial Scribes (rotating); Postulant Liturge di Carrenost in the antechamber being assessed for the empty seat she does not yet know she is being courted for.
- **Throughline tests:** 6 (this is the throughline's KEEL; the curated count lives here), 4 (Velim writes the doctrine in genuine certainty), 3 (every entry is a ledger entry).

##### KEY LOCATION 6 — THE HALL OF THE LONG VIGIL (VEXILLARIUS'S CHAMBER)

- **Ring/Ward:** Marshal Ring, Marshal Boulevard
- **Scene-type:** Order audience / oath / Grace-reserve distribution / standing-check
- **Atmospherics:** A stone-vaulted chamber with the Vexillarius's standard chained at its keel to the floor — the chain is a canon-historical fact, the standard may not leave the city. A brass-rimmed clock on the wall whose tick is audible at all times. The Wall-of-Names runs along one side; the wall has been re-faced four times (the smooth places are visible if you know to look). Severa Aurriste-cadet works at an oak desk with a single clean blotter, a brass inkwell, and her Roll-number tattoo just visible at her left wrist. A small side-table holds a brass flask (water) and a stack of libellus gratiae chits in their wax-sealed sleeves.
- **Who is present:** Marshal-Vested Severa Aurriste-cadet (41, Vexillarius, cool, courteous, will give the cohort an honest read); a Lectorate clerk taking notes; occasionally Marshal-Vested Orric Veillarde dropping by on his slow descent.
- **Throughline tests:** 3 (Roll-numbers, standing-ledger), 4 (Severa is righteous, refused two divine bargains, would give her own Grace before allowing a soldier hers), 1 (Grace as physical chits in wax sleeves).

##### KEY LOCATION 7 — THE VERIQUEST (READING-CELL OF INQUISITOR-MAGISTERIAL SEVERA DI VELL-OS-CARRENOST)

- **Ring/Ward:** Marshal Ring, off the Hall of the Long Vigil
- **Scene-type:** Stain-reading / interrogation / disclosure
- **Atmospherics:** A small bare cell with a single chair, a small writing-desk, and the aspersoir on a stone plinth — a brass instrument, three feet tall, with mercury in a sealed glass column and six tick-bands on a calibrated brass dial. The instrument smells of mercury and brass-polish. The chair is wood, hard, deliberately uncomfortable. A small grille in the wall opens onto a Sworn Lectorate office where a clerk transcribes the reading. The light is a single oil-lamp; Severa's hands are always cold; she warms them at a small brazier before placing them on the petitioner.
- **Who is present:** Inquisitor-Magisterial Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost (51, the Office's best Reader, soft-spoken, smells of vigil-grain); one Lector-Scribe behind the grille; whoever has been called.
- **Throughline tests:** 2 (the aspersoir reads what the doctrine wants seen; the dual-scale is hidden in the instrument), 1 (Stain is operational, metered, exhaustible to falsify), 4 (Severa is the most righteous Reader in the city and her best reading will not catch a hidden Stain — her trust IS the danger).

##### KEY LOCATION 8 — THE BROKERAGE OF THE FIRST LIGHT (NERA SLAG-HAND THE ELDER'S OFFICE)

- **Ring/Ward:** Cinderbelow, off the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp
- **Scene-type:** Mortal-bargain striking / debt-collection / information-trade
- **Atmospherics:** A windowless stone room two steps below the Drinkings' tea-room. One oak table, two stools, three lead-lined boxes against the wall holding her ledgers. A single lamp. Nera sits with her right hand on the table and the place where her left hand was tucked against her side. The smell is forge-smoke (from the Erdunost Quarter beyond), tea, and the faint sulfur breath of the Cinderbelow's hell-grates. A small Ferrenkin clan-sigil burned into the table's edge. A chalkboard near the door: today's Bench Rate, the day's open debts.
- **Who is present:** Nera Slag-Hand the Elder (67, missing left hand, retired Lampwarden 568-585); occasionally one of her Smallhander clerks; whoever has come to bargain.
- **Throughline tests:** 3 (mortal debt is logged with the same rigor as divine oath), 5 (the Brokerage is two steps from the Order's favorite pub), 4 (Nera will refuse a bargain she thinks her daughter would refuse — her righteousness is also a danger to a desperate petitioner).

##### KEY LOCATION 9 — THE LAST LAMP (HERETICAL CHAPEL, NEW-MOON NIGHTS)

- **Ring/Ward:** Cinderbelow, lowest level, no chancery map-name
- **Scene-type:** Refusal / Conscripted League meeting / underground organization
- **Atmospherics:** A small chapel-shaped chamber at the deepest accessible Cinderbelow level. The lamp is genuinely the last — a Lamplost wick in a single brass lantern, hung from a low iron beam. The walls are old Caer-Druin stone, predating the Cathedral; faint older sigils show through the lamp-soot. Wooden benches for thirty. The smell is lamp-soot, old stone, and the faint chemical bite of paper-and-ink (the Brothers of the Cinder Hand bring fresh issues of *The Refusal*). The chapel is silent until the meeting begins, then the language is the practical Pyrian of people who have decided to disobey carefully.
- **Who is present (new-moon nights only):** Wren Ashlin (former Cohort of the Long Patience Battle-Mage, organizer); twenty to forty Refused or wavering Called; one or two Brothers of the Cinder Hand running the press; occasionally a Caer-Druin singer with the parallel ledger.
- **Throughline tests:** 4 (the Refused are the morally clearest people in the city and are by doctrine the most condemned), 6 (the Last Lamp keeps a counter-ledger that the chancery does not have), 5 (heretical chapel in the lowest Ring; the most honest room in Sebastopyr).

##### KEY LOCATION 10 — CONFESSOR MORTANE'S CHANCERY OFFICE

- **Ring/Ward:** Choir Ring, adjacent to the Sebastopater's chambers
- **Scene-type:** Information control / political pressure / discovery of intercepted correspondence
- **Atmospherics:** A small, tidy office. Three leather portfolios stacked on a desk (the cohort does not know which is which: one is the daily filing for the Sebastopater, one is the redirected, one is what does not get filed at all). A locked correspondence-cabinet behind Mortane's chair. A small brazier always lit, even in summer (Vesperine constitution runs cold). A single window onto a north courtyard; the light is always thin. The smell is paper, beeswax, leather, and the faint Vesperine cold that follows Mortane wherever he goes. On the wall: a small icon of Saint Severa di Pyrigorne — the Vesperine martyr, Mortane's chosen patron, the irony unintentional.
- **Who is present:** Confessor Mortane (53, soft-voiced, hands always folded, will offer tea); occasionally a chancery clerk delivering or collecting; very rarely, Sebastopater Iohanne crossing through to the Cantor's terrace.
- **Throughline tests:** 4 (Mortane edits in love), 6 (he IS the official-story curator at the human scale), 2 (his Stain has read clean for 23 years; the chancery's own most-trusted Reader cannot find it).

##### KEY LOCATION 11 — THE LAMP TENDERS' COMPACT (VERIARCH THELOS'S OFFICE)

- **Ring/Ward:** Under-Ward Ring, Lamplost Ward
- **Scene-type:** Underground press / shelter / dissident sanctuary / information broker
- **Atmospherics:** A modest parish office above a Lamplost orphanage. The ink-stain on Veriarch Thelos's right thumb is the first thing you notice. The office holds parish books, a small icon of Saint Asperine of the Lamps, and a writing-desk with three pens and a careful order. The window opens onto the orphanage courtyard; children's voices float up. Below the office, accessed through a trapdoor under the rug that even the orphans do not know about, is the Reflected printer's press. The smell is parish-tallow candles, orphanage-laundry soap, and the very faint metallic smell of ink that the trapdoor lets out.
- **Who is present:** Veriarch Thelos di Cinderost (parish priest, Lamp Tenders' Compact head, runs *The Refusal*); occasionally an apprentice Almoner; whoever has come for shelter.
- **Throughline tests:** 4 (Thelos is righteous and also doing something the doctrine calls heresy and the Constantine throughline calls truth), 5 (orphanage above, dissident press below), 6 (Thelos is the visible alternative-curation, hunted nine years).

##### KEY LOCATION 12 — THE INDICATIVE SPEAKER'S CELL (CARCER CELL EIGHT)

- **Ring/Ward:** Under-Ward Ring, the Carcer
- **Scene-type:** Discovery / forbidden testimony / scene with a witness who knows
- **Atmospherics:** A stone cell, deeper than most Carcer cells (the floor is two steps below the corridor). Iron-grilled door with a wax-stopped speaking-grille at chest height. The prisoner sits cross-legged on the floor — ageless, indeterminate, eyes that are too old. The cell holds nothing but a stone bench, a clay cup, a chamber-pot, and a thin straw pallet. The smell is straw, stone, the faint mineral cold of a cell that has held the same body since PD 591. The grille is wax-stopped because the chancery would prefer it not be opened often. The Indicative Speaker speaks pre-Fall Saemurian only, only in the indicative case, and only when a question is asked of him in the indicative. In two hundred and fifteen years he has answered three questions.
- **Who is present:** The Indicative Speaker; an Order guard at the corridor's end (will not approach the cell within twenty paces; the indication-pressure makes him uneasy); whoever has bribed, sanctioned, or stolen their way to the grille.
- **Throughline tests:** 6 (the Indicative Speaker knows the names of suppressed paragons — the curation has a witness, kept caged), 2 (his Stain has never registered; he is not a demon, not a saint, not anything the doctrine can classify), 4 (the Order does not torture him because no one is sure he can be harmed; the Inquisition does not approach because his reading comes back UNKNOWN).

---

#### IV. WALKING THE BELL — A One-Day Tour for a Cohort

A native Pyrian (Liturge Marent-Veillarde of the Pyric Mercantile Guild, say, owing the cohort a favor) would route a newly-arrived cohort thus:

1. **First bell (dawn):** Sanctuary Ring exterior, Cathedral plaza. See the Pyric Bell toll for the night's Grace-spent. Do not enter; you have not been invited.
2. **Third bell:** Choir Ring tour from the public side. The Vocation House from across the plaza only. Postulants pass with dockets.
3. **Fifth bell:** Marshal Ring. The Hall of the Long Vigil's outer chamber, the Wall-of-Names, the brass-rimmed clock.
4. **Seventh bell:** Common Ring. The Great Market, the Brass Pelican (introductions), the Reliquary Ward, a relic-broker, a meal at a Saintwomb Lane chop-house.
5. **Ninth bell:** Almongate. Bread-dole. Mother Aspine if she is at the soup-house. A first quiet exposure to the libellus gratiae system.
6. **Eleventh bell:** Under-Ward Ring. Lamplost (the parish, not the press). Quietus (silently). The Carcer only from outside.
7. **First bell after midnight:** Cinderbelow. Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp. Old Pell's parlor. Optionally, the side-door to Nera Slag-Hand's Brokerage, if the cohort has business.

The cohort will not see the Audit-Below, the Aspirant's Lodgings, the Veriquest reading-cells, or the Indicative Speaker's cell on a first day. Those are paid for in standing, in debt, in oath. As everything in Sebastopyr is.

---

#### V. A CLOSING NOTE ON ATMOSPHERE

Sebastopyr at night is the Constantine city in full: rain on cobbles, bells at the quarter-hour, the smell of incense and Mort-Censorium ash and the faint sulfur breath of Cinderbelow grates, lamp-light through stained glass, a parish bell ringing for a soul whose last Grace has been spent on the wall, a fight outside a Saintwomb Lane chop-house, a Cantorial Scribe descending the Cantor's Stair by lantern-light to forge cursivus sebastinus minor on slate, a Mournwing courier landing on a Sanctuary spire with a letter folded inside her wing-canvas, the Sebastopater weeping in the lower transept because he has begun to lose count of the ivory tally-beads in his right hand, the Paragon in his outpost ten years gone writing a question that will be intercepted and filed without answer.

The city holds. The bell rings. The count is kept. The saint endures.

Yet.

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:the_city_itself` (the city itself)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* Sebastopyr is the only place in Aevarn where rain falls THROUGH the smoke of two hundred censers before it touches stone, and the citizens taste the difference between a Cathedral rain (which leaves a faint iron-and-myrrh film on the tongue) and a Cinderbelow rain (which leaves nothing, because the Cinderbelow drinks it). The city is RING-SORTED by grace-altitude: the closer you live to the Cathedral, the more Grace passively accrues in your daily breath, and the closer you live to the Cinderbelow, the more Stain quietly drips into yours — which means the geography of Sebastopyr is, mechanically, a slow vertical bargain no one named. The Pyric Wall is not a defensive structure that happens to be holy; it is a holy structure that happens to be defensive, and the distinction is why the wall-rites take precedence over the wall-repairs in the chancery's budget, and why three towers are condemned-and-renumbered rather than rebuilt. The under-ward broker-rooms can sell you a strike_bargain in the time it takes a Cathedral bell to finish ringing, which is exactly long enough that the bell counts as witness to the deal and therefore, by chancery liturgical precedent, sanctifies the venue — a loophole the brokers exploit and the Cathedral pretends not to know. The Calling ritual happens in a chamber the city's daily rhythm is built around without naming: bells are silenced for the Mass of Arrival, markets close, the Mournwing do not fly, and everyone pretends this is not happening, which is the most Sebastopyric act of all. The Constantine texture is literal here: there is no district in Sebastopyr where you cannot hear a bell, smell incense, and see a deal being made within the same minute. The city's particular signature, distinct from any other bastion-city, is that ITS BUREAUCRACY IS LITURGY — a clerk filing a report and a priest performing a rite are not analogically similar; they are doctrinally the same act, and this is why losing a file is heresy and why the deepest corruption lives in the chancery rather than in the under-ward.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The smell of the Cathedral Ring on a wet morning: wet limestone, myrrh, gun-grease from the Order's morning drills, and the faint copper of consecrated mercury that has boiled and re-cooled in a Reader's brass aspersoir overnight.
> - The Pyric Bell does not toll on the hour. It tolls when a soul on the wall spends its last Grace and the rite registers the spending. Citizens of the Cathedral Ring sleep through it; citizens of the Cinderbelow count it.
> - Children's rhyme heard in Lamplost Ward: 'One arrow, two arrow, three for the saint / Four arrow, five arrow, count what you ain't.' The last line is the joke; the count that you AREN'T is the one the Cathedral keeps.
> - The curse 'Ad audit!' said with a shrug means 'to hell with it.' Said with the eyes closed and the right hand making the small downward gesture (palm to floor, fingers spread) it means 'I am calling the Auditor as witness to this oath' — a binding most who use it do not know they have invoked.
> - The hand-gesture of the Vesperine inquisitor when greeting another Vesperine: a brief touch of the right thumb to the left wrist, where the pulse is. It is read by the Cathedral as a courteous bow of equals. Among the Vesperine it is the silent question: 'Are you still clean?'
> - Mournwing perched on the upper spires at dusk make a low, three-note keening that the bell-keepers call 'the wing-vigil.' On nights the Calling is performed, the Mournwing do not keen. Their silence is the only public sign that the rite is happening.

---

## V. Timeline — Deep History and the Recent Triumph

### HISTORICAL TIMELINE
##### Sebastopyr · The Reclaimed Crown of Vespertin · Aevarn · Therimaur
*A chronology compiled in the indicative case from the curated register, with annotations marking the seams where the deemed register diverges.*

---

#### ON THE DATING SYSTEM

The Pyrian world reckons all years from THE FALL. The official designation is **PD** — *Post Damnationem*, "after the damning" — formally pronounced in the Old-Tongue as *Post Damnationem Mundi* but spoken in everyday Vespertine simply as "the year." Before-Fall dates carry **PT** — *Pre-Tenebras*, "before the dark" — and run backward from the Year of Reading (PD 0).

Three things to note about the calendar before reading the chronicle:

1. **There is no Year Zero in the indicative register.** The Cathedral's official chronology jumps from PT 1 to PD 1 because the Old-Tongue lacks a future tense in liturgical mode, and the year of the Fall was deemed by the founders to be God's tense, not mortals' — therefore unnameable. The chancery uses **PD 0** only in administrative records, never in liturgy. (A scholar reading a document that names PD 0 in a sacred context is reading a forgery, or a heresy, or a private record never meant for the light.)
2. **The year begins at the Octave of the Standing**, twenty-three days after the autumnal equinox, which was the day Halden Orriste held the line in PD 583. This calendar reform was promulgated in PD 589 with the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity. Before PD 589, the year began at the vernal equinox (the **Vernal Reckoning**), and pre-589 dates in old chancery documents must be silently shifted by readers — a known and tolerated source of off-by-one errors in the deep archive.
3. **The Old-Tongue distinguishes the indicative case from the deemed case.** A year written *Anno PD DLXXXIII* (583 PD, indicative) is a year that occurred. A year written *Anno Decreto PD DLXXXIII* (583 PD, decreed) is a year the Cathedral has decided occurred a particular way. Most public chronicles use the decreed case without marking it. **Throughout this timeline, dates given without comment are decreed-case unless otherwise specified.**

**Current year: PD 606.** Twenty-three years since the Standing. The Crown is in its twenty-third year of Reclamation.

---

#### I. THE BEFORE — PT (Pre-Tenebras)

The pre-Fall chronology is recorded in three reservoirs and contradicted in two of them.

##### PT c. 1200 — *The Saemurian Foundations*
The pre-collapse polity that built the first watchfire-stones along the Pyric ridge. The Cathedral teaches them as a holy theocracy that prefigured the bastion's rites. The Caer-Druin sing of them differently — as administrators who paid hell's representatives in tribute for four centuries before the tribute came due. Both readings are in the archive. Only one is in the catechism.

##### PT 400-100 — *The Long Door, opening*
Periodic incursions of the Damned through what the deep archive calls *the Long Door* — a slow-widening aperture in the lower delvings beneath Therimaur. The Saemurian Theocracy responded with the Treaty Liturgies (recorded in *cursivus sebastinus minor*, locked stratum), a sequence of formal bargains with what would later be called the demonic offices. The bargains held the Door. The bargains also wrote names into the Long Ledger that came due in the Fall.

> **GAP NOTE.** The Cathedral's public chronology elides PT 400 through PT 47. Nine centuries of recorded history are summarized in the catechism as *"the long preparation."* The Audit-Below's seventh stratum contains the elided records. They are written in *cursivus sebastinus minor* and accessible only by the Custodes Numeri and three living readers: **Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste**, **Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde**, and **Inquisitor-Magisterial Cassian de la Pyrille the Long Confessor**. A fourth reader — **Postulant Liturge di Carrenost**, age 22 — is rapidly approaching fluency. She is the niece of the murdered Confessor Thelos di Carrenost. She is asking questions.

##### PT 47 — *The Aurriste burns in port*
A trading ship named *Aurriste* — "the Golden Dawn" in Old-Tongue — burned at her moorings in what is now the Drownmire, then a working harbor. Cause unrecorded in the public chronicle. The Caer-Druin remember the captain's name (Brigith Halloran, later drowned PD 312 in suspicious circumstances) and sing that the burning was the first foreclosure. The ship's keel-timber, charred and salt-blackened, was recovered and stored.

##### PT 1 — *The Last Year of Tongues*
The final year of the pre-Fall calendar. The Saemurian administrative records end mid-quarter. The Cathedral teaches this as the year the Theocracy "fell silent in prayer." The Ferrenkin, who came up from the lower delvings during this year, teach it differently in their forge-songs: as the year the heat rose past the threshold the Treaty Liturgies had been holding back, and the Saemurian administrators understood what they had purchased.

---

#### II. THE FALL — PD 0 to PD 47

The Fall was not a moment. It was a forty-seven-year administrative collapse, recorded mainly in marginalia because the people maintaining the records were dying.

| Year | Event | Source |
|------|-------|--------|
| **PD 0** | The Reading of the Numbers begins. The Long Ledger calls in its accounts. Saemurian administrators begin dying in office, found at their desks with quill in hand and the wrong column tallied. | Audit-Below, stratum 6 (sealed) |
| **PD 0-12** | The high cities of Therimaur fall in succession. Public chronicle names twelve; private records name twenty-seven. The eighteen forgotten cities were paid out in the Treaty Liturgies and are listed only in *cursivus sebastinus minor*. | Cathedral catechism (12); deep archive (27) |
| **PD 9** | The PT 9 ambush — a Saemurian legion attempting evacuation of the Sustines watershed is overrun. **Patriarch Thelos Cassian-cadet of Lector's Fall**, age 71, has been corresponding with Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste about the truth of this ambush. He has a private chronicle. He has not published it. | House Cassian-cadet archive |
| **PD 14** | The Watershed Reversal. Rivers east of Sustines reverse course and begin flowing west into what become the Hordeflesh sinkholes. The Cathedral teaches this as the moment "the land turned its face toward the wall." The Ferrenkin teach it as the moment hell's geography overwrote the surface's. | Both registers agree on the event |
| **PD 23** | Sebastopyr's first curtain wall (the inner ring, now buried under the Sanctuary Ring) is completed under **First-Archvigil Severa di Pyrigorne**, who would be martyred at the Reading. | Founding ledger |
| **PD 41** | Cohorts of refugees from the fallen high cities arrive carrying the relics of their dead. The Caer-Druin, the Ferrenkin, the Vesperine, and the Mournwing all reach the wall in this decade. | Convergence Records |
| **PD 47** | **THE READING.** Saint Severa di Pyrigorne is martyred reading the names of the Sustines dead at the Almongate. The Cathedral declares the Fall completed and the war begun. The Old-Tongue indicative case *Mundus Damnatus Est* — "the world has been damned" — is canonized. **PD 47 is the last year the public chronicle and the deep archive agree on a single death-count.** Public chronicle: 1.2 million dead across the forty-seven years. Deep archive: indeterminate but greater. The discrepancy was first noted by Cantorial Scribe Iohanne Aurriste-Halloran in PD 312 and has been three times re-tabulated and three times resealed. | Catechism; Audit-Below; sealed |

> **GAP NOTE — THE FORTY-SEVEN YEARS.** The Fall is the most-curated stratum of the public chronicle. The Cathedral teaches a clean linear collapse. The deep archive shows an administrative bargain — multiple Treaty Liturgies invoked, suspended, renegotiated, and ultimately defaulted. The forty-eight nameless paragon-cases in the suppressed registry begin in PD 14, not PD 51, but this fact was extracted from the chronology by the same scribal hand that signed the PD 584 requisition removing the 565 PD Refusers' Index. **The hand is identifiable. Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde knows whose. She has not said.**

---

#### III. THE EARLY SIEGE — PD 47 to PD 200

The first century and a half of the siege established the operational doctrines that govern Sebastopyr to this day. They were not received from heaven. They were drafted, revised, ratified, and quietly amended by named men.

##### PD 51 — *The First Paragon (officially: the first saint)*
The public chronicle records the first Aspirant — **Saint Iohanne of the Almongate**, who held at the Almongate breach and was canonized after death. The official Saint Count begins at one.

The suppressed registry tells a different opening: it dates Iohanne's miracle to PD 51 but also names **three souls in PD 14, PD 29, and PD 41** who manifested divine attention and were not canonized. Two of the three were Caer-Druin. One was a Ferrenkin smelter whose name was scraped from his marker. **These are the first three of the seventy-three named-suppressed paragon cases.**

##### PD 73 — *The Keel-Block*
The charred keel-timber of the PT 47 *Aurriste* is installed beneath the new Sebastopater's throne in the Cathedral. The installing Sebastopater is **Sebastopater Cassian II**, whose chancery name has not been redacted. The reason for the installation is given in the public ledger as *"a remembrance of the first burning, that we may know the cost of the Door."*

> **CANON NOTE — THE BURIED THING.** This is the keel-block whose name-coincidence with the Paragon's polished surname would, in PD 602, be prevented from cross-referencing by a chancery clerk's stroke. *The throne the Sebastopater sits on is named for the Paragon's family.* No one currently alive knows this except Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste and Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde. Halidan himself does not know.

##### PD 108 — *The Doctrine of the Deemed Eternal*
**Sebastopater Mauritz V** and **Cantor-Magisterial Orric of the Lower Pyr** promulgate the foundational doctrine that would govern Sebastopyr for four hundred and seventy-five years: ***Bellum Aeternum Decretum*** — *The War Is Deemed Eternal*.

The doctrine's argument, as recorded in the founding text:

> *"The war is not eternal in the indicative case, for only God's works are eternal in that case. The war is eternal in the deemed case, which is to say: it has been settled by the Cathedral, in consultation with the Hierarchs, that the war shall be treated as eternal for the purposes of doctrine, rite, succession, and the rationing of Grace. Whether the war is in fact eternal is a question reserved to the Almighty, and is not for mortal scholars to decide. To deem is to choose to know."*

**This is the doctrine the Standing of PD 583 broke.** It is also the doctrine that was *quietly preserved* in the PD 589 Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity, which rescinded the eternal status of the war but did not rescind the doctrinal principle of the deemed case. The Cathedral may still deem things settled. It has not stopped.

##### PD 141 — *The Office of Sanctioned Bindings (Curiate Vincula) is instituted*
Drafts, witnesses, and files every officially sanctioned divine-bargain in the Crown. The binding formula adopted in PD 141 is word-for-word identical to a clause confiscated from a heretic-broker in PD 712, five hundred and seventy-one years later. The chancery's public position is that the heretic stole the formula from the Cathedral. **The founding ledger's marginalia record the reverse.** The marginalia are in *cursivus sebastinus minor* and have been re-shelved fourteen times.

The Office's defining feature is the *gap-where-the-saint-stood* — a legally mandated breath of silence between the grant-clause and the price-clause of every oath. Three hundred and fourteen years of records show **NO ONE has ever withdrawn during the gap.** This fact is taught as the doctrine's vindication. It might also be the doctrine's indictment.

##### PD 167 — *The first recorded calibration of the Aspersoir Scale*
**Cantor-Magisterial Severa di Almonine** and **Reader-Magisterial Cassian Ferrenkin-Halloran** (the only Ferrenkin to ever hold Reader-Magisterial rank, his name preserved by an oversight) establish the dual-scale aspersoir — the underlying 0-to-10 continuous Stain grade and the 1-to-6 operational tick-readout. The chancery makes a quiet decision: **the operational threshold for clinical concern will be calibrated to underlying 0.9.** Three subsequent recalibrations will raise this threshold to 1.2, then 1.5, then 2.0. All four calibrations sit within tick-band 2 on the operational instrument. *The instrument reads as clean what the doctrine wants seen.*

---

#### IV. THE MIDDLE SIEGE — PD 200 to PD 500

Three centuries of operational steady-state. The wall held. The Hordes broke against it. The dead were counted, the names read, and the next dawn came. Nothing in this period is taught as eventful, which is itself a tell.

The middle siege is when the curation system *matured*. The Office of the Cantorial Scribes — operational name; self-name *Custodes Numeri* — is instituted in PD 312 by **Sebastopater Velim III**, who promulgated the founding charter and was dead within the year. The charter authorizes seven scribes to maintain "the parallel register of the indicative truth" — that is, to record what actually happens, in case it must one day be reconciled with what is taught.

This is the body that, six centuries later, would hold the suppressed paragon count. **They were instituted to be the conscience of the curation, and they became its executors.** This is the world's longest slow corruption.

##### PD 312 — *Brigith Halloran of the Caer-Druin drowns*
Singer of the Watch-Cantos, daughter of the PT 47 *Aurriste*'s captain, last living person to remember her father's name in the original Caer-Druin. Drowned in the Drownmire in suspicious circumstances. Her death is recorded in the public chronicle as accidental. The Caer-Druin sing it as the second foreclosure.

##### PD 359 — *The Plate of Sebastian is sealed*
Forty-foot stratum of fused saint-bone, slag iron, and consecrated mortar laid down beneath the Cathedral over a single liturgical year by **Sebastopater Halidan IV** and the surviving Aspirant-saints of the previous century. Approximately four hundred "blessed unnamed" second-martyrs are interred.
