The canonical status of these four hundred was revised three times during the laying — promoted from "lay-blessed" to "co-martyrs" to "blessed unnamed" — and the final status erases all individual records. **The Plate is the third stratum of saint-count, after the Official Count (143) and the Suppressed Paragon Count (121).**

##### PD 411 — *The seven concentric courses of the Pyric Wall reach completion*
The Ferrenkin smith-clans record this year as the year the wall became "as it now stands." The public chronicle lists *"four hundred and eleven towers raised, three hundred eighty-three standing, twenty-eight condemned"* across all seven courses. These totals are honest. The current dispute is over the outer course's specific tower-count, which would not become a problem until PD 583.

##### PD 451 — *The Calling rite is formalized*
The ritual that pulls souls from other worlds, other Earths, other genres of existence is *not* invented in PD 451 — it predates the Fall, surviving as one of the Treaty Liturgies. What happens in PD 451 is its *formalization* as a sanctioned annual rite under **Cantor-Magisterial Severa Vell-os-Carrenost the Second**. The rite's mechanical structure — the nine-second Discernment, the three-prototype routing, the Vesperine processors — is largely unchanged from PD 451 to PD 606.

The Cohort of PD 451 was the first to be officially named: **the Cohort of the First Welcoming.** The Cohort of PD 606, currently being processed at the Vocation House, is **the Cohort of the Quiet Mercy.** Both names are taught with the same gentleness. Both populations have, in different proportions, included souls who would have preferred to remain where they were.

---

#### V. THE LATE SIEGE — PD 500 to PD 583

The eight decades preceding the Standing are when the system began to strain at its joints. Three events from this period are load-bearing.

##### PD 565 — *The Cohort of the Lost Vespers*
A Calling in which one hundred and seventeen souls manifested anomalous Grace-resonance during the nine-second Discernment. The Archvigil of the time — **Archvigil Liturge di Mauritz**, whose name was redacted from the rank-roll in PD 584 — flagged the cohort for review.

The review concluded that the one hundred and seventeen were "paragon-adjacent" — souls with the divine-attention signature but not the manifestation. They were routed to the Reclamation Corps's deepest hazard postings and died, in disproportionate numbers, within two years. **The Refusers' Index for this cohort was retained until PD 584.**

> **CANON NOTE — THE COMPOSITION OF THE SIXTH NOTARY.** The Mournwing intelligence, kept in the upper-spire martyr-rolls and shared with the Cathedral only in fragment, dates the beginning of the Sixth Notary's name-composition to **PD 565.** Hell's bureaucracy began drafting a name in the year the Cathedral suppressed one hundred and seventeen paragon-adjacent souls. The name is, in PD 606, still incomplete. *The opportunity for binding before completion is real and is not in the chancery's possession.* The Mournwing have not shared it. They have their reasons.

##### PD 583 — *THE LONG VIGIL AND THE STANDING*

The single most consequential year in six centuries.

**Spring PD 583:** The Iron March's forward outposts fall in a coordinated assault. Refugee columns reach the Almongate in numbers the chancery's grain-rationing cannot absorb. **Regent-Lord Cassian Veillarde** (predecessor of the current Regent) orders the third-tier rationing protocols.

**Late summer PD 583:** Simultaneous breach attempts at the Almongate, the Lower Pyr, and the eastern curtain. The Hordes coordinate — for the first time in recorded history — in a three-day push. The chancery's siege-rotation breaks. The Fourth Shieldwall, scheduled for eleven-hour rotations, is held in place for **twenty-two hours**.

**The eleventh hour past rotation (the Long Vigil's twenty-second hour total):** The Almongate breach widens. Relief fails to arrive. Sergeant **Halden Orriste** of the Fourth — a name half-recorded in the muster-roll as *"Hldn. Orriste"*, his first name uncertain in at least one chancery copy that reads *"Holden"* — holds the line past the point a body holds. He is twenty-eight years old. He has been on the wall for seven years.

**The Standing:** Divine attention manifests. Halden becomes the first Paragon in living memory. The Almongate holds. The Hordes break. The siege-rotation reconvenes. Eleven other survivors of the Fourth depose what they saw. Their depositions are sealed in the Audit-Below, stratum 3.

**The same day, before nightfall:** Four towers of the outer course are silently condemned and renumbered. The Mute, the old 14, the old 31, and the old 49. The condemnation orders are signed by **Cantor-Magisterial Orric of the Lower Pyr**. The towers had been compromised in the breach. The renumbering hides the breach's true extent. This is the only major curation-decision known to have been made on the same day as the Standing. The throughline reader will draw their own conclusions.

| **Named participants in the Standing** | **Status in PD 606** |
|---|---|
| Halden Orriste, Sergeant, Fourth Shieldwall (28) | Saint-Aspirant Halidan Aurriste, age 51, at Ferrostat-on-the-Mire |
| Eleven other Fourth Shieldwall survivors | All dead by PD 591; six in combat, three of "fatigue," two unrecorded |
| Cantor-Magisterial Orric of the Lower Pyr | Died PD 588, two days after the elevation of Sebastopater Iohanne IX |
| Archvigil Mauritz di Cassian | Died PD 585, of "the wall-cough" |
| The Quartermaster of Tongues | Demonic office; still active; account with Halidan OPEN |
| Sub-Vicar Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost (28) | Sebastopater Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX, age 81; blind in left eye from this year's Grace-strain |

> **THE BURIED MOMENT.** The night before the Standing, the Quartermaster of Tongues offered Halden Orriste a bargain. The offer is recorded only in the demonic Long Ledger, which the chancery cannot read but the Mournwing scholars have partial access to. Halden refused. Hours later, divine attention found him. **He has never been certain the divine attention was not the Quartermaster's second offer, accepted without his knowledge.** The account is OPEN in hell's books. This uncertainty is the single most important fact about the Paragon and is known to no one in Sebastopyr except Halidan himself.

---

#### VI. THE DOCTRINAL HARDENING — PD 583 to PD 600

The seventeen years following the Standing are when the new doctrine was built. The old doctrine had been *the war is deemed eternal*. The new doctrine had to be its replacement and its echo simultaneously — something that justified the Reclamation without indicting the six centuries that had not attempted it.

##### PD 583, autumn — *The Polishing of the Roll*
Begins within weeks of the Standing. Chancery clerks polish *"Hldn. Orriste"* to *"Halidan"* (which scans as a Vespertine saint-name) and *"Orriste"* to *"Aurriste"* (which puns on the Old-Tongue *aur-*, "gold" or "dawn"). The polishing is taught later as the natural evolution of a holy name. The clerk who initiated it was **Postulant-Scribe Velim of the Lower Choir**, age 22, who would in PD 589 author the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity at age 31. *He is the same man as the current Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste.* The cousin-relationship to the Paragon's polished name is, in PD 583, manufactured — and then, by the working of fashion, becomes true: the Aurriste-cadet branches multiply across the noble houses in the following decade because the name has become desirable.

##### PD 587 — *The Concilium Sebastinum*
**Sebastopater Cassian VII** convenes the Concilium to address the theological problem of a living saint. Canonization is reserved for the dead; Halidan is not dead; the chancery cannot canonize him and cannot leave him uncategorized. The Concilium invents the **Aspirant-rank** — a living saint, beatified but not canonized, whose Grace expenditure is metered as if from a canonized reserve. The doctrine is written by Velim Aurriste, then a Confessor-Ordinary. It is signed by Cassian VII. It is the first instance of a rank being invented to fit a person rather than the reverse.

##### PD 588 — *The taking of Ferrostat-on-the-Mire*
Halidan, now Saint-Aspirant Halidan Aurriste, leads the first sortie beyond the wall in ninety-three years. **Ferrostat-on-the-Mire** — at the time, a ruined Saemurian-era foundry-town — is taken in three days. The outpost becomes the seed of the Reclamation.

The same year:
- **Sub-Vicar Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost** is elevated to Confessor-Ordinary at age 63, on the strength of his survival of the PD 565 Vocation-strain that took his left eye. He will be Sebastopater seventeen years later. This is the elevation pattern that produces, by PD 606, four Vell-os-Carrenost senior clerics in interlocking positions of trust.
- **Postulant-Scribe Velim Aurriste** strikes the **Octave Bargain** with the Quartermaster of Tongues in the eighth night of the Octave of the Taking. The grant is doctrinal clarity — specifically, the formula that would become the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity. The price is "a future silence to be named." Velim is 31. The price has not yet been collected. *Velim does not know when it will be.*

##### PD 589 — *The Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity*
Promulgated by Sebastopater Cassian VII, drafted by Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste (elevated at 31 to draft his own doctrine). The text:

> *"The war is no longer deemed eternal, by the same authority by which it was deemed eternal in the year PD 108. The Standing of PD 583 has shown that the deeming was provisional. The deeming was a discipline, not a metaphysic. We rescind it now. The war may be won."*

The doctrine preserves the principle of the deemed case while rescinding its application. The Cathedral may still deem things settled. It chooses to deem the war winnable.

The same doctrine institutes:
- The **Octave of the Standing** as the new year-beginning.
- The **PD calendar reform** (no Year Zero, autumn equinox transition).
- The **Aspirant-Protection clauses** that would be formalized in PD 599.

##### PD 591 — *Cassian VII dies of "fatigue of the heart"*
Fourteen months after signing the Doctrine. The death is taught as the natural conclusion of a holy life. The Audit-Below's stratum 4 holds an unsigned medical-confessional indicating the Sebastopater requested a specific aspersoir reading the week before his death and was refused by his confessor. The confessor was **Mortane the Half-Kind**, then a young Vesperine Reader-Confirmed, now Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind, master of access to the current Sebastopater. He has been editing reality for thirty-three years.

Sebastopater **Mauritz I** is elevated. He will reign thirteen years.

##### PD 597 — *The Walker-Beyond-the-Wall epithet*
The fourth liturgical epithet for the Paragon is added by chancery decree. Saint-Aspirant Halidan Aurriste becomes *the Walker-Beyond-the-Wall* — a title that liturgically encodes his right to operate beyond the curtain. The decree's drafters are Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste and Confessor Mortane. The decree's *secondary function* — known to fewer than ten people — is to establish a liturgical apparatus for **succession**: a Walker-Beyond-the-Wall, in the event of the present Walker's death or incapacity, may be liturgically continued under a different name. The Aspirant-rank can be filled. The cult does not need the man.

The Vesperine Loyalty Tally faction lines crystallize this year. **Hierarch-of-the-Mire Cassian Aurriste** begins privately listing Vesperine clerics suspected of insufficient zeal. The list is currently maintained by his secretary, Marent de la Pyrille, and has 84 names on it.

##### PD 599 — *The Aspirant-Protection Ordinance*
Signed by Sebastopater Mauritz I. The Ordinance establishes the Paragon's legal-theological inviolability — restricting independent aspersoir readings, restricting access to the Aspirant's correspondence, restricting Stain-investigations within three degrees of his lineage. Enforced by **Inquisitor-Vested Orric de la Pyrille**, who is the cousin of the current Captain-Pyric and three layers of de la Pyrille kin distant from the Long Confessor. The Ordinance is taught as protection of a holy man. It is also, *operationally*, the legal apparatus by which the Paragon's daily aspersoir readings at Ferrostat — which return CLEAN every dawn for what is now twenty-three uninterrupted years, a duration that is theologically unprecedented — are filed without escalation.

---

#### VII. THE RECLAMATION YEARS — PD 600 to PD 605

| Year | Event | Named participants |
|------|-------|---------------------|
| **PD 600** | Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste's third aspersoir reading returns **UNKNOWN**. (Prior readings: PD 588 CLEAN; PD 594 ANOMALY.) The reading is filed under the Aspirant-Protection Ordinance's lineage-clause, citing his polished Aurriste-cadet status. **Sebast-Auditor** (sealed identity) authorizes the filing. | Velim Aurriste; the Sebast-Auditor; Inquisitor-Vested Orric de la Pyrille |
| **PD 601** | **BANNER-FALL.** The eastward advance, attempting to reach the ruins of Saintmire, breaks against an unanticipated Horde concentration. Three banners lost. The Paragon's left hand is crushed beneath a falling stone — the Reclamation's only major defeat that the Paragon was personally present at. **Marshal-Vested Severa Aurriste-cadet** (then a line-captain, 36) drags **Captain-Pyric Cassian di Pyrille** from the field and is afterward elevated to Vexillarius of the Order. The captured banners are not recovered. | Halidan Aurriste; Severa Aurriste-cadet; Cassian di Pyrille (dies of wounds PD 601); Cassian de la Pyrille (the surviving cousin, becomes new Captain-Pyric) |
| **PD 602** | **The chancery clerk's stroke.** A senior chancery cross-reference officer collapses at his desk while compiling the keel-throne provenance index. His successor — appointed by Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste — does not complete the cross-reference. *The keel-block's name and the Paragon's surname are never officially linked in the public registries.* The accident is, from one angle, the load-bearing accident that protects Halidan's ignorance. From another, it is the most fortunate stroke in the chancery's six-century history. | The chancery clerk (name redacted); Velim Aurriste |
| **PD 604** | **Sebastopater Mauritz I dies.** Of natural causes (chronicle); of "exhaustion of the conscience" (private medical-confessional, sealed). **Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX** is elevated immediately, at age 79. He is the second Sebastopater elevated since PD 591. The chancery has not had a stable succession in thirteen years. The institution is fragile. | Mauritz I; Iohanne IX; Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind (managing the transition) |
| **PD 605** | **THE MOURNWING LETTER.** The Paragon writes a personal letter to the chancery — not via Confessor Mauritz at Ferrostat, but via a Mournwing courier directly to the Cathedral. The letter asks one question: *"How many saints have there been?"* The letter is intercepted by Confessor Mortane and filed without answer. **The Mournwing courier who carried it has not been heard from since.** The Mournwing keep their own martyr-rolls and have added a name. | Halidan Aurriste; Confessor Mortane; the unnamed Mournwing courier |

---

#### VIII. PRESENT — PD 606

The year now unfolding. What follows is recorded in the indicative case, because it is happening.

##### Spring PD 606 — *The Cohort of the Quiet Mercy*
The annual Calling, performed at the Vocation House by twenty-four summoners under the direction of Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde (musical liturgy) and the doctrinal supervision of Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste. The cohort: **211 souls**. Translation-shock deaths in the first hour: **31** (the published figure; the true count is, per Bera Quist's parallel ledger, the same — a rare year of honest reporting). Oathed-Called: **146**. Refused: **34**. The 34 Refusers are presently routed: 19 to the Order's Auxiliary Roll, 11 to the Carcer (including **Jin of Macau, 2019** — Battle-Mage prototype, anomaly Stain-reading from arcane-signature cross-trip, cell three doors from where Hester Brunn was held), and 4 to the Inquisition.

##### Summer PD 606 — *The Carrion Census preparing at Ferrostat*
The Sixth Notary's foreclosure-detail is preparing a writ that will name the Paragon "as a clerical error to be corrected." The chancery does not know of the writ. The Mournwing know. **Confessor-Ordinary Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost** at Ferrostat has begun filing his daily aspersoir readings of the Paragon with an additional notation in *cursivus sebastinus minor* — a single Old-Tongue word, *quaero*, "I question." The notation is not in his commission. He has filed it sixteen times.

##### Autumn PD 606 — *The Octave approaching*
The Octave of the Standing falls on the twenty-third anniversary of the Paragon's miracle. The Cathedral is preparing the Octave of Triumph relic-display, which will require the Paragon's presence in Sebastopyr — his first return in **ten years**. The chancery has declined to invite him three times in those ten years; this time the invitation has been sent. **The fourth aspersoir reading of Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste is scheduled for the third day of the Octave.**

##### *In the background*

- **The murder of Confessor Thelos di Carrenost** (Cantorial Scribe, seventh seat) remains under investigation. **Inspector Nera Cazares** — Called from Earth-1947, Detective prototype — has been assigned. She has reached the clue-state "INFERRED" on the killer's identity. She does not yet know that the muster-rolls she has been working from are pre-edited.
- **Postulant Liturge di Carrenost**, the murdered Confessor's niece, has reached reading-fluency in *cursivus sebastinus minor*. The Custodes Numeri are courting her for the empty seventh seat. She does not yet know they may have killed her uncle.
- **The Brothers of the Cinder Hand** — Hester Brunn, Tomas Reyes, Skar Slag-Hand — publish *The Refusal* weekly. Four Inquisitor-Vested defectors are now contributing. The press is operated by Veriarch Thelos di Cinderost, head of the Lamplost Lamp Tenders' Compact.
- **Captain-Pyric Cassian de la Pyrille**'s anomaly aspersoir reading from the PD 605 Iron March deployment remains filed and not actioned. The Paragon's authorization for his Auxiliary Roll dead — *"Count them well"* — is the only authorization any of those deaths have.
- **The fourteen high-Stain Carcer prisoners** identified by Reader-Adjunct Korreth Slag-Tongue's private parallel readings remain in their cells. Three are politically loaded. None have been re-read by the Office.
- **Halidan Aurriste sleeps four hours a night.** The black silk glove conceals the crushed hand and the Grace-decline tremor. His Grace pool stands at 1240 units, projected by chancery medical archive to reach the minimum-operational threshold in eleven years. He has not been told the projection. He has not asked. **He has not stopped asking after earlier saints.** The Aspirant-Clerks managing his correspondence have a precise liturgical deflection formula. They use it daily.

---

#### IX. THE BELL OF THE LONG VIGIL

The Pyric Bell tolls every evening at the close of vespers, once for each soul whose last Grace was spent that day in defense of the wall. In PD 606, on a typical evening, it tolls between four and eleven times. On the night of the Standing in PD 583, it tolled four hundred and forty-seven times. On the night of Banner-Fall in PD 601, it tolled six hundred and twelve.

The bell-rope is held by a child of the Choir Ring, blindfolded by tradition so the child cannot count. **The count is kept by the Cantor's Stair scribes** — three of them, in rotation, who are themselves blindfolded as a doctrinal courtesy and rely on a Vesperine sub-cantor to confirm each toll by touch.

The blindfolded counters have, three times in the past six centuries, miscounted in the same direction (under). The miscounts are recorded in the Audit-Below, stratum 2. **One of those nights was the night of the Standing.** The true number was four hundred and fifty-one.

Four names from that night, the Cathedral never received. They sing in the deep archive in a hand no surface-cantor reads.

---

#### CLOSING NOTE FROM THE COMPILER

*This timeline has been compiled in the decreed case where the indicative case is not available, marked where the gap is wide enough to see through, and silent where the silence is itself the record. The Custodes Numeri's parallel register would tell it differently. The Caer-Druin sing it differently. The Mournwing keep their own. The Ferrenkin forge-songs hold a fourth version, in technical Old-Tongue the chancery does not recognize as Old-Tongue. The reader is invited to remember that the gap is not the failure of the record; the gap is the record. The bell rings. The count is kept. The saint endures. The lamp does not go out — yet.*

*Filed PD 606, Octave of the Held Breath.*
*Sustineo et numero.*

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:deep_history_pre_fall_and_curated_records` (deep history — pre-Fall and curated records)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* Sebastopyr is built ON, IN, and OUT OF its own pre-Fall corpse, and the city's daily life is structured by what was paved over. Specifically: (1) The Cathedral does not sit on bedrock — it sits on the inverted hull of the pre-Fall Sebast-Reliquarium, a hollow theocratic foundry from before the Fall, and what the chancery calls the Audit-Below is its inverted bell-chamber, where the saint-count is kept on tin sheets because tin does not burn the way parchment does. (2) The Pyric Wall is not one wall but seven, each built atop the slumped course of the last; Ferrenkin masons know which numbered courses are missing and have stopped saying so. (3) Three of Sebastopyr's eleven principal cisterns are pre-Fall Saemurian rain-shafts that still answer to keyed brass chimes — children in the Cinderbelow play the chimes for echoes and the Cathedral has criminalized the rhyme without explaining why. (4) The Carcer holds, in its eighth-deepest cell, a person who has not aged since 591 PD and who refuses to speak Old-Tongue except in the indicative — meaning they describe pre-Fall events not as memories but as facts. The chancery classifies them as "Aspirant-Adjacent" and feeds them through a slot. (5) Every Stain-Reader in the Inquisition is unknowingly working with a brass aspersoir whose mercury was distilled in a pre-Fall sebastic crucible that itself was hell-touched in the closing year of the Fall — meaning the instrument is calibrated to a baseline that already includes a small Stain. The cleanings come back clean because the instrument is already tilted clean. (6) The Sebastopater's throne is the keel-block of the pre-Fall ship-of-state called Aurriste's Vessel — a name the Cathedral has never officially connected to the Paragon's polished surname, because the chancery clerk who would have caught it died of a stroke in 602 PD before filing the cross-reference, and the cross-reference was never refiled, which is the closest the lore gets to luck.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The smell of the Audit-Below: cold tin and old beeswax, with a thin sweetness underneath that the Cantorial Scribes call 'archive-honey' and that is, according to one Ferrenkin smith, the smell of consecrated oak slowly losing its sanctity over three centuries.
> - A Vespertine child's skipping-rhyme heard in the Cinderbelow, criminalized in 412 PD without published reason: 'One in six hundred / nine in the deep / count for the saint who / forgot how to sleep.' Modern children sing it without the last line, which their grandmothers remove with a hand-gesture (two fingers laid over the mouth) the children imitate without knowing why.
> - The sound a brass aspersoir makes when held over a Hellfade stone: a single soft tick, like a pocket-watch being wound one notch, which Inquisitors are taught to interpret as the instrument 'settling.'
> - The hand-gesture a Cantorial Scribe makes on closing a tin sheet: thumb to first knuckle of forefinger, then a small downward push, as if pressing a seal. Used elsewhere in the city as a gesture meaning 'let it lie' in conversations about other people's debts.
> - A Vespertine curse used by archive-clerks when a cross-reference fails: 'os Carrenost' — 'in Carrenost's hand' — invoked without anyone remembering who Carrenost was. The phrase has traveled into the under-wards as a general curse for things that should add up and don't.
> - The specific incense burned in the Mort-Censorium during a case-closure ceremony: a Saemurian recipe called *fumus quietus* (the quiet smoke), made of myrrh, dried sebast-thistle, and a single hair of consecrated oak. It does not smell like any other incense in the Cathedral. Clerks who work the Mort-Censorium go home with their robes smelling faintly of it, and their families have learned not to ask.

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:recent_history_the_young_triumph` (recent history — the young triumph)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* Sebastopyr in the present moment is a city of bunting that never came down. Triumph-banners hung at the Pyric Bell twenty years ago for the First Outpost are now sun-bleached to the color of old bone, and the chancery has issued seven successive directives clarifying that they are not banners but RELICS-OF-OCCASION and may not be removed without a Prelate's seal — which means they will hang until they rot, and the seamstresses' guild that once profited from their making has become the Aurriste-cadet of Pyrille's quiet rentier income from the relic-textile monopoly. The streets are walked by three new classes of person who did not exist before the Triumph: the Reclaimers (veterans of the twenty-year push, swaggering with Mire-mud still in their boots and Grace-pensions in their pockets), the Bypassed (the wall-veterans who held for forty years before the miracle and whose careers ended the day the doctrine of eternity was rescinded — they drink in the Lamplost Ward and use the curse 'Per Halidan' with a particular bitter inflection), and the Aspirant-Clerks (the new chancery sub-order that exists to manage the theological awkwardness of a living saint, and which has metastasized in twenty years into the most powerful single bureaucratic body in Sebastopyr after the Inquisition). The Carcer holds three former Archvigils who said the wrong thing about the count of saints between PD 588 and PD 595 and have been sentenced to silent contemplation in perpetuity — their cells are visited by a single Aspirant-Clerk every quarter who brings them new vestments and takes away their notes. The Sanctuary Ring smells different than it did before the Triumph: the new triumphal incense (called LAUDS-MIXTURE-VII, blended in PD 588 to commemorate the First Outpost and burned at every Cathedral mass since) has a hint of mire-cedar in it from the reclaimed marches, and an entire generation of Pyrians under twenty cannot remember what mass smelled like before. The Mort-Censorium has been quietly enlarged twice in twenty years — not for the bastion's dead, which have decreased, but for the OUTPOST'S dead, which arrive in iron-banded crates on the Aurriste Road every eight days and are processed by a night shift that did not exist before PD 591. And in the Audit-Below, the cursivus-sebastinus-minor readers — the four remaining clerks who can parse the small running hand — have been one by one reassigned to triumphal projects (the Compilation of the First Light, the Codex of the Reclaimed Marches, the Index of Aspirant-Miracles) that keep them from the saint-count rolls. The reassignments are signed by Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste, and no one has asked why.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The smell of LAUDS-MIXTURE-VII incense in the Sanctuary Ring at dawn: frankincense, myrrh, mire-cedar, and a thread of gun-oil from the Ferrenkin foundry where the censer-bowls are blessed — twenty years old now, instantly recognizable to anyone born after PD 588 and faintly nauseating to anyone older.
> - The sound of the Aurriste Road at the third hour of night: the iron-shod wheels of the casualty-wagons coming back from the Mire March, and the soft bell at the Quietus Ward gate that the deathwatch rings ONCE per crate regardless of how many bodies are inside (because the chancery decreed in PD 593 that the bell should toll for the wagon, not the dead, to keep morale).
> - The phrase 'before the Light' — used by Reclaimers to mean before PD 587, said with a slight upward inflection of pity for anyone whose career peaked then; the Bypassed answer back with 'before the Polish,' said flat, meaning before the chancery began editing the muster-rolls.
> - The weather on the Eighth of Lauds (the anniversary of the First Outpost): always recorded as 'clear with a high wind from the marches,' even on years when it has rained — the Cantor-Magisterial's office issues the official meteorology for the Octave of Triumph regardless of sky.
> - The little gull-like bird that nests in the new triumph-banners as they rot — called the BANNER-WREN by the Common Ring, *parva sustineo* in the Cathedral's bird-rolls — and the soft chittering it makes at vespers, which has become the unofficial soundtrack of the Triumph and which the Aspirant-Clerks have begun trying to suppress because it interrupts the recorded sermons.
> - The curse 'Per Halidan, then' — said by the Bypassed when something obviously curated is announced; the 'then' is the load-bearing word, meaning 'and look how that worked out,' and saying it within earshot of an Aspirant-Clerk is a misdemeanor under the Aspirant-Protection Ordinance of PD 599.

---

## VI. Daily Life — Bread, Lamps, Laundry, and Audit

### Mundane Life and Material Culture
##### How Pyrians live, eat, work, fuck, mourn, and pay in PD 606

The daily life of Sebastopyr is what the doctrine looks like when you stop being holy about it. The bell tolls, the rent comes due, the bread goes stale by sext, the child loses a tooth, the lover lies, the funeral is paid for on the never-never, and somewhere a priest with kind eyes signs a Stain-reading he has not actually looked at. This is the texture beneath everything else — what a player sees, smells, tastes, and pays for, and what a DM puts in the foreground of any scene that is not about a wall, a ritual, or a writ. Every entry below carries at least one of the six throughline tests. The material is the doctrine, rendered as objects.

---

#### I. CURRENCY — what changes hands and what the change means

The Crown mints, the Cathedral blesses, the under-ward discounts, and demons keep their own coin. Pyrians carry three pockets and use all three in a single afternoon.

##### THE FOUR LEDGER-METALS

| Coin | Material | Worth (in bread) | Who issues | Who refuses it |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **The Crown-piece** (*solidus pyricus*) | Stamped silver, Paragon's arrow-stand glyph one side, Wall seven-course glyph the other | 12 dawn-loaves | Crown mint at Marshal Ring | No one openly; under-ward shaves the edges |
| **The Bell** (*nummus campanae*) | Bronze, hexagonal, struck with the Pyric Bell | 1 dawn-loaf, or 2 sext-loaves (the loaves halve in worth at midday by tradition) | Crown mint | Cathedral almoners give them out, do not take them back |
| **The Wafer** (*libellus gratiae*, "Grace-chit") | Stiff vellum, beeswax-sealed, Cathedral chancery sigil, perforated for filing | Not a coin proper — a receipt that you have tithed and may claim a parish service (a Stain-reading, a small ward, a death-rite) | Cathedral chancery | Refusable by demonic brokers; valid only inside the wall |
| **The Slip** (*chartula*, "the gutter-paper") | Rough lampblack-on-rag IOU, signed in either party's hand, witnessed in the third's | Whatever it says, redeemable in favor not coin | Anyone, but the Under-Ward Audit-Below registers them for a 4% bite | The Cathedral, formally; in practice the chancery clerks keep them in their desk drawers |

##### THE FIFTH CURRENCY — what the demons take

Demonic brokers do not take coin. They take what coin cannot replace: a year off a name, a sentence the bargainer will never again be able to speak, a memory of a child's face, the smell of a particular rain, a single specific minute (the one your mother died in, say — they will name it). Mother Aspine's discount bench at Lampgate accepts only these. The bench's daily tariff is chalked at the railing in cursivus sebastinus minor that almost no one can read. Asperine os Veillarde, when she walks past on her way to the Mort-Censorium, can read it; she has not told anyone what it says.

##### THE COIN-SHAVERS' GAME

Crown-pieces have been shaved at the edge for two centuries by under-ward children with files; the Crown re-stamps them every seven years and the shavers wait six and a half. A Crown-piece in the Common Ring is taken at face. A Crown-piece in the Cinderbelow is weighed.

##### THE BENCH RATE

The under-ward's exchange (the Brokerage of the First Light, run by Nera Slag-Hand the Elder from the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp tea-house) posts a daily chalkboard at the third bell:

> **PD 606, the 14th of Lauds**
> 1 Crown-piece = 11 Bells (officially 12 — the missing Bell is the Brokerage's bite)
> 1 Grace-dose, second-tier = 1 Crown-piece + 3 Bells, or 1 mortal-favor of second magnitude
> 1 small Stain-reading (private, off the chancery roll) = 9 Bells, or 1 favor owed to Old Pell the Rationer
> 1 Slip-of-the-gutter, witnessed = face value, less 4%

Old Pell himself does not handle coin. He marks the slate in beeswax and the slate is wiped at midnight, which means his entire ledger lives in his head and in the marker-stones his apprentice carries in a pouch around his neck. The boy is twelve, illiterate in Vespertine, and can recite three hundred and forty markers without missing a beat. Pell pays him in the warm end of the tea-pot and a roof.

---

#### II. FOOD — what Pyrians eat, and what eats with them

The bastion eats from the kingdom and from itself. Grain comes up the Aurriste Road from the Iron March and the Ash March; salt fish comes from the Mire holds (the ones still held); and a great deal of what Sebastopyr consumes is grown on its own rooftops, in its own under-ward damp gardens, and in the long parish pig-yards that line the inside of the Pyric Wall. The Cathedral teaches that the city feeds itself by miracle. The Crown's grain-master files quietly say the city feeds itself by 41% rooftop and gutter, 52% kingdom levy, and 7% imports the chancery will not formally name (Caer-Druin smoke-fish; Ferrenkin grub-meat from the deep galleries; salt from sources east of the watershed that the doctrine says cannot exist).

##### THE DAILY BREAD

**Dawn-loaf** (*panis lauda*) — coarse rye, weight of a clenched fist, sold from the parish bakeries between matins and prime. Costs 1 Bell. Stales by sext.

**Sext-loaf** (*panis sextae*) — same dough, half-weight, sold midday at half price. By tradition the loaf "loses its Grace at noon," which is the bakers' way of saying it goes inedible and they would rather sell it for half than throw it.

**Vesper-loaf** (*panis vesperis*) — the day's leavings, dried, broken, and sold by the basket for soup-thickening or pig-feed; 3 Bells the basket. The under-ward children scavenge the gutters at vesper-bell and resell to Cinderbelow forge-cooks at 1 Bell.

**Octave bread** (*panis octavae*) — week-end loaf with honey and cinder-ash (a flavor specific to Sebastopyr — the ash is from the Mort-Censorium, sifted, blessed, and sold by the half-pound to bakers; this means the city eats its dead, ceremonially, every Octave-day, and almost no one says this out loud). 4 Bells a loaf. Eat by family.

A working family of four eats 14-16 dawn-loaves a week, plus an Octave bread on Octave-day. A noble family pretends to eat the same and actually eats white wheat from the Crown's private mill in the Sanctuary Ring.

##### THE PROTEIN LADDER

| Tier | What | Who eats it | Throughline |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Top** | Sanctuary lamb, salt-cured Aurriste Road veal, Mire-eel in honey, white-wheat loaf | Sebastopater's table, Hierarchs, high noble houses | The Sanctuary kitchens employ 47 cooks; the chancery has approved 31; the others are paid by Confessor Mortane out of access-favors |
| **Upper** | Parish pork (the wall-pigs), salt-fish, hen, butter, soft cheese | Marshal Ring officers, mid-clergy, mercantile families | The Pyric Wall pigs are fed on Mort-Censorium ash-leavings and parish swill — a closed loop the chancery teaches as "the city's self-feeding miracle" |
| **Common** | Pig-bone broth, smoked fish, hard cheese, root mash (turnip, parsnip, the under-ward purple radish), pickled cabbage, dawn-loaf | Order Numerati on stipend, working-class families, parish folk | A working soldier of the Order is paid 9 Bells/day and eats at the Hall of the Long Vigil canteen 2 meals; the third meal is at home and is broth-and-bread |
| **Under-ward** | Sext-bread soup, fish-skin, lung-and-liver stew (*pulmentum*), Ferrenkin grub-meat (called "iron-roe" politely, "wormbread" in the gutter), gutter-mushroom, mortar-greens (cress grown in the wet seams of the lower walls) | Carcer-eligible poor, day-labor, the unsponsored Called | Bera Quist, retired Ferrenkin lay almoner-physician, runs a soup-line at the Lamplost Almoner-house — she serves 311 a day, formally; 590 a day, actually; the chancery counts the formal number |
| **Cinderbelow** | Whatever was cooked in a forge that day | Forge-folk, the Brothers of the Cinder Hand, smugglers, runaways | A forge's cooling-down hour produces a meal: bread baked in the iron-cooling stone, fish blackened on tongs, a thin beer brewed in the slag-pots. The forge-cook earns a slip of the gutter from each forger she feeds |

##### A SPECIFIC SCENE — the saint-day pie

On the feast of Saint Severa di Pyrigorne (the 23rd of Matins; she of the Reading of the Numbers, martyred PD 47), every parish bakery prepares the **pie of the seven endurances**: seven layers of root, fat, smoked fish, hard cheese, parsley, pickled cabbage, and a top crust scored with seven arrow-marks. In the Marshal Ring it is a sit-down course at officers' tables, served with thin spiced wine. In the Common Ring it is sliced in eighths and sold from a parish window at 2 Bells the slice. In the under-wards there is no fish, no cheese, often no top crust; the pie is "slashed" — the bakers cut a saint-day pie in the morning, withdraw the cheese and fish, replace them with mortar-greens and gutter-cress, score the seven marks, and sell at 1 Bell the slice to whoever can pay. The under-wards know they are eating the same pie the Marshal Ring is eating, only stripped. The Cathedral teaches this is the saint's lesson: the pie's holiness is in the scoring, not the filling. Children learn the seven-mark cutting before they learn to write their names. **Throughline 4 and 5 in a single dish.**

##### DRINK

- **Thin parish beer** (*cervisia tenuis*) — the daily drink, low alcohol, brewed in parish coppers, 1 Bell the quart. Brewed with the previous day's bread-leavings. A working man drinks 3 quarts a day; the Cathedral teaches this is moderate.
- **Wall-wine** (*vinum muri*) — soldiers' wine, harsh, watered, issued at 1 cup per shift on the Pyric Wall. Sold privately by file-leaders at 2 Bells the cup; the practice is illegal and universal.
- **The Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp** (the under-ward tea-house) — a fermented bark-tea called *crassio*, dark as boot-polish, sold by the small pot. The pot costs 3 Bells; the second pot costs 2; the third pot is on the house if you have stayed past the third bell of the night, which is when the Brokerage of the First Light begins its discount work. This is by design.
- **Spiced wine** (*vinum aromaticum*) — Sanctuary Ring drink, served warm with cloves, mace, and a single fleck of cinder-ash. The cinder-ash is the chancery's joke at its own expense. A pitcher at a noble dinner costs 4 Crown-pieces.
- **The Octave Drink** (*haustus octavae*) — at week's end, in any bar, the off-hour pour: the night's last cup, given for nothing if the patron stays to drink it in silence. The silence is the price, and silence is what the demons want, and the bar's owner does not say which demon — but every Pyric drinker over forty has heard the joke that "the Octave Drink is the cheapest bargain in the city."

##### A NOBLE BREAKFAST — House Aurriste of Carrenost, the 9th of Matins

At the table: Lady Asperine Aurriste-elder (76, family matriarch, drinks her tea bitter); her grandson Velim Halidan-Aurriste (44, the Reclamation Concession chairman); a Confessor-Ordinary in attendance against the wall (a sub-confessor named Thelos di Lampgard, on retainer, eats afterward in the pantry).

The service: white wheat *panis lauda* with cold butter and honey; a small dish of softly fried duck eggs with parsley; a single grilled Mire-eel split lengthwise and served with a vinegar of capers; spiced wine pitcher, warm, two cups; a closing dish of figs in a brandy syrup, six figs, the smallest reserved for the Confessor and refused by him in the ritual fashion (the Confessor must refuse three times; on the third refusal he eats it).

The silver: heavy, old, stamped on the back with the family glyph (the seven-arrow stand). The Confessor's seat has plain pewter. This is precisely calibrated.

The conversation: Lady Asperine asks the grandson whether the Reclamation Concession's share of the Halidan-stat salt road will be reviewed at the Octave session. He says it will not. She asks who is preventing the review. He says Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste, "your cousin." She corrects him: "Distant cousin." He concedes: "Distant cousin." She watches the Confessor against the wall. She says: "And the Cantor-Magisterial's silence — what does he take in trade for it?" The Confessor is looking at his own folded hands. The grandson does not answer. After breakfast, the Confessor will file a memorandum to Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind, who will read it in the late afternoon and decide what reaches the Sebastopater. **Throughline 4 and 6.**

##### A WORKING-CLASS EVENING — the upper Lamplost Ward

A file-leader of the Order's Tenth File (a Ferrenkin, Nera Slag-Hand the Younger, 52, mother of two grown sons) comes off the north wall at the third bell of the evening. She has been on shift since prime. Her wife (a Vespertine seamstress named Marent, 49) has been working at home on a chasuble-edge for the Reliquary Ward, the kind of liturgical embroidery a parish pays in Grace-chits not in coin.

The supper: pig-bone broth thickened with vesper-bread (purchased at 3 Bells the basket; this is the third night the basket has done duty); a small dish of pickled cabbage; a quarter-loaf saved from the morning's dawn-loaf, now stale, dipped in the broth; one cup each of thin parish beer; for the wife, a piece of the previous Octave bread saved against tonight, eaten last with butter saved against tonight.

The pay: the file-leader earns 11 Bells/day (Ferrenkin file-leaders earn 2 Bells over standard for the metallurgical knowledge they bring to the wall-plate). Two of those Bells are diverted by the Order to a Grace-reserve fund that her sons may someday draw against if they take orders. Three Bells go to rent (a single room over a tanner's shop, Lamplost Ward third street). Two Bells go to the parish tithe. Four Bells are the household's daily working capital for food, fuel, candle-stub, and the wife's needles. Marent's chasuble work, paid in Grace-chits, is saved against her sister's deathbed Stain-reading — the sister is dying of a wasting fever and the family wants a Confessor-Ordinary's reading not a parish lector's, and the difference is the chits.

The conversation: Nera does not tell Marent which towers are condemned. She has not told Marent in twenty-one years. Marent has not asked in twenty-one years. They speak of the eldest son, who took orders three years ago and is now at Ferrostat. They speak of the leaking ceiling. They do not speak of the file-leader's mother, the elder Nera Slag-Hand, who keeps the Brokerage of the First Light at the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp. The two Neras have not spoken in seventeen years. Marent has visited the elder twice in secret, each time bringing dawn-loaves wrapped in a cloth, each time being received without comment and sent back without reply. **Throughline 5 and the Cathedral/under-ward fracture rendered as a quiet supper.**

After supper, Nera sleeps four hours. Marent works the chasuble-edge by the parish candle (3 Bells the candle, lasts 9 hours, the household uses half a candle a night). The bell tolls vespers and then the Pyric Bell tolls a single mournful note for someone, somewhere, who has just spent their last Grace. Marent does not look up. She has heard that bell six thousand times in her life. Tonight it is for a baker in the lower Quietus Ward who died of a chimney-fall. She does not know this. The bell does not say.

---

#### III. CLOTHING — what Pyrians wear and what the wear says

The bastion's clothes are wool, linen, leather, and ash. Color is theological; cut is professional; cleanliness is class.

##### THE COLOR DOCTRINE

The Cathedral assigns colors to the year's offices, and most clothing-dyers in the Common Ring will not work outside the assigned palette without a parish permission. The current palette (decreed PD 604, in force):

- **White, undyed linen** — Postulants, Lectors, Vesperine confessors at parish work, Aspirant's regalia (Halidan's white linen alb under the black silk glove)
- **Black** — Confessor-Ordinary and above; Cantorial Scribes (their bone-handled scalpel-cases are black silk); the Mournwing; mourning of any standing
- **Burgundy/blood-red** — Inquisition, Office of the Pyric Audit; the readers wear burgundy stoles over black; the aspersoir-cart is burgundy
- **Indigo** — the Order's officer rank; Marshal-Vested wear indigo capes, Captain-Pyric indigo collars
- **Iron-grey** — Order Numerati (rank-and-file), wall-soldiers, the Ferrenkin (their natural skin-color matched the doctrine, which the Ferrenkin find darkly funny)
- **Lampblack-tar** — Lampwardens, parish night-watch, the lower clergy of the Almoner houses
- **Wax-yellow** — the Almoners; the soup-line servers; the parish midwives
- **Saffron** — *forbidden in the city*; worn only by the Caer-Druin singers at the dusk Watch-Cantos because the Cathedral folded their rite into liturgy and could not take their color
- **Mortar-grey with one red thread at the hem** — the Brothers of the Cinder Hand printers; a marker the Inquisition has been hunting for nine years and has not learned to recognize because the red thread is on the *inside* of the hem
- **Unmarked rough wool** — everyone else

##### THE WORKING WARDROBE

A common Pyrian working-class adult owns: 2 linen shifts (one worn, one drying), 1 wool tunic, 1 wool over-tunic for cold months, 1 leather belt (the household's most expensive single garment, 3 Crown-pieces from a Reliquary Ward leather-worker, expected to last 40 years), 1 pair of leather shoes (1 Crown-piece, expected to last 2 years), 1 woolen cloak (4 Crown-pieces, hands down through families, often three generations), 1 head-cloth or coif.

A noble's wardrobe runs to 30-50 garments and several pairs of shoes. Lady Asperine Aurriste-elder owns a velvet over-mantle that has been hers since her wedding (PD 549) and is the most-mended garment in the house. She refuses to retire it. The mending is done by a Vesperine seamstress in the Common Ring who charges 9 Bells a visit and has been to the house monthly for thirty years. The seamstress is the principal informal source of Halidan-Aurriste household intelligence in the Cinderbelow Brokerage's files, and she does not know this.

##### THE INSIGNIA OF GRACE

A blessed soldier of the Order wears a *cingulum gratiae*, a Grace-cord, around the upper arm. The cord is wax-stiffened linen, knotted by parish Confessors, and indicates the rank of Grace the soldier may draw: one knot for a Numerus (3 Grace-doses authorized per shift), two for a File-Leader (5), three for a Captain (8), four for a Marshal-Vested (12), five for a Hierarch (16). The Paragon wears no cord — his Grace is open-ended and the cord is meaningless on him.

When a soldier spends his authorized doses, parish chancery clerks come down the wall at vespers and **clip a knot**. A soldier who has clipped his last knot is allowed to leave the wall and seek a Confessor for re-blessing. A soldier whose knots cannot be replaced (because no Confessor is available, because the parish has run dry, because the Grace-reserve fund has been raided) wears the clipped cord anyway. The clipped cord is the symbol of the empty meter. The under-ward calls a man with a clipped cord a *cingulus mutus*, a silenced belt, and the slang has spread to mean any man who has run out and not been refilled — a drunkard, a mourner, a husband whose wife has died.

The Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp pours the third pot free for a man wearing a *cingulus mutus*.

---

#### IV. WORK — how Pyrians earn the day

Sebastopyr keeps about 184,000 souls inside the wall (chancery count) and at least 211,000 (Bera Quist's quiet count of the Lamplost soup-line and the under-ward parish baptisms). The Cathedral employs ~9,000 in liturgy and chancery; the Order employs ~14,000 in wall-rite and frontier; the Crown's secular bureaucracy ~3,400; the rest work in trades, parish service, the under-wards, the rooftop gardens, and the Cinderbelow.

##### TRADES AND THEIR PARISH ALLEGIANCES

| Trade | Who runs it | What they make | Throughline texture |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Censer-tenders** | Reliquary Ward, House Marent monopoly | Cleaning, refilling, and re-consecrating incense-censers for all parish services | Censer-tenders are also informal markers-keepers — every censer that goes out for cleaning leaves a slip-of-the-gutter behind, the priest's marker for the cleaning fee, and the tenders bank the markers against the priest's next favor |
| **Beeswax pourers** | House Marent de la Pyrille monopoly | Liturgical candles, Grace-chit seals, the warm-wax styli of the Cantorial Scribes | The chancery's beeswax purchases have spiked 17% in three years and the spike correlates with no recorded saint; Severa Marent is having quiet audiences with Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde about it |
| **Brimstone-shard cutters** | House Vell-os-Carrenost monopoly | Sulfur shards for wardings, demon-binding tablets, and the Vocation House rite | The house is stockpiling against "an unnamed future"; the foreman of the cutters does not know what the future is and has been told to double output for three years |
| **Iron-shot aspersoir builders** | Ferrenkin (Korreth Slag-Tongue's workshop) | The official chancery aspersoirs; Korreth also builds private ones | His private aspersoirs read 31% anomaly on Carcer prisoners; the chancery's read 99.7% clean; he keeps both ledgers |
| **Bakers** | Parish (each ward has its parish bakery, owned by the parish under Veriarch lease) | Daily bread, Octave bread, saint-day pies | Bakers know the cinder-ash truth and are sworn to silence at their parish initiation; new bakers' apprentices are told the truth at the third year |
| **Leather-workers** | Reliquary Ward; trade-bynames "the Bull-Hands" | Belts, shoe-soles, scabbards, reliquary-cases | The reliquary-case work bonds them to the Cathedral; the Inquisition's evidence-cases are made by the same hands as the heretic-broker's bargain-needle wrappers |
| **Dyers** | Common Ring's Dye Row; many small shops | The eight-color palette and forbidden saffron | A dyer who is caught with saffron is fined; one who sells it is exiled; one who teaches its mordant is racked; the practice is universal and quietly tolerated under a 3-Bells-a-month parish "blessing of the vat" bribe |
| **Lampwardens** | Lamplost and Common Ring parish | The street lamps that mark the rings; the night-watch; the parish day-book | Lampwarden Marent de la Pyrille (Lamplost Ward) chains her day-book to her wrist at sundown and does not know whom she is hiding it from; she has heard the Brothers of the Cinder Hand are reading her book through the shop's back wall, which is not true; the reader is Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste's secretary |
| **Mort-Censorium ash-sifters** | Cathedral-employed lay brothers; about 40 men | The fine ash sold to bakers; the coarse ash sold to wall-plate forges; the consecrated mid-grade used in censers | These men know who has been cremated and on which day; their ledgers are the second-most-curated in the city (after the Sealed Anomaly Ledger), and at least three have been quietly murdered since PD 591 |
| **Mournwing couriers** | Mournwing remnant, ~400 souls | All chancery mail above a certain seal; private noble correspondence; intercepted letters re-sealed | The Mournwing know whose letters they have read and which they have broken; they keep a martyr-roll the Cathedral has never seen |
| **Caer-Druin singers** | Caer-Druin remnant, ~1,100 souls | The Watch-Cantos at dusk; informal lullaby-and-dirge work in the under-wards | Their pre-Old-Tongue parallel-ledger song, sung quietly at funerals, names the suppressed paragons; no one in the chancery has ever asked them to translate |

##### THE STIPEND OF THE WRONG

When a worker is injured in parish service — a wall-soldier crippled, an Almoner exposed to the Stain in her soup-line, a beeswax pourer scalded — the parish pays a *stipendium falsi*, "the stipend of the wrong-done," which is the parish admitting in legal form that the work injured them. It is 4 Bells/day for life. The Stipend of the Wrong is the slowest-disbursing line in the parish ledger and the most-defended. The Order's veterans' caucus has fought three doctrinal battles to keep it alive. The Cathedral's actuaries calculated in PD 599 that the city carries 11,302 stipends — more than the wall's full Numerati strength. **No one in chancery has done the math on what this means.** Throughline 3.

##### THE BYPASSED PENSIONS CRISIS

Since PD 591, the chancery has been quietly closing stipend-cases by re-classifying the injuries as "non-parish-attributable" (a chimney-fall reclassified from parish-watch to private-accident; a Stain-exposure reclassified from soup-line to home-contact). The reclassifications are signed by Confessor-Ordinaries who do not visit the cases. Bera Quist has compiled, on the inside of a folded laundry-bill, a list of 487 reclassified cases since PD 600 and is waiting for someone to ask her about it. **No one in chancery has asked.** Throughline 6.

---

#### V. WORSHIP — what Pyrians do with God

The Cathedral teaches that there are 144 prescribed daily acts of worship. A diligent Pyrian performs about 30. A working Pyrian performs about 8. A Cinderbelow forge-folk performs perhaps 2, and one of those is spitting on the wall when they pass a chancery sigil.

##### THE OBSERVED LITURGY

| Time | Bell | Rite | Who actually does it |
|---|---|---|---|
| Matins (pre-dawn) | Single low note, 4 strikes | Cathedral mass, parish lay-prayer | Cathedral clergy, devout pensioners, the Caer-Druin (in their own tongue) |
| Lauds (dawn) | Three-note ascending | Wall-rite at the seven-course Pyric; the kindling of the parish lamps; the dawn-loaf blessing | The Order on shift; the parish bakers; mothers in their kitchens |
| Prime (first work-hour) | Two strikes | Beginning of the working day; the chancery's bell of opening | Everyone, by default; the under-ward marks time by it |
| Terce (mid-morning) | Single strike | Mid-watch on the wall; the parish lectors' classroom hour | Children; wall-soldiers; almoners |
| Sext (noon) | Five strikes | The Heat-of-the-Day rite; the Cathedral's noonday mass; the bread-halving | The Cathedral; the Common Ring; almost no one in the under-wards (lunch is more important) |
| None (mid-afternoon) | Three descending | The wall-rotation rite; the Reliquary Ward's afternoon service | Wall-soldiers rotating; Reliquary clergy |
| Vespers (sunset) | Long, mournful, 9 strikes | The Watch-Canto; the parish vesper-mass; the under-ward's kindling-of-the-Last-Lamp | Everyone, because the Caer-Druin are singing and the city stops to listen |
| Compline (full dark) | Single deep strike | The Cathedral's closing; the day's last prayer; the parish accounting | Devout pensioners; the chancery's night-clerks; the dying |
| The Pyric Bell | Single bronze note, irregular | The death-rite — rung whenever a soul spends their last Grace | Every Pyrian hears it 6-12 times a day and rarely knows for whom |
| The Held Breath | Silence at dawn for 73 seconds | The remembrance of the Saint Severa's reading | Universally observed; even demonic brokers will not transact across the Held Breath; the Quartermaster of Tongues has been recorded refusing a high-tier bargain offered in those 73 seconds |

##### THE WATCH-CANTO AT DUSK

Every dusk, from the Caer-Druin singers stationed at the seven gate-houses of the Pyric Wall, the Watch-Canto rises. The Cathedral folded the rite into orthodox liturgy three centuries ago; the Caer-Druin permit this; they still sing the Cantos in their own pre-Old-Tongue, which the Cathedral has cataloged as "translated harmonics" and which no one in chancery has actually translated.

The Canto is a three-voice round: a low drone, a middle line of named-endurances ("the watch was held; the lamp was lit; the count was kept; the saint endured"), and a high descant that varies night by night and is composed by the lead singer of each gate-house. The high descant is where the parallel ledger lives. On the night the Cohort of the Lost Vespers was suppressed (PD 565, the 11th of None), the descant at the Almongate sang 117 short syllables in a meter that has no liturgical name. The Cathedral did not notice. The Caer-Druin have not stopped singing the 117 syllables since. They are sung once a year, on the 11th of None, by every Caer-Druin singer in the city. Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde has been to the Almongate twice on the 11th of None and has counted. **She has not told anyone she counted.** Throughline 2 and 6.

A Pyrian working family at supper will sometimes step to the doorway when the Canto starts. The Cathedral teaches this is reverence. The under-ward teaches it is so the cooking-smoke does not blur the high descant. Both are true.

##### A CHILDREN'S GAME — the Arrow-Counter's Rhyme

Pyrian children play a clapping game called *one-arrow-stood, two-arrows-stood*, in which two players clap palms in a complicated pattern while reciting:

> One arrow stood, the saint stood too,
> Two arrows stood, the line stood through,
> Three arrows stood, the gate stood true,
> Four arrows stood, the wall stood you,
> Five arrows stood, the Pyr stood new,
> Six arrows stood, the bell rang two,
> Seven arrows stood —

And on seven the children both clap once and stop. The rhyme used to go to twelve. The Cathedral, in PD 588 (the year after the Standing), gently encouraged parish lectors to teach the seven-version "for the seven courses of the wall." The twelve-version is still known by Caer-Druin grandmothers and by Cinderbelow children who learned it from forge-cooks. The twelve-version, the Cathedral's archives note, ends:

> Twelve arrows stood, the saints stood true,
> Twelve arrows stood, the count went through.

The Cantorial Scribes' summary of the rhyme-redaction is filed under *Curatio Ludorum*, "the curation of children's play." It is one page. It is signed by a Sebastopater whose name has been redacted. Asperine os Veillarde knows whose. She has not said. **Throughline 6 in twelve claps.**

##### THE PARISH STAIN-READING

Every Pyrian, by Cathedral law, must submit to a parish Stain-reading once every two years. The reading is performed at the local parish house by a Reader-Confirmed using a small iron-shot aspersoir. It costs nothing to the parishioner; the Cathedral pays its readers from the tithe.

The reading process: the parishioner sits on a wooden stool; the Reader sets the aspersoir on a small folding table; the Reader puts a single drop of consecrated water on the parishioner's tongue and a single drop on the back of their left hand; the Reader watches the aspersoir's mercury for 90 seconds. Tick-1 (clean) is recorded with a single chancery sigil. Tick-2 is recorded as "within tolerance." Tick-3 ("anomaly") triggers a re-reading in 30 days. Tick-4 and above triggers Inquisition referral.

In practice: a Reader who is short of patience, or short of conviction, will record tick-1 for any reading that does not loudly tick-4. A Reader who is themselves carrying Stain (like Asperine Nocta, 2.4 hidden, terrified) will record tick-1 to avoid drawing attention. A Reader who is honest and overworked (like Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost, the Almongate Cluster's senior Reader) will record honestly and will, over a 20-year career, build a private commonplace book of the anomalies she has seen — Cassian de la Pyrille the Long Confessor's 1,247-name book is the most famous; there are at least nine others.

The under-ward calls a parish reading "the cup," and a man who has come back with a cup is "cupped." "She was cupped at Lamplost last Tuesday." It means clean. It means the system says so. It is said with the same intonation as "he was acquitted at trial," which is to say, half-believingly. Throughline 2.

---

#### VI. LOVE, MARRIAGE, AND THE FAMILY LEDGER

##### COURTSHIP

Pyrian courtship runs through parish channels — the Veriarch is the introducer, the parish hall the venue, the Octave-eve dance the principal occasion. A young couple's parish files include their tithe-record, their parish-reading history, their parents' standing, and a Confessor's note on suitability. Noble courtship runs through chancery channels and is conducted in writing.

The Cinderbelow does not bother with parish channels. Cinderbelow couples walk to the Brokerage of the First Light, declare themselves to Nera Slag-Hand the Elder, exchange a copper bargain-needle (the Swallow, made by the Ironcount Ferrenkin smithy) as a tally-token, and are considered married by the under-ward. The Cathedral does not recognize the rite. The Cinderbelow does not recognize the Cathedral.

##### MARRIAGE

The Cathedral marriage rite is the Vows-of-the-Three-Endurances: the couple stands before a Confessor and swears endurance against hunger (poverty), against fire (catastrophe), and against the wall (whichever of them is on shift when the wall falls). The third vow is the load-bearing one. The Cathedral teaches that the third vow is metaphorical. Wall-soldiers and their spouses know it is not.

The dowry/bride-price economy is small but real: a working family's dowry is a wool cloak (the cloak the bride has been weaving since age twelve), a copper pot, and 11 Crown-pieces, of which 9 go to the parish for the ceremony and 2 to the household. Noble dowries run to land, brimstone-shard inventory, and political marriages. Lady Asperine Veillarde's betrothal to the Paragon's deputy (a Captain-Pyric named Mauritz Halidan, distant cousin to everyone) was negotiated by Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind in PD 604 and the dowry includes a Grace-reserve of 480 doses against the Captain's frontline service.

##### DIVORCE

The Cathedral does not permit divorce. The Cathedral permits the *vita seorsum*, the "life apart" — a Confessor-blessed separation in which the marriage is held to continue spiritually while the spouses live separately. The vita seorsum requires a Confessor's note and 14 Crown-pieces. About 4% of Pyrian marriages end in vita seorsum, formally. About 17%, informally. Spouses who simply leave the city are recorded as "absent on the wall" by the parish, which is a polite fiction. The parish bell rings for them at vespers like any other death.

The Cinderbelow has no such rite. A couple unties their needle-bond at the Brokerage and the needles are remelted by the Ironcount smithy and made into new needles for new couples. The under-ward joke is that half the city's bargain-needles are old wedding-rings.

##### CHILDREN

Pyrian children are born in parish midwifery houses (Wax-yellow Almoners attend; the midwife's fee is 3 Crown-pieces or 4 Grace-chits) and named at the Naming-of-the-Seventh-Day, a parish rite at which the Confessor enters the child's name in the parish roll and assigns the child's first Stain-reading appointment (14 years out).

A working child's first eight years are play and small parish errands. From eight to fourteen, the child apprentices: parish bakery, beeswax pourer, censer-tender, leather-worker, dyer's vat-boy, lamp-tender, Mournwing courier-runner (the Mournwing take any child small enough), Ferrenkin forge-help. At fourteen, the first parish Stain-reading, and the assignment to a trade or to orders.

Cinderbelow children play in the forge-yards, learn the whistling-language (a tonal cant that the chancery cannot transcribe and has tried to ban three times), and grow up bilingual in Vespertine and the whistle. The whistle is how the under-ward signals across the noise of the forges and across the cordons the Inquisition periodically throws around the Cinderbelow. The most common warning-whistle is two short rising tones, meaning "burgundy ahead" (the Inquisition's color). It can be heard, in a busy forge-week, three or four times a day. The whistle has saved more lives than any rite.

##### A CHILD'S GAME — the Names-We-Don't-Say

A game played by Pyrian children, mostly in the under-wards and the Cinderbelow, in which the players stand in a circle and one child in the middle is "the Confessor." The Confessor closes their eyes and chants:

> Name me one we do not say,
> Name me two we do not say,
> Name me three we do not say —

And on each beat the circle of children whispers names — invented, half-heard, fragments of grandmother-talk. The Confessor must catch a name they have heard before, repeat it back, and the child who whispered it is "out" and must trade places. The game is harmless. The names that come up include: *Aurriste-of-the-Sixth-Course*, *Halloran*, *the saint of the second arrow*, *the one whose hand wrote the cipher*, *the four-and-forty*.

The Cantorial Scribes know the game. They permit it. The names children whisper are, statistically, harmless fragments. Statistically. **Asperine os Veillarde has heard a child whisper *Brigith Halloran* — the Caer-Druin singer drowned PD 312 — and asked the child where they learned it; the child said their grandmother. Asperine wrote nothing down and went home and did not sleep.** Throughline 2 and 6.

---

#### VII. DEATH AND THE FUNERAL ECONOMY

##### THE PROCESS

A Pyrian dies. The parish midwife (who serves as parish death-attendant in most wards) is called. She confirms the death, records the time, and rings the parish bell. The Pyric Bell — the great bronze in the Cathedral apse — is rung by the Cathedral once it receives the parish's notification, which can take from one hour to one day depending on the ward and the day. The Pyric Bell rings once per soul, regardless of station.

The body is washed (parish rite, 1 Crown-piece, performed by Almoners; the wash-water is poured at the threshold), shrouded (linen, parish-issue, 4 Bells), and carried to the Mort-Censorium by the household or by a parish bier-crew (3 Crown-pieces for the bier-crew if the household cannot carry).

At the Mort-Censorium, the body is logged, blessed by a Lector (4 Bells, included in the standard fee), and cremated. The chancery's cremation fee is 11 Crown-pieces flat — a working family's two-week food budget. The ash is sorted: fine, mid-grade, coarse. The mid-grade is returned to the family in a parish urn (linen-wrapped, 2 Crown-pieces for the urn). The fine ash is sold to bakers. The coarse ash is sold to wall-plate forges. The family is not informed of the secondary uses.

The family takes the urn to the Quietus Ward and either: (a) interns the urn in a parish niche (a one-time fee of 9 Crown-pieces secures a niche for 33 years, after which the niche is reused and the ash is composted into the Quietus Ward's parish gardens — a fact the parish does not advertise but does not hide); (b) carries the urn to the family's hold or holding outside the wall (rare, expensive); (c) scatters the ash from the parish wall during the Compline silence (free, the most common option, considered the holiest).

##### COST SUMMARY

| Service | Cost (Crown-pieces) | Cost (Bells) |
|---|---|---|
| Midwife confirms death | 1 | — |
| Wash | 1 | — |
| Shroud | — | 4 |
| Bier-crew (if needed) | 3 | — |
| Cremation | 11 | — |
| Urn | 2 | — |
| Niche (33 years) | 9 | — |
| **Working-class total (with niche)** | **27** | **4** |
| **Working-class total (scattered)** | **18** | **4** |

A working family's death-fund is the household's most defended savings. Most families maintain a death-jar (a sealed ceramic crock kept behind the cooking hearth) with 14-20 Crown-pieces saved against the parents' deaths. When a sudden death exhausts the jar, the family takes a slip from Old Pell the Rationer or, less often, a parish loan from the Almoners (at 4% per year, which is the only interest rate the Cathedral permits because higher rates are heretical).

##### A FUNERAL SCENE — the Quietus Ward, the 18th of Lauds

A baker dies. His name was Velim os Aurriste — common name, no relation to House Aurriste, born in the Almongate, baked in the Lamplost parish bakery for 41 years, age 64, died of a chimney-fall while inspecting his oven's flue. The Pyric Bell rang for him at vespers the night of his death. Most of the city did not register it.

His wife, Severa, 61, has been baking beside him for 39 of those 41 years. She washes the body with their daughter Marent (32, parish dyer in the Common Ring). They use a clean parish linen, water from the kitchen, and a fragment of consecrated wax shaved from the parish lamp. The wash takes two hours. They do not speak for the first hour.

The shroud is purchased from the Almoners; Severa pays in 4 Bells from the death-jar. The bier-crew is declined — Marent's husband Halidan and Velim's apprentice (a boy of 17 named Cassian) carry the body on a parish bier, which is loaned for nothing.

At the Mort-Censorium, the wait is three hours because two cohort-Translation-shock dead from the Vocation House have just come in and the censorium is processing them under priority. Severa sits on the censorium's wooden bench and watches the Lector log her husband's name in the day-book. The Lector is a young man, lampblack-tar habit, kind-faced; he says "the Father endures" and Severa says "the Father endures" and Marent says nothing.

The cremation is at the third hour after sext. Severa is not permitted to watch. The censorium's screening curtain is dyer's burgundy, and through it Severa hears the furnace's iron breath and the Lector's voice intoning the rite of the Returned Element. She has heard the rite at funerals all her life. She has never heard it from this side.

The urn comes out at vespers. The mid-grade ash inside it is white-grey and warm to the touch. Severa carries it home and sets it on the kitchen table beside the morning's last dawn-loaf, which she did not eat. The dawn-loaf has gone stale and she eats it that night, dipped in broth Marent has made, and she says to no one, "He baked this one. The yeast was his." Marent does not answer. The Pyric Bell tolls in the distance for someone else. Severa goes to bed and does not weep until the third night.

On the seventh day after the death, Severa takes the urn to the Lamplost parish wall and scatters the ash during the Compline silence. Half the parish is there. The Veriarch reads the Octave of Remembrance. A Caer-Druin singer, passing on her way home, hums the Watch-Canto descant for two bars. Severa does not know whether to thank her.

After, Severa goes back to the bakery and bakes the next morning's dawn-loaves. The bakery is hers now. She will sell it within the year. **Throughline 5 — the sacred and the seedy share the kitchen, the urn, and the loaf that fed the city the same week it ate the dead.**

---

#### VIII. LEISURE — what Pyrians do when they are not working

The Cathedral teaches that leisure is suspect. The Pyrians do it anyway. Pyrian leisure runs to: parish games, parish theater, parish-permitted music and dance, taverns at the off-hour, the Octave-eve dances, the Long Vigil Plays cycle, gambling (technically forbidden, universally tolerated), the bathhouses, the public gardens of the Common Ring, and the Caer-Druin night-singings in the under-wards.

##### THE LONG VIGIL PLAYS

A cycle of eighteen plays staged at the Cathedral's outer apse during the eighteen days leading up to the Octave of Triumph (the annual celebration of the Standing). The cycle dramatizes the six centuries of siege, the Fall, the Long Door, the silent centuries, and the Standing of the Paragon. The eighteenth play, *The Standing*, is performed on the Octave eve and is the city's principal annual entertainment. Free attendance, parish seats, noble boxes.

Of the eighteen plays, seventeen are extant. The fourteenth — *The Cohort of the Lost Vespers* — was struck from the cycle in PD 565 (the year of the suppression). The Cathedral teaches that the fourteenth play "is performed silently" between the thirteenth and fifteenth: the audience sits for the duration of an act (about 45 minutes) and watches an empty stage. The Cathedral teaches this is "the silence of the Vespers." Most Pyrians have always assumed this is some sort of liturgical austerity. **It is, in fact, an absence dressed as a presence — the play exists in the archive (cursivus sebastinus minor, three drafts, all in Velim Aurriste's hand-copies of older originals); the silence is the curation.** During the silence, the children in the audience fidget; the adults pretend to pray; and the Caer-Druin singer stationed at the cathedral's high gallery hums, very quietly, a single sustained note in pre-Old-Tongue that no one in chancery has ever asked her to translate. The note is the first syllable of *Halloran*. Throughline 6.

##### THE BATHHOUSES

Sebastopyr maintains eleven public bathhouses, parish-run, segregated by ring (Sanctuary Ring bath is private to clergy; Marshal Ring bath is shared by clergy and officers; Common Ring has three baths for the trades; under-ward has four; Cinderbelow has two). Cost: 1 Bell, includes towel-rental and one bowl of vinegar for hair-rinsing.

The bathhouses are also the city's principal informal information exchange. A trade-broker who needs to find a leather-worker meets in the Reliquary Ward bath. A parish Confessor who needs to consult informally with another meets in the Marshal Ring bath. A husband and wife who have not spoken in a week often reconcile in the family-hour at the under-ward bath.

The Inquisition has tried to place readers in the bathhouses three times since PD 580. The bathhouse-keepers, who are Almoners by Cathedral assignment but Cinderbelow Concord signatories by practical alliance, have politely defeated each attempt — once by losing the requisition, once by closing the bath for repairs the day the reader was scheduled, once by re-routing the reader to a closed bath in the Quietus Ward. The Inquisition has not tried a fourth time.

##### THE TAVERNS AT THE OFF-HOUR

The off-hour — the hour between vespers and full dark when the city's working day has ended but compline has not yet quieted the streets — is the Pyric drinking hour. Taverns range from the Common Ring's licensed parish-houses (clean, well-lit, parish-signed, serving thin beer at 1 Bell the quart) to the Cinderbelow's forge-bars (smoky, illegal, serving slag-beer at 3 Bells the pot and small forge-fish at 2 Bells).

##### A SCENE — the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp, the off-hour, the 9th of Sext

The Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp is a tea-house in the Cinderbelow, not a tavern — but its third pot is fermented and is, in practice, the most-drunk drink in the under-ward.

The room: low-ceilinged, beam-and-stone, two iron lamps (one lit, one ceremonially unlit — *the last lamp*, kept against the day the city's lamps fail). Six small tables. A bench along the back wall. The bar is a slab of slate. Behind the slate: Nera Slag-Hand the Elder, 67, Ferrenkin, missing left hand below the wrist, prosthetic of cooled forge-iron strapped to the stump, used as a counter-weight when she pours. She does not speak unless spoken to.

The patrons at the off-hour, this evening: a Mournwing courier (drinking the second pot, paying with a Bell, taking a moment between deliveries to read a sealed letter she has just broken — her hand-movements are too practiced for it to be the first time); a Pyric Wall file-soldier off his shift (drinking the third pot, his Grace-cord clipped, eyes red, will pay for the pot with a slip-of-the-gutter that Nera will redeem against the Order's Drinkings Reserve at the next Octave); an old Caer-Druin singer named Pell Halloran (no relation to the drowned Brigith — or possibly distant, the Caer-Druin have stopped tracking — drinking the first pot, humming under her breath, the Watch-Canto descant from the night of the Standing); two Cinderbelow children, eight and ten, drinking small-beer at the bench, doing the seven-claps of the Arrow-Counter's Rhyme but missing every other clap because the eight-year-old has a fever.

Old Pell the Rationer comes in at the fifth bell of the off-hour, walks past the bar, nods at Nera, sits at the back table. He does not order. Nera pours him a pot of crassio (third pot, fermented) without a word. He drinks half of it and watches the room. The Mournwing courier closes her sealed letter. The file-soldier puts his head down on his table. The children finish their game and run home. Pell pays for the pot with a slip and Nera takes it.

What has happened: the Mournwing courier was reading a Cathedral memorandum from Confessor Mortane to Sebastopater Iohanne IX containing a partial answer to the Paragon's PD 605 question. She broke the seal at the off-hour to read it in safe space. She will reseal it at her shop in the Marshal Ring and deliver it to the chancery at compline; the seal will pass inspection because the Mournwing have known how to break and reset Cathedral seals for 314 years. Nera saw what the courier was reading; she will tell no one. Old Pell saw what Nera saw; he will tell no one. The Cathedral will receive the memorandum at compline. The Sebastopater will not read it; Mortane will. **The Constantine throughline rendered as an evening pour.** Throughline 6.

##### THE OCTAVE-EVE DANCES

Every Octave-eve (the last day of each week), parish halls hold dances. Live music: a parish piper, a small drum, a hurdy-gurdy played by whoever in the parish can play one (most parishes have one player; some, none). The dances are circle-dances and line-dances, partner-rotation built into the figures. Courtship happens here. So does the parish's informal politics. A working couple's engagement is announced from the dance-floor at the half-hour; a Confessor may attend in the second hour; a parish quarrel is resolved by the Veriarch in the back room while the dance continues.

Noble dances are held in the Sanctuary Ring's family halls and are stiffer, more formal, less interesting.
