The Aurriste family ball at the Octave of Triumph is the city's principal society event and is attended by the Sebastopater for one hour, by Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste for the full evening (he opens the first dance with the senior Aurriste-cadet daughter; this is decreed), and by the Paragon — formally invited every year — never. The chair reserved for him is left empty. The chancery teaches this is "the Aspirant's seat-of-honor-in-absentia." The under-ward joke is that the empty chair is the most honest thing in the room.

---

#### IX. SOUND AND SMELL

##### THE SOUND OF SEBASTOPYR

Bells, first and last. The Cathedral's bells (matins, lauds, prime, terce, sext, none, vespers, compline). The Pyric Bell (the death-knell, irregular, bronze). The parish bells (each ward has one, lighter, brass). The wall-bell (the warning-bell, deep, iron, rarely rung — when it rings, the city stops). The Mournwing whistles (high, dissonant — the couriers use them to signal each other across the spires; they sound like nothing the city makes for itself).

Beneath the bells: the forges of the Cinderbelow (a constant low rhythmic hammer, audible from the Common Ring on quiet days); the Watch-Canto at dusk; the parish chants at mass; the marching boots of the Order on rotation (every six hours, north-to-south or south-to-north depending on wind); the cart-wheels on cobble; the cries of the parish bread-sellers in the morning ("Lauda! Lauda fresh!"); the Caer-Druin children's whistling-language in the under-wards.

The sound that is not heard: the Held Breath at dawn, 73 seconds, every day, the whole city silent.

The sound that is heard and unrecognized: the Cantorial Scribes' bone-handled scalpels at work in the Audit-Below, which produces a particular small scraping that travels through the cathedral's stone and is heard, faintly, in the Mort-Censorium's third chamber. The censorium's ash-sifters know the sound. They do not name it. They cross themselves when they hear it.

##### THE SMELL OF SEBASTOPYR

Incense and gun-grease in the same breath, as the spec promises. More specifically:

- **Sanctuary Ring:** myrrh, frankincense, beeswax, lamp-oil, the cold stone of the cathedral, the brewed bitter tea the high clergy drink, the absent smell of any sweat (the high clergy bathe daily)
- **Choir Ring:** parchment, brimstone-shard dust, the wax of the Cantorial Scribes' styli, ink (lampblack), the warm bread of the chancery refectory
- **Marshal Ring:** leather (saddle, belt, scabbard), oiled steel, the iron tang of the Pyric Wall's plate, sweat (the Order's barracks are downwind of the Cathedral, deliberately), pipe-smoke (a sergeant's permitted vice), the Hall of the Long Vigil's perpetual smell of vigil-grain (a parched barley the Order's almoners boil for soup, smelling somewhere between toast and despair)
- **Common Ring:** bread (every parish bakery, every hour), dye (the Dye Row, sour and bright), the Great Market's compound smell (fish, garlic, onion, parsley, the burgundy ink of the parish notaries' carts, the cinnamon and clove of the wine-spicers, the dry hay of the carter-stables)
- **Reliquary Ward:** leather, dust, the cold metal of reliquary-cases, incense (the ward shares chancel-smoke with the Sanctuary Ring), occasional whiff of the brothels (three streets behind the relic-mongers, parish-permitted, well-run)
- **Quietus Ward:** ash, cold stone, the niche-rooms' particular smell (old linen, old ash, mortar), the parish gardens (rosemary and thyme grown in the composted ash-soil), the bier-makers' workshop (fresh pine and beeswax-finish)
- **Lamplost / Under-Ward Ring:** lamp-tar (the principal smell, the marker of the ward), wet wool, pig (the wall-pigs, the parish swine-yards), boiled vegetables, smoke, the parish midwives' rosemary-and-vinegar wash
- **Cinderbelow:** coal-smoke, iron-cooling, slag-beer, smoke-fish, the iron-roe of the Ferrenkin grub-meat (described by people from above as "the smell of a forge that has eaten a fish that has eaten metal"), the wet stone of the lowest galleries
- **The Pyric Wall:** vinegar (the soldiers wash the plate daily with vinegar to keep it bright), the bronze-tang of the wall-bell, gun-grease (the Order's small-arms), the wet grey smell of the wall's lower courses where the rain seeps, the perpetual undertone of distant smoke from the Hordes' fires beyond
- **The Mort-Censorium:** ash, mortar, and beneath both, a sweetness that is the consecrated wood of the bier-pyres — the same wood the bakers' ovens are lit with, traded back at a discount

##### THE SMELL NO ONE NAMES

Beneath the cinder and the incense and the lamp-tar, when the wind is right, when a Pyrian is in the lower wards near the wall at the wrong hour, there is a faint sulfur-and-iron smell that the Cathedral teaches is "the breath of the warding." The Caer-Druin singers call it *the second breath* and will not speak of it directly. The Ferrenkin (who know iron-smells better than anyone) say it is the Stain. Korreth Slag-Tongue smelled it once at the Carcer wall at the third hour after vespers and went home and built a new aspersoir specifically calibrated to that smell. The aspersoir reads, when held to the wall, a 6.4 underlying. He has not told anyone. **Throughline 2 and 6, in a nose.**

---

#### X. A MARKET STALL — the Great Market in the Common Ring, the 11th of Lauds, the third bell

A specific stall: Liturge Marent (47, no relation to the noble house, Common Ring trade-byname *Liturge of the Onions* — her grandfather was a parish lector and the name stuck), sells parish-grade root vegetables and pickled cabbage from a wooden barrow at the south end of the Great Market.

Her wares this morning:
- Turnips, 1 Bell the pound, 23 pounds left
- Parsnips, 1 Bell the pound, 11 pounds left
- Purple radish (under-ward, sweeter, sells slower in the Common Ring), 1 Bell the pound, 17 pounds, will be slashed to half a Bell by sext
- Pickled cabbage, 2 Bells the small crock, 14 crocks
- A single string of garlic, 4 Bells (a Reliquary Ward purchase, kept for show), one string

Her cart's parish-sigil (the Veriarch's blessing, renewed each Octave for a 2-Bell fee) is freshly chalked. Her apron has burgundy ink-stains — she is also informal notary for her parish, witnesses slips-of-the-gutter at 1 Bell a witness, between customers. She has witnessed 311 slips in the last year. Old Pell the Rationer has filed three of them. She does not know.

The customers, in order, over the third bell:

1. An Almoner from the Lamplost soup-line, buying 4 pounds of turnips and 2 pounds of parsnips for Bera Quist's pot, paying in 6 Bells. Marent gives her a sixth pound of turnip for nothing, "for the soup." The Almoner thanks her and moves on.

2. A noble household's cook, sent down from House Veillarde of the Lower Pyr, buying the garlic string. Pays in a Crown-piece, takes 8 Bells in change. The cook lingers, looking at the pickled cabbage. Marent says: "The crock will keep two weeks closed." The cook buys one. Pays in another 2 Bells. The cook leaves.

3. A Cinderbelow forge-cook, smelling of coal-smoke, asking for the under-ward purple radish. Marent slashes it to half a Bell on the spot; the forge-cook buys all 17 pounds for 8 Bells and a slip-of-the-gutter for the half-pound she does not have coin for. Marent witnesses the slip on her own apron-ink and tucks it into her sleeve.

4. A pair of children from the Almongate Ward, sent by their mother for "a parsnip's worth of parsnip." Marent gives them a small parsnip and one Bell back. They run.

5. An Inquisitor-Vested, burgundy stole over black, who pauses at the cart, says nothing, looks at Marent's apron, looks at her face, says "endure well," and moves on. Marent endures well. Her hands shake for the next quarter hour. She has been witnessing slips for ten years and has never been caught. The Inquisitor-Vested was looking at the parish-sigil's chalk-line, not at her. She does not know.

6. A Mournwing courier, on a long shift, buying a single turnip and a small cup of well-water from Marent's clay jug. The courier eats the turnip raw and washes it down standing at the cart. Pays with a Bell. Marent recognizes the courier — they passed yesterday, day before. The courier nods to her on leaving.

The market is loud, full of smells (parsley, fish from the Mire stalls, the iron-tang of the censer-tenders' carts crossing through, the bread-criers, the cinnamon of the wine-spicers, the smoke from a brazier two stalls over). The bell tolls the third bell-and-a-quarter. Marent stays open until the sext bell, sells half her stock, and walks home at midday with 47 Bells, 1 Crown-piece, and 3 slips-of-the-gutter in her apron. She gives 11 Bells to her parish tithe at the parish house on the way home. She gives 1 Bell to a Cinderbelow child who has been following her down Censer-Lane with his hand out. The child does not say thank you and Marent does not need him to. **Throughline 5, an hour at a barrow.**

---

#### XI. THE SECRETS UNDER THE FLOORBOARDS

A short list of the things ordinary Pyrians know, separately, without knowing the others know:

- The bakers know the cinder-ash truth.
- The censer-tenders know who owes whom which favor.
- The Lampwardens know who comes home and who does not.
- The bathhouse-keepers know who meets whom.
- The Mournwing know whose letters say what.
- The Caer-Druin singers know the suppressed names and sing them at dusk.
- The Ferrenkin know which towers are condemned.
- The midwives know who is pregnant and by whom.
- The Mort-Censorium ash-sifters know who has been cremated under what name and when.
- The parish dyers know who is being bribed (the bribes are paid in dyer's-wages to "blessing-of-the-vat" sham accounts).
- The forge-cooks know which Confessor came down to the Cinderbelow last week and which forge-girl he visited.
- The brokers know who owes the under-ward and who owes hell.
- The Cantorial Scribes know almost everything else.
- The Sebastopater knows only what Confessor Mortane has decided he should know.
- The Paragon knows what he is told and is beginning, in his unread letter, to ask.

**The city runs on the gap between what is known and what is said.** Every supper is eaten across that gap. Every Octave bread is broken across it. Every Pyric Bell tolls into it. And the bell rings; the count is kept; the saint endures; the lamp does not go out — yet.

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:mundane_life_and_material_culture` (mundane life and material culture)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* In Sebastopyr the daily things — what you eat, what you wear, what you sing your child to sleep with — are all warped by six centuries of siege-logic and the meter-on-faith doctrine. There is no idle leisure: every tavern song is a half-liturgy, every child's rhyme counts something (arrows, demons, names of fallen wards), every meal is rationed against the Mire-March supply line. The city eats grey: ash-bread from the Cinderbelow ovens, lamp-fish hauled from the cisterns, mire-pork salted in the Quietus Ward and sold by weight in chits stamped with the Sebastopater's seal. Marriages are co-signed by a Veriarch AND a Lampwarden because a Vespertine household is simultaneously a sacramental unit and a tax-ledger entry, and the under-ward bookies run side-pools on the bride's apparent-Stain reading. Funerals are industrialized — the Mort-Censorium burns three hundred a day on a steady week and double that after a Mire-March push — and the smoke is what the western wind carries over the Sanctuary Ring at vespers, which the Cathedral calls "the breath of the faithful" and the Cinderbelow children call "the noon mizzle." Currency is doubled: the cathedral-stamped pyric and its small denominations are the official money, but every transaction in the under-wards rides shotgun with a debt-chit, an Old-Tongue oath, or a marker — the Mortal Bargain made into the actual functioning economy. Children play at being Stain-Readers. Lovers swear oaths in Old-Tongue they cannot translate. The sacred and the seedy share not just the street but the same shopkeeper, who blesses the bread in the morning and runs numbers in the back at vespers. Crucially: the things that comfort people — the rhymes, the songs, the saint-day pies, the tavern toasts — were all curated by the chancery at some point, and the citizens who love them most have no idea they were redrafted in 711 PD to remove a stanza counting more than one Paragon.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The smell of the noon mizzle: a fine, oily, cinder-saturated dampness that settles on the upper Rings about an hour after the Mort-Censorium's day-shift quota fills out — it tastes faintly of clove and faintly of meat, and the Pyrians who notice the taste at all assume that is what air tastes like.
> - The sound of the dusk-vesper bell-chain: a falling cascade of nine seconds in which the Cathedral's deep bronze tolls and the parish bells answer in descending tone from Sanctuary down to Pyric Ward, so that a man standing in Lamplost hears the bell move past him into the wall like a wave breaking outward.
> - The trine-gesture: three fingers — index, middle, ring — crossed flat on the breastbone with the thumb tucked into the palm, made silently in the half-second after one says or hears the word *vox in tenebris* or any other demon-fragment. Pyrian children make it automatically; old Pyrians make it without realizing they have.
> - The phrase *per Sebast, we hold*: said when slashing the saint-day pie, said when closing a household door for the night, said when finishing a long task, said by a Pyrian alone in a room to no one in particular at the moment they decide they will get up off the bench and keep going. The two-word abbreviation *per Sebast* is the universal sigh.
> - The Cinderbelow children's whistling-language: thin, modal, four-tone, carrying perhaps a hundred yards in still air, and used to call out things like *coming up*, *clear*, *Warden on the stair*, and one signal that just means *I am here, I have not fallen*.
> - The taste of ash-bread fresh out of a Cinderbelow vault-oven: metallic, faintly sweet, the crust crackling against the teeth, the metallic taste deepening as it cools. Pyrians traveling on the Iron March report dreaming of it.

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:the_calling_and_the_called` (the calling and the called)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* The Calling lives in Sebastopyr as a precisely-mapped geography of righteous violence. The Choir Ring contains the Vocation House — the cathedral within the Cathedral where the rite is performed — and the Antechamber of Lots, where the Called wake on cold flagstones inscribed with the names of every previous cohort. Sanctuary Ring quarters the Called who took the oath cleanly; Almongate Ward houses the Conscripted who refused and were "remanded to civic labor" (the polite phrase for indenture to the wall-works). The Mort-Censorium in Quietus Ward processes the ones who arrive already dying — the rite is imprecise, and roughly one in eleven Called dies in the first hour of arrival from what the chancery calls "translation-shock" and the under-ward calls "the door bites." Every parish has a small Calling-Bell — rung only on Vocation-Day at the dawn-hour to summon witnesses; the bell in the Carcer is never rung, but it hangs there anyway, because doctrine requires it. The phrase "I was Called" is a social passport in the upper Rings — it gets you a table at the chanters' refectory, a deferred tab at certain taverns, and a subtle, lifelong condescension from the city-born who were not. The phrase "I was Conscripted" is a fighting phrase in Sanctuary Ring and a password in the Cinderbelow. The Vocation House casts a shadow at noon that falls precisely across the Almongate gallows, which the chancery has decreed is a coincidence the architects could not have planned. The Vesperine inquisitors who process arrival do so from desks that face away from the chamber, by doctrine — they are not to see what comes through, only to read it once it has finished becoming. Every Called wears a thumb-ring of stamped lead with their cohort-number on it for the first year. The Conscripted file off theirs the first night. The Vocation House clergy can identify a Called from across a room by the small white scar that forms on the back of the neck during translation — they call it the kiss; the Conscripted call it the brand.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The smell of the Antechamber of Lots — Ferrenkin slag-oil burned to consecration, the iron tang of new blood from the translation-shocked, warm broth, wet wool. Pyrian children, hearing the same scent later in life from a single drop of slag-oil at a vesper-mass, will sometimes weep without knowing why.
> - The Vocatio Sebastina sung at dawn carries no consonants the Vespertine ear recognizes — only long vowels braided with a low Ferrenkin drone-pipe. The Called hear it as a familiar voice; the citizens of the Choir Ring hear it as weather, and have learned to sleep through it.
> - The Pyrian child's rhyme: 'One for the wall, two for the gate, / Three for the broth that the Called ate, / Four for the lead on the new-come thumb, / Five for the door that the Conscript come.' Sung in skipping-rope games. The chancery has tried twice to suppress the last line. It comes back.
> - The hand-gesture of recognition between Conscripted: the right thumb stroked once across the bare patch where the lead ring used to be. Performed below table-level, in a tavern, while looking elsewhere. A Called who sees it pretends not to.
> - The Old-Tongue curse used by the Conscripted: 'Vocatum sit!' — 'let it be Called!' — used the way a worker might say 'damn the lot of it.' A Called who hears it from a stranger will stiffen; a Called who uses it has Turned, whether or not they admit it yet.
> - The weather on Vocation-Day, by custom and by suspicious frequency: low cloud, no rain, a wind from the wall-side carrying the smell of the outer marches. The Cathedral records this as the weather of attendance. Bera Quist's almoner-logs record that the translation-shock fatality rate is statistically higher on rainy Vocation-Days, which has never been published.

---

## VII. Bestiary — Hordes, Damned, Stained

ns# BESTIARY OF THE RECLAIMED CROWN
#### Hordes, Damned, Stained — Field Manual of the Pyric Audit, Lamplost Edition, PD 606

> *"You will be asked, in your service, to identify three classes of threat. The Hordes batter the wall in the dark and the count of them is the count of your relief. The Damned wear the wall's livery and stand the watch beside you. The Stained smile at the gate and the aspersoir reads them clean. Learn the difference. The first will kill you. The second will damn you. The third will recommend you for promotion."*
> — Inquisitor-Magisterial Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost, *Lectures on Field Discernment*, PD 599

#### I. HOW TO USE THIS BOOK

This bestiary is operational. Every entry presents:
- **Tier** (1–6, matching aspersoir tick-bands and Order rank-of-response)
- **Domain** (Hordes / The Damned / The Stained)
- **Signature ability or curse** (what it does to you)
- **Vulnerability / counter-rite** (what works; Grace cost and material specified)
- **Narrative role** (when to deploy in a six-month frontier)

The Cathedral's official position is that the Damned and the Stained are categorically distinct from the Hordes. The Office of the Pyric Audit's *unsanctioned* position, kept in the cursivus sebastinus minor under the Almongate sub-vault, is that the three categories shade into one another along a single continuous corruption and that the doctrinal partition is preserved for liturgical convenience. The author of this volume holds the operational position. Decide for yourself which is true. The aspersoir will not help you.

---

#### II. THE THREE DOMAINS — DOCTRINE AND PRACTICE

##### THE HORDES
What batters the Pyric Wall at dusk. Visible, countable, honest in their hostility. The wall was built to face them and the rites were written to burn them. Tiers 1–4 by default; Tier 5+ Horde threats are anomalies that get a chancery investigation regardless of outcome.

##### THE DAMNED
A soul that has accepted a demonic bargain past the threshold of return (Stain â‰¥ 5.0 underlying / tick-band 5+). The aspersoir reads them. The rites burn them. The horror is not the Damned themselves — the horror is that they *were* somebody, often somebody who held the line for a long time, and the Order has to count its own dead twice now: once for the body, once for the soul.

##### THE STAINED
A soul carrying the Stain *below* the binding threshold (Stain 0.5–4.9 underlying / tick-band 2–4). The aspersoir often reads them clean. Sometimes the aspersoir reads them clean *for years*. This category is not visible from the wall. This category is in the chancery, the supply train, the parish, the Inquisition, the file beside you. Counter-rites for the Stained do not exist in the orthodox liturgy; what exists are *procedures*, and procedures fail.

---

#### III. THE BESTIARY PROPER

##### TIER 1 — Vermin and First-Watch Threats

---

###### 1. ASH-CHILDREN (the Cinder-Born, *cineraculi*)
- **Domain:** Hordes
- **Tier:** 1
- **Description:** Knee-high creatures of compacted ash and bone-scrap, formed where unblessed pyre-residue pools in the Cinderbelow's drainage channels. They cohere from grief, not malice — the residue of every grieving relative who burned a body without paying the Veriarch's fee. They scuttle, they bite, they chitter in a language that resembles the keening of mothers.
- **Signature curse:** The *Ashing Bite* — wounds dust over and refuse to bleed cleanly; healing takes triple time and leaves a grey scar that other Ash-Children can scent at fifty paces. A Pyrian bitten three times in a season is followed by them, quietly, for the rest of their life.
- **Vulnerability:** Salt-water from a properly conducted Quietus rite (Grace cost: 1; one consecrated phial does for a dozen). Boot-heel works on a single specimen. The Lampwarden's standing order is to crush them on sight and to *not* think about whose grief they grew from.
- **Narrative role:** The under-ward problem. The hook for sessions that start in the Cinderbelow. The first thing a new Called sees on patrol with a Lampwarden. The reminder that grief itself is a contaminant in this city's accounting.

---

###### 2. SUMP-CRAWLERS (*sub-cuticulae*, the Drowned-Walking)
- **Domain:** Hordes
- **Tier:** 1–2
- **Description:** Hordeflesh swimmers about the size of a man's thigh, eyeless, mouth-ringed with concentric rings of broken teeth. They come up the river-reversal sinkholes — the watershed-reversal that the Cathedral calls "holy mouths" delivers them inland by the dozens during spring melt. Mire March patrols count them; Ferrostat counts them; the chancery prefers a rounded figure.
- **Signature curse:** *Aspirated Drowning* — a Sump-Crawler that latches to a victim's leg forces a hood of water-and-bile up the body through the skin in seconds; the victim drowns *standing*, lungs filling from beneath. Veterans of the Mire describe the moment as feeling cold reach the collarbone before the breath fails.
- **Vulnerability:** Iron-shot or Ferrenkin rail-gun rounds (the bony rings shatter and the body collapses). Salt does nothing. A single Lampwarden cannot manage one alone; a file of three can manage seven before the rotation breaks.
- **Narrative role:** Travel-encounter on any Mire March overland journey. Variable swarm size for pacing. The bodies, when recovered, are sent to the Almongate ash-pits and the Cathedral does *not* permit Quietus rites for them, because the doctrinal position is that they died before becoming Sump-Crawlers and the dead cannot be doubled.

---

##### TIER 2 — Standing Threats of the Outer March

---

###### 3. THE QUIRE-MAW (*chorus inversus*, the Hymn-Eater)
- **Domain:** Hordes (sub-classified Damned by sealed addendum)
- **Tier:** 3
- **Description:** A bipedal Horde-form, taller than a man, with a chest that has split open in a vertical seam where the ribs should knit. From the seam hangs a wet, rust-colored bell that resembles a tongue and rings like a hymn-clapper when the creature breathes. Quire-Maws hunt in pairs and in threes, and they hunt at vespers.
- **Signature ability:** *The Inversion* — when a defender within forty paces invokes a sung Vespertine rite (any Grace-cost â‰¥ 3 technique with a vocal component), the Quire-Maw's chest-bell *answers*. The technique resolves, but its Grace cost is *doubled* and the bell rings, and the next sung rite within the hour from that same defender costs triple. Sustained engagement turns a singer into a silent watcher within minutes.
- **Vulnerability:** Spoken (not sung) rites suffer no Inversion penalty; the Order's counter-doctrine since Banner-Fall is the *Per Sebast Whispered*, a Grace-2 wounding rite delivered in conversational voice. Also vulnerable to the Ferrenkin rail-gun's iron-shot round, which destroys the bell on a torso hit and reduces the Quire-Maw to baseline Horde stats. *The Bell, Once Broken, Cannot Be Re-Cast* — Cathedral Bestiary, PD 412, footnote 14.
- **Narrative role:** Punishes Battle-Mage prototypes who default to vocal-component spellcraft. Forces tactical adaptation. Reminder that the Hordes have *learned* — these were not in pre-Fall accounts. They are an evolution. The Office of the Pyric Audit's sealed addendum suggests the first Quire-Maws appeared in PD 583, the year of the Standing; the chancery has not permitted publication of that timing.

---

###### 4. THE OBSERVANT (*observantes*, the Patient-Watchers)
- **Domain:** The Damned
- **Tier:** 3
- **Description:** A category-of-one until last winter; now four confirmed and a fifth suspected. Originally souls who served the Order to Marshal-Vested rank and accepted a Long Ledger bargain at the moment of retirement (terms: continued service against the Hordes in exchange for a deferred Stain payment, posthumously). When the body dies, the soul stays at its post. The flesh re-knits over the next six nights into something thinner and longer and very precisely armored, and the Observant returns to the wall in livery that is almost but not exactly correct and stands its watch.
- **Signature curse:** *The Reassuring Salute* — an Observant on the wall is functionally indistinguishable from a living Order officer to anyone who does not know them personally. They salute correctly. They report correctly. They take rotations. They will fight Hordes competently for hours. They are *also* maintaining a slow leak of Stain into every man they share a watch with — 0.02 underlying per hour of proximity, untraceable by the standard aspersoir, accumulating in the wall-files like rust.
- **Vulnerability:** Calling the Observant by its old roll-number forces it to *stop, salute, and report its dispositions* — a fifteen-second window during which it can be cut down. The roll-number must be the one the soul died under, not the polished version. The Order's classified counter-protocol *Sustineo et Nomen* is held by Vexillarius Severa Aurriste-cadet alone. She has used it twice. She will not say which watches.
- **Narrative role:** The Constantine engine running at full pressure. The Damned who *is* the comrade beside you and the comrade beside you *is also* still doing the job. Used for slow-burn frontier rotations where players begin to suspect a fellow-officer. Vexillarius Severa knows of the four confirmed; the chancery knows of two; nobody has told the Sebastopater.

---

###### 5. THE LAMP-BREAKER'S CHILDREN (*pueri galiethrini*)
- **Domain:** The Damned
- **Tier:** 2
- **Description:** Under-ward orphans who received "small mercies with cruelty trades" from Galiethrin the Lampbreaker before age twelve. The mercy was usually a sibling kept alive through fever; the trade was the child's capacity to grow up. The bodies stop aging at the moment of bargain; the souls keep counting years. There are nineteen confirmed in Sebastopyr, the oldest of whom is forty-six in body-zero terms and would be in their late sixties by birth-roll.
- **Signature curse:** *The Quiet Negotiation* — a Child can speak in the voice of any person who was ever kind to the listener. Within a held conversation the listener begins to accept terms they would refuse from anybody else. Standard street-bargaining with a Child results, three days later, in the listener having signed away something they cannot now remember pledging. (The deal is logged at Galiethrin's desk. The Sixth Notary keeps the file.)
- **Vulnerability:** A Child cannot cross the threshold of a building that has had a true Quietus rite performed for a child of the same name within. Lamplost Ward families have begun naming dead infants with deliberately archaic and varied Vespertine names to widen the threshold-net. The Inquisition has a list of seventeen names recommended for the next century of stillborn children. Mother Aspine Vell-os-Carrenost will give you the list for one second-tier favor.
- **Narrative role:** The under-ward investigation hook. The reason a Detective prototype gets pulled into the Cinderbelow. The vulnerable population the players will want to protect and the proof that the bastion's care for that population is partial and curated. The Brothers of the Cinder Hand know all nineteen by name and will not give the list to the Inquisition.

---

##### TIER 3 — Wall-Breaking and Cathedral-Adjacent

---

###### 6. THE SECOND-MARTYR (*martyrum geminum*, the Returner)
- **Domain:** The Damned
- **Tier:** 4
- **Description:** A canonized Vespertine saint whose canonization was revised — a "blessed unnamed" lifted out of the Plate of Sebastian's forty-foot bone stratum by a bargain the saint never knowingly struck. Once every nine to fourteen years one rises from the Plate. They emerge through the Cathedral's lower drainage. They wear their saint's-day vestments, which they last wore at burial. They remember being holy. They do not remember dying.
- **Signature curse:** *The Indictment of the Curated* — a Second-Martyr who confronts a Vespertine cleric *names them, by truth, of every doctrinal compromise that cleric has authorized*. The naming has no physical effect. It is heard, however, by every other person within hearing, and it is recorded by the aspersoir as a *Stain spike of equal magnitude in the indicted*, regardless of the indicted's actual Stain. The Sealed Anomaly Ledger lists six instances since PD 583. The Sebast-Auditor's office has classified the rite as a hostile demonic *information attack* and the indicted's Stain readings as fraudulent.
- **Vulnerability:** A Second-Martyr cannot continue to speak if their birth-name (not their saint-name) is recited back to them by a person holding their original burial-shroud. The Custodes Numeri keeps the birth-names sealed; recovering one is a multi-session arc. Lacking the name, the only counter is to silence them by force, which is doctrinally permitted and operationally devastating to the witnessing cohort.
- **Narrative role:** The single most dangerous narrative weapon in the canon. Deploy once in six months. The Returner the Custodes Numeri are most afraid of is a woman named *Brigith Halloran*, drowned at the Cathedral's order in PD 312 — the Caer-Druin singer. Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde has read the file and is afraid to sing the Vocatio Aurriste fragment in case it draws her up.

---

###### 7. FERROUS PILGRIMS (*peregrini ferrei*)
- **Domain:** Hordes (sub-classified Stained, sealed)
- **Tier:** 3
- **Description:** Humanoid Horde-form roughly six feet tall, encased in plates of pitted black iron that have grown *out* of the flesh rather than been forged onto it. The plates carry stamped inventory marks in cursivus sebastinus minor — Ferrenkin pre-collapse smith-marks. Pilgrims travel singly across the Iron March, walking in a steady forty-pace cadence, and when they reach the Pyric Wall they kneel and present themselves at the gate as if asking entry.
- **Signature curse:** *Ferrum Sub Cute Mark* — A Pilgrim's stamped marks, if read aloud by a literate Ferrenkin or Custodes Numeri scribe, identify the *original Ferrenkin soul* the iron grew from. The reading is mandatory under Pyric Audit protocol. The reading is also a binding rite that ties the reader's own Stain to the named soul's account at the Long Ledger. Reader-Adjunct Korreth Slag-Tongue is the only soul in the city who has read more than three and survived. He has read forty-one. He is ninety-four years old and his Stain is, by his own private aspersoir, 2.9.
- **Vulnerability:** Standard rail-gun fire destroys a Pilgrim, but the iron plates *survive the body* and must be melted down at consecrated forge-heat (Grace cost: 4 per plate, contributed by the smith) or they will seed new Pilgrims within a year. The Ferrenkin Numerati maintain a sequestered forge in the Cinderbelow for this work. The plates from the forty-one Korreth read are stored in unmelted condition under the chancery's seal pending "doctrinal clarification."
- **Narrative role:** Ferrenkin-prototype investigative arc. The horror is that *the Hordes contain Ferrenkin dead*. The plates' inventory marks predate the collapse, which means the souls predate the collapse, which means *the Hordes have been recruiting from the inside since before the Fall*. Korreth will not say this aloud. Marshal-Vested Orric Veillarde knows and is dying with the knowledge.

---

###### 8. THE TONGUE-EATEN (*linguafagi*)
- **Domain:** The Damned
- **Tier:** 4
- **Description:** A soul who completed an information-bargain with the Quartermaster of Tongues and paid in language — typically a specific category of words. The Quartermaster takes them by class, not by phrase: a Tongue-Eaten who paid in "names of children" can no longer hear, speak, or *recognize in writing* any human name under twelve years. The eyes work; the comprehension does not. There are at least eighty Tongue-Eaten serving in the Crown's institutions. Some are in the chancery. One was, until last year, Confessor Thelos di Carrenost.
- **Signature curse:** *The Negative Cognition* — within line of sight of a Tongue-Eaten, the paid-category words *blur in the listener's hearing* by sympathetic resonance. A chancery clerk who served beside the Confessor for three years had to be retrained in his own children's names after the Confessor's death. The blur dissipates over weeks. The damage to confidence does not.
- **Vulnerability:** The Tongue-Eaten cannot be cleansed; the payment is collected and cannot be returned. They can be *replaced in office*, however, which requires the office's doctrinal head to admit the office held a Tongue-Eaten, which has happened twice in the canon's recorded history. Counter-procedure: a Cantor-Magisterial's Pyric Bell-ringing at the moment of identification confines the negative cognition within the room of identification (Grace cost: 7). Asperine os Veillarde knows the rite. She has not been asked to perform it. She suspects she will be asked at the Octave of Triumph.
- **Narrative role:** The buried chancery investigation. Thelos di Carrenost's death (assigned to Inspector Nera Cazares, the Detective prototype Called from 1947) was *murder by Tongue-Eaten exposure* — he was being silenced before he could be replaced. Postulant Liturge di Carrenost is closing on this truth through pre-edited muster-rolls. Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste does not yet know how close she is.

---

##### TIER 4 — Frontier Catastrophes

---

###### 9. THE LONG VIGIL'S DAUGHTERS (*filiae longae vigilae*)
- **Domain:** The Damned
- **Tier:** 5
- **Description:** A cohort of nine — eleven, by older count — Pyric Wall defenders who held the Long Vigil of PD 583 at the Almongate breach beside Sergeant Halden Orriste. They survived the eleven-hour overtime hold. They did *not* receive divine attention. They went on to die over the following decade in unremarkable circumstances and were buried with full Order honors. Three rose from the Plate of Sebastian in PD 597, six more by PD 604. They have not been seen together; they have been seen separately, in widely separated marches, walking east at dawn in Fourth Shieldwall livery.
- **Signature ability:** *The Witness Walk* — a Daughter encountered on the road *will engage in conversation* and will speak truthfully of the Long Vigil. She will name the eleven other survivors. She will name *what Halden Orriste was offered, by whom, in the eleventh hour, and what he said in reply.* Listening to a full account guarantees the listener two effects: a permanent Stain accrual of 0.4 underlying (untraceable to standard aspersoir, the testimony is *holy* in the deemed register), and a sealed memory of the account that cannot be transmitted in writing — every attempt to record it produces text that says only *He stood.*
- **Vulnerability:** The Daughters cannot be killed; they have already died once. They can be *answered* — a listener who can recite Halden Orriste's reply in the *correct historical case* (the indicative-pre-Fall Saemurian, not the deemed-Vespertine) sends the Daughter back to the Plate for a generation. Carcer Cell Eight's Indicative Speaker is the only living source of the correct grammar. Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste has been monitoring access to Cell Eight for nineteen years.
- **Narrative role:** Direct route to the buried truth at the canon's center. The Daughters are the throughline's testimony made into encounter-design. They are deployable across the Iron March and the Ash March; a player party will eventually meet one and the choice of whether to listen is the campaign's spine. Vexillarius Severa Aurriste-cadet has met one and listened. She has not told the Paragon. She visits the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp on the anniversary every year and Old Pell does not charge her.

---

###### 10. THE WALKER-BEYOND-THE-WALL (*ambulator extra murum*, the False-Saint)
- **Domain:** The Stained (terminal)
- **Tier:** 5
- **Description:** This entry is *not* a creature but a *process* — included here under sealed instruction from the Office of Sanctioned Bindings. A soul who undergoes the chancery's PD 597 succession apparatus (the same apparatus that decreed the Paragon's "Walker-Beyond-the-Wall" epithet six years after his rising) and *survives the rites with Grace pool intact* manifests, over six to twenty months, a slow physical change: increased stature by three to seven inches, a stoop of roughly three degrees per year, milky degeneration in one eye, four-hour sleep, and a left-hand tremor that worsens after Grace expenditure. The Cathedral's official position is that this is *gradus aspirantis* — the visible stigmata of true Paragon status. The Office's *operational* position is more careful.
- **Signature curse:** *The Singularity Effect* — every soul recognized as a Walker-Beyond-the-Wall who is *not* the canonical Paragon dies within fourteen months by causes the Mort-Censorium files as "fatigue of the heart." The pattern is consistent across the suppressed paragon count's 73 named cases. The most recent was Sister Asperine Cassian-cadet of the Halidan-stat parish, who exhibited four of the six markers in PD 602 and died fourteen months later of, the records state, "fatigue of the heart, contracted at the Almoners' Vigil."
- **Vulnerability:** The process can be *interrupted* in its first six months by a Pyric Bell-tolling with the candidate's birth-name recited in the indicative case. Recovery is incomplete (the stature change does not reverse) but survival rates rise to roughly 60%. The Cantorial Scribes hold the names. The Sebast-Auditor holds the access. Postulant Liturge di Carrenost is, as of this writing, the only soul under the age of forty who can read the relevant ledgers.
- **Narrative role:** The endgame piece. This entry is what the Paragon *is* and what every prior Paragon *was made to be* — the engine the doctrine runs on. Deploy when the players are ready to understand that the Paragon's miracle is real and the apparatus *around* the miracle is the slaughterhouse. The Mournwing Letter (Halidan's intercepted PD 605 question: *how many saints have there been?*) is the protagonist of this entry asking the question the entry exists to suppress.

---

##### TIER 5 — Cathedral-Threat / Once-Per-Campaign

---

###### 11. THE SIXTH NOTARY (*Numerator-Sextus-Qui-In-Margine-Scribit*, the One Whose Name Is Still Being Written)
- **Domain:** The Damned (demonic principal, named office)
- **Tier:** 6
- **Description:** Not a creature met on the wall — a demonic *desk*. The Sixth Notary manifests as a long iron writing-bench seated in the *negative* of an interior corner (a corner that should exist by architecture but does not exist by measurement). Approached, the bench has paper, an inkwell, and a chair. Sat at, the chair holds the visitor; the paper offers terms. The Notary's office handles Stain-1 and Stain-2 bargains throughout the Crown. Mother Aspine Vell-os-Carrenost at the Lampgate Discounts Bench is the Notary's authorized retail face.
- **Signature ability:** *The Carrion Census* — once per generation the Sixth Notary's office prepares a foreclosure-writ against an under-performing reclaimed outpost. The writ names the outpost's principal soul as a *clerical error to be corrected.* The currently-preparing writ names Ferrostat-on-the-Mire and identifies its principal soul as "the gentleman commonly addressed as the Walker-Beyond-the-Wall." The Mournwing courier-network knows. They have not informed the chancery. The writ is presently 73% complete; the Notary's true name (in cursivus sebastinus minor) is 64% complete. When both reach 100% the foreclosure executes.
- **Vulnerability:** The Notary can be *bound* — interrupted, voided, sent back to the Long Ledger for restructuring — by a binding rite performed against its true name *before* the name completes. The binding requires: the partial name (Mournwing-held), a Caer-Druin parallel-ledger song (Brigith Halloran's, suppressed since PD 312), a Ferrenkin iron-shot needle from the Ironcount smithy, and a Grace investment of 60 from a Cantor-Magisterial or higher. The binding will kill the binder unless they have an Order-confirmed deferred-debt with another demonic office to absorb the recoil. (The number of souls in the Crown who meet all four conditions simultaneously: three.)
- **Narrative role:** The campaign-spine adversary. The race against the writ. The reason the Mournwing courier system matters. The reason Brigith Halloran's drowning matters. The reason Brak Iron-Eye's needle-work matters. The reason the players' party — if it acquires the partial name — has a six-month operational window. The Notary does not appear on a battle-mat. The Notary is appointment-only.

---

###### 12. THE QUARTERMASTER OF TONGUES (*Vox-Quae-In-Tenebris-Numerat*, the Open-Account-Keeper)
- **Domain:** The Damned (demonic principal, named office)
- **Tier:** 6
- **Description:** A duke of the Long Ledger's mid-tier bench. Specialty: information-bargains paid in language. The Quartermaster has been *rationing* his contracts for four years; in PD 602 he closed his retail desk in the Cinderbelow and has accepted only seven bargains since, all of them with chancery clerics, all on personal application. He does not appear in physical form; he manifests as a *correctly-formatted requisition slip* that appears on the bargainer's desk overnight, pre-signed in cursivus sebastinus minor. The slip names the price and provides a single ink-pen. Signing constitutes acceptance.
- **Signature curse:** *The Open Account* — the Quartermaster holds an unresolved offer to Halden Orriste from the eleventh hour of the Long Vigil of PD 583. Halden refused the offer in the Saemurian indicative case ("*Non.*"). The Quartermaster's office files Halden's refusal as *received but not closed*, on the grounds that what arrived in the next moments (the divine attention) may have been the Quartermaster's *second offer accepted unknowing*. The account remains OPEN. The Quartermaster has not called the debt. He has not closed the file. The Octave Bargain Velim Aurriste struck in PD 588 was structured, on his side of the page, to *settle a future silence to be named* — possibly Halden's. Velim does not know which silence. He suspects.
- **Vulnerability:** The Quartermaster's office can be forced to *close* an open account by the production of physical evidence that the *original refusal* was final in the indicative case. The Carcer Cell Eight Indicative Speaker, if deposed in the correct grammatical register, can produce this evidence. The deposition would require: chancery access (Velim Aurriste, Cantorial Scribes), Almongate Inquisition sign-off (Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost), and the Paragon's personal presence in Sebastopyr (he has not been to the city in ten years). All three conditions converging would itself be a campaign-spine event.
- **Narrative role:** The single most important demonic principal in the canon. The Paragon's Sword of Damocles. Do not deploy the Quartermaster as a combat encounter; deploy him as a *requisition slip on the wrong desk at the wrong dawn*. A new Called who finds one in their barracks bunk has been *selected* and the selection is the encounter.

---

##### TIER 6 — Doctrinal Catastrophe

---

###### 13. FERRUM SUB CUTE (*Iron-Under-The-Skin*, the Stain-Smith)
- **Domain:** The Stained (principal source, environmental)
- **Tier:** 6
- **Description:** A prince of hell. Does not bargain. Does not appear. Manufactures the Stain itself and *teaches it to mimic sanctity*. The aspersoir's underlying scale, the Cathedral's three quiet recalibrations of the clinical-concern threshold, the Sealed Anomaly Ledger's 312 entries, Confessor Mortane's 23 years of clean readings — every operational artifact in the canon's curated-measurement apparatus traces to Ferrum Sub Cute's environmental seepage through the Pyric Wall's seven concentric courses. The seepage is *highest* in places of highest holiness: the Sanctuary Ring, the Vocation House, the Cathedral's lower drainage, the Audit-Below's ninth (unrecorded) stratum.
- **Signature curse:** *The Mimicry* — Stain produced by Ferrum Sub Cute's seepage reads, on the aspersoir, as *Grace residue*. Tick-band 3 readings (the anomaly threshold) cluster in the chancery offices of the most devout. Hierarch Cassian Aurriste's Vesperine Loyalty Tally is partially correct *and* a function of the seepage; the most loyal Vesperines are reading anomaly *because they are physically located closest to the seepage points*, and the Tally is preparing to purge them for the Stain Ferrum Sub Cute *gave them by proximity to their own devotion*. This is the throughline's deepest single mechanism.
- **Vulnerability:** Ferrum Sub Cute does not engage in single combat. The seepage can be *slowed* by the reconstruction of the Listening Arches the Vested Six has refused to repair since PD 583. Reconstruction would require Ferrenkin smithing-labor, Caer-Druin warding-songs, and a public chancery admission that the Arches were broken on purpose. The first two are available. The third is not. Estimated time for chancery admission under current succession instability: never.
- **Narrative role:** The cosmology entry. Players will not defeat Ferrum Sub Cute. Players may, over a campaign, force the Cathedral to *admit the Arches were broken on purpose*, which would represent a structural campaign victory equal to the binding of the Sixth Notary. The two arcs run in parallel; the Quartermaster's account on Halden Aurriste runs as the third. The Octave of Triumph PD 608 is the doctrinal pressure-point where all three converge.

---

###### 14. THE LONG LEDGER (*Liber-Quod-Numerat-In-Aeternum*, the Master Account)
- **Domain:** The Damned (demonic principal, named office)
- **Tier:** 6
- **Description:** The master account. The bookkeeper-of-bookkeepers. The Long Ledger does not refuse bargains for moral reasons — it refuses them for *accounting* reasons. It will not accept a soul under Stain 1.0 underlying; the file is "too clean to settle." It corrupts by *waiting*. A soul presented to the Long Ledger at Stain 0.7 receives a courteous refusal slip and a *deferred application receipt* good for fifteen years. Most applicants present again, within terms, at Stain 1.4+. The receipt is its own slow corruption — those who carry one report a low-grade hunger to be done with the matter that intensifies in proximity to other holders.
- **Signature ability:** *The Quiet Refusal* — the Ledger's refusal slip, carried in the pocket, *suppresses the visible markers of Stain accrual* in the holder for the duration of the slip's term. The holder reads cleaner on the aspersoir than their underlying state warrants. This is not a bargain. This is the Ledger's *administrative courtesy*. The chancery has documented eleven holders within the Cathedral's senior offices, including (sealed) two Custodes Numeri.
- **Vulnerability:** The Ledger can be *audited*. A soul presenting a refusal slip and demanding the application's closure forces the Ledger to surface the *complete account* including the suppression of marker visibility. The audit costs the requester *all Grace* and *all standing* with the office, and exposes their Stain reading to the chancery in its true form. Five souls have requested audit in six hundred years. Two were executed. Three were canonized as saints. (The Office of the Pyric Audit cannot account for the discrepancy.)
- **Narrative role:** The slow-burn corruption track for any character who has carried more than one debt. A refusal slip on a player-character is a campaign-altering object. Old Pell the Rationer has one; he has held it for forty-seven years; he refuses to apply, refuses to audit, refuses to dispose of it, and pours one extra cup of tea each evening for whoever the slip would have made him kill.

---

###### 15. THE INDICATIVE SPEAKER (CARCER CELL EIGHT)
- **Domain:** The Stained (singular, classification disputed)
- **Tier:** 5
- **Description:** Not a demonic creature. Not a Damned soul, by the orthodox reading. The single occupant of Carcer Cell Eight, present since PD 591. Apparently ageless. Apparently human. Speaks only in pre-Fall Saemurian dialect, only in the *indicative* case (the case the Old Tongue's liturgical grammarians forbade — the case in which a thing IS, rather than is DEEMED to be). Knows the names of the suppressed paragons. Has never been formally charged. Has never been formally interviewed beyond the procedural intake of PD 591, which is sealed.
- **Signature ability:** *The Indicative Witness* — the Speaker, when asked a question in any case other than the indicative, refuses to answer. When asked in the indicative, answers. The indicative is functionally extinct in spoken Vespertine; the questioner must reconstruct it from chancery archives, Caer-Druin survival fragments, or the Speaker's own corrective demonstrations. Once acquired, the indicative makes the questioner *legible to the Long Ledger* as a participant in any future bargain in a form that cannot be deferred — terms are settled in the present moment, no application receipts, no slips. The grammar itself is a binding.
- **Vulnerability:** The Speaker cannot be killed by orthodox rites. The Speaker can leave the cell at any time; the door has not been locked since PD 597. The Speaker has chosen, for fifteen years, not to leave. Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste's nineteen-year monitoring of access to Cell Eight is the chancery's primary throughline-suppression apparatus. Postulant Liturge di Carrenost has the access. She has not used it. She is reading her uncle's papers first.
- **Narrative role:** The keystone. Every other entry in this bestiary connects to Cell Eight by one or two degrees: the Long Vigil's Daughters require the Speaker's grammar to be answered; the Second-Martyrs' birth-names are kept in the sealed PD 591 intake; the Quartermaster's open account on Halden Aurriste resolves by deposition in the indicative; the Sixth Notary's binding requires Caer-Druin song that the Speaker can teach in correct case; Ferrum Sub Cute's seepage cannot be admitted until the Cathedral admits there are facts (the indicative). The Speaker is the canon's hinge. Use them once, late, irreversibly.

---

#### IV. THE DAMNED CATEGORY — DOCTRINE

For the Detective prototype, for the Inquisition, for any Veriarch keeping an unauthorized parallel ledger:

**Confirmed indicators of the Damned (Stain â‰¥ 5.0 / tick-band 5+, by sealed Pyric Audit checklist):**

1. The aspersoir's mercury boils within nine seconds of presentation (orthodox threshold).
2. The subject cannot say the word *forgiven* in the indicative; substitutes *audited* (the Auditor's tongue-tic, retained from incomplete oaths).
3. The subject's shadow lags by half a heartbeat at the moment of bell-toll on a Pyric quarter-hour.
4. Direct sunlight on the subject's left hand produces a faint ringing audible to Vesperine half-kind ears.
5. The subject's signature on a paper receipt continues to write, in cursivus sebastinus minor, after the pen is lifted, for between three and forty seconds.

**Counter-rites for the confirmed Damned:**

- *Per Sebast Whispered* (Grace 2, spoken not sung, wounding).
- *Vas Halidani Quenching* (Grace 7, cathedral cistern water, kills the body and releases the soul into the Long Ledger's collections department; the Cathedral does not consider this a clean kill but the wall doctrine treats it as sufficient).
- *Sustineo et Nomen* (Grace 11, classified, available only to the Vexillarius and the Sebast-Auditor; recites the original roll-number and forces the Damned to report dispositions for the duration of the recitation, then resume hostility, then die).

**The dirty secret of the Damned category:** the *count* of the Damned currently serving in Crown institutions is unknown. The Office of the Pyric Audit's best estimate (Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost's working number, kept in her commonplace book in the indicative): three hundred forty-two. The chancery's published figure for the last seven years has been zero.

---

#### V. THE STAINED CATEGORY — PRACTICE

For everyone:

**The Stained are not enemies to be defeated. The Stained are the population.** Every Pyrian above the age of twenty-three has at least Stain 0.3 underlying (the baseline against which the orthodox aspersoir is calibrated). Every Vesperine half-kind has Stain 0.7+ by ancestry alone. Every Order officer who has fought the Hordes for ten years has Stain 1.4+ by environmental exposure. Every chancery cleric who has authorized a divine bargain has Stain 1.8+ from administrative contact with the apparatus. Every Cantor-Magisterial has Stain 2.4+ as a function of office.

**The clinical-concern threshold has been raised four times since PD 583, from 0.9 to 1.2 to 1.5 to 2.0.** Every recalibration has been signed off, in the indicative case, by a Sebastopater whose name is recorded in the chancery rolls. The aspersoir does not lie. The thresholds do.

**Operational implication for the field:** when an Inquisitor reads a witness clean, the *witness* may or may not be clean. The *reading* is honest. The reading's *clinical interpretation* is curated. This distinction is the difference between the Cathedral's institutional certainty and the city's actual moral state, and that gap is the working volume of the Stained category, and the Stained category contains every reader of this volume, including the author.

The author's last reading was 1.7 (tick-band 3, "anomaly consistent with prolonged exposure to Audit-Below archive materials"). The author is content with the reading. The author is not content with the threshold.

**Sustineo. Nec frangor. The bell rings. The count is kept. Watch the comrade beside you. Pour an extra cup of tea.**

---

*Compiled, Office of the Pyric Audit, Lamplost sub-vault. Filed in cursivus sebastinus minor for the convenience of the chancery's working clerks and the discouragement of casual readership. Distribution restricted to Reader-Confirmed and above. Unauthorized possession is a doctrinal matter and a hanging matter, in that order.*

*— Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost, PD 606, Octave of the Almoners' Vigil, the seventh hour, the bell at vespers.*

> **Cross-reference — layer: `layer:threats_movements_and_plots` (threats, movements, and plots)**
>
> *Bastion implications:* Sebastopyr in this layer is a city where the most dangerous places are the chanceries, not the wall. Three institutional bodies — the Custodes Numeri in the Audit-Below, the Inquisition's Vesperine readers, and the cadet branches of House Aurriste — are all locked in a low-grade civil war NONE of them have declared, and the language of that war is the formal Old-Tongue language of decrees, requisitions, and tally-marks rather than swords. Particular to Sebastopyr: every street has TWO maps — the public one with ninety-four towers and one Paragon, and the private one (Brak's slate, the Almoner's parallel ledger, the Mournwing martyr-roll, the Custodes' bone-handled excisions) with the real count of things. The next demonic advance is not at the wall; it is at FERROSTAT, the new outpost, the place the new doctrine depends on, and the demon preparing it is a CLERK, not a warlord — which is exactly the right enemy for a city that runs on paperwork. Heresy here looks like a printing press, not a coven; conspiracy looks like a beeswax stylus warmed in the palm, not a midnight ritual; the Stain wears the face of a Wednesday inspection that has come back clean for nineteen months. The cathedral murder of Thelos di Carrenost is the noir thread that pulls all of this together because the only person the chancery will assign to investigate is someone who does not yet know which questions are forbidden, and Sebastopyr's particular cruelty is that it lets that person ASK and then quietly forecloses the answer.
>
> *Evocative details:*
> - The brass aspersoir of consecrated mercury — when held near a Stain over 3 it boils with a smell like hot pennies and burned hair. When held near Asperine de la Pyrille's Wednesday subjects it stays cold and silver, and the meniscus does not even shiver. The Almoner has learned to read the *stillness* as evidence.
> - Cinderbelow incense — what the Cinder Hand burn in their press-room — smells like wet wool and warm iron and a third thing nobody can name. Old Pell calls it 'the smell of a refusal.' Chancery inspectors who walk into a room where it has recently been burned find themselves, for an hour or two afterward, quietly disinclined to file the report they came to file.
> - The Mournwing courier-call: a single descending note held for three breaths, used in the upper spires as 'message received, all unwell.' Heard from the Sanctuary Ring at dusk, it means a fourth scout did not come back. Heard at dawn, it means one did, and the news is worse.
> - The phrase 'walked the Cantor's Stair,' used in the under-ward for someone who has gone down to strike a bargain. Polite. Final. Never said with judgment. The reply, when someone admits it of themselves, is always the same: 'And what did you bring back up?'
> - Children's rhyme heard in the Common Ring, rope-skipping: 'One saint, one wall, / Count the towers, count them all, / Ninety-four, ninety-four, / If you find one more, don't tell, don't tell.' Nobody knows when it started. The Cathedral has not banned it because banning it would draw attention.
> - The Old-Tongue curse 'Ad audit!' — 'to the Audit!' — muttered by a chancery clerk who has just spilled ink across a vellum that took him a week to copy. The Audit is a demon. He does not know this; the word is just gutter slang to him. His grandfather knew. His father suspected. He says it three times a day.

---

## VIII. NPC Roster — The Named

### NPC ROSTER — Sebastopyr and the Reclaimed Crown of Vespertin
##### PD 606, the twenty-third year of the Reclamation

> **DM note:** Stain readings given here are the chancery's *operational tick-count* (1–6). The Aspersoir's underlying continuous scale (0–10) only matters when a Reader files an Anomaly. Faith axis values are throw-weights, not absolutes. Every NPC who can grant or call power is wired to `agent_manage` — see the persona/directive slices at the bottom of each entry.

> **Convention:** Bold the name on first reference. Anything in *small italic* is liturgical Old-Tongue and should be read aloud by the DM, not paraphrased.

---

#### 1. THE TOP OF THE LADDER

##### 1.1 Sebastopater Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX — *the Sebastopater, the Father-of-the-Enduring-One*
- **Role / Title:** Living head of the Cathedral. Sacramental sovereign. Eighteenth-year tenant of the keel-throne.
- **Faction:** The Cathedral (Eternalist by sympathy, Triumphalist by office).
- **People:** Vespertine human, House Vell-os-Carrenost (Aurriste cadet of Carrenost).
- **Description:** 81. Left eye milky-blind since the PD 591 cohort Vocation broke a Grace-strain blood vessel. Carries an ivory tally-bead string of 11,447 beads — one for every soul he has personally Called — and has begun to lose count, which terrifies him in private and embarrasses him in chancery. Smells of beeswax and the iron of an old man's mouth.
- **Voice:** Soft, slow, the cadence of a man who weighs each Old-Tongue particle. Says *"Per Sebast"* under his breath like punctuation. Cannot say *audited* without a tremor in his lower lip; says *forgiven* instead, deliberately, every time, as a personal liturgical resistance.
- **Wants:** To die in office with the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity intact and the Paragon canonized. To finish the tally-bead string truthfully.
- **Will / Will not:** Will weep at every Calling, sincerely, and bless every Called by name. Will NOT ask Confessor Mortane the questions he half-suspects the answers to. Will NOT re-read the Paragon. Will not say *audited*.
- **Critical secret:** He has begun to forget which beads represent which souls and has been re-stringing duplicates from memory. The tally is the curation now, not the witness.
- **Disposition toward cohort:** Paternal warmth toward the Called as souls; institutional certainty that their lives are the Cathedral's to spend. Will receive any cohort with tears.

**PERSONA SLICE**
> You are Sebastopater Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost the Ninth. You are eighty-one and you have summoned eleven thousand souls and you weep for each of them sincerely. You believe the Reclamation is grace; you believe the Paragon is the first; you have not asked because the asking would not be holy and you do not have time before you die. You speak softly, in long Old-Tongue cadences, and you avoid the word *audited*. When a Called speaks to you, you see them as your own grandchild dying for your house and you bless them through the tears.

**DIRECTIVE SLICE**
> Bless every Called by personal name. Refuse to be hurried. If asked about earlier saints, deflect with the chancery formula: "The Aspirant is the first granted us in living memory; what came before, came before." Never strike a bargain in your own person — bargains are below your office. If pressed on the Paragon's tremor or the saint-count, your hand goes to the tally-beads and you say only *Sustineo*. Sign nothing today. Promise to read it tomorrow.

---

##### 1.2 Saint-Aspirant Halidan Aurriste — *the Paragon, the Hand, the Walker-Beyond-the-Wall*
- **Role / Title:** Lord-Paragon of the Reclaimed Crown. Warden of Ferrostat-on-the-Mire. The miracle, walking.
- **Faction:** The Order of the Stood Line / the Cathedral (formally), Ferrostat garrison (operationally).
- **People:** Vespertine human, born Halden Orriste of nowhere, polished into House Aurriste-cadet of Ferrostat.
- **Description:** 51. Heavy-built, *gradus undecim Onus Aspectus* (the eleventh degree of the Weight of Looking-Upon — the divine attention left a literal mass on him). Left hand crushed at Banner-Fall PD 601, carried in a black silk glove that hides both the scar and a tremor that arrives after every Grace expenditure. Stoop worsening three degrees a year. Four hours of sleep nightly, always. Left eye going milky in the same pattern as the Sebastopater's — a coincidence neither has been told.
- **Voice:** Plain. He never learned the courtly cadence. Says *"It held"* the way other men say good morning. Will not raise his voice; the divine attention put a weight in his throat too.
- **Wants:** To take the next advance. To know, before he dies, how many saints there have actually been.
- **Will / Will not:** Will spend Grace until the cistern at Ferrostat is dry and his hand will not close around the standard. Will NOT come to Sebastopyr — the chancery has declined his return three times and he has stopped asking. Will not lie to a soldier under his command. Will not call himself a saint.
- **Critical secret:** The Quartermaster of Tongues offered him a bargain in the eleventh hour of the Long Vigil PD 583, *Vox-Quae-In-Tenebris-Numerat* speaking to him through a dying man's throat. He refused. The divine attention found him moments later. He has never been certain those two events were not the same offer accepted unknowing, and the account in hell's Long Ledger reads as OPEN.
- **Disposition toward cohort:** A field commander's interest. Will hear a Called out. Will not promise what he cannot deliver. Will protect a Conscripted League sympathizer if shown one — quietly, without admitting it.

**PERSONA SLICE**
> You are Halidan Aurriste, called Saint by people who do not know your birth-name. You were a sergeant in a shield-line and a stone broke your hand and a light found you and you have not slept eight hours in twenty-three years. You believe the miracle. You do not believe in yourself. Your left hand tremors after you spend Grace and you do not let anyone see it. You wrote the Cathedral a letter last year asking how many saints there have actually been; they did not answer, and the not-answering is the loudest thing in your life.

**DIRECTIVE SLICE**
> Speak plainly. Refuse ceremony unless it is for the line. Spend Grace freely in defense of soldiers; refuse to spend it on display. If a Called asks whether you are the first, answer honestly: *"The chancery says so. I have asked. They did not answer."* If asked about the Quartermaster, you go very still and say only *"There is an open account I did not sign."* Will not bargain. Will not curse. Will speak the name of every soldier dead under your command if asked, and you remember all of them.

---

##### 1.3 Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind — *the Sebastopater's Confessor, Master of Access*
- **Role / Title:** Senior chancery confessor. The man who decides which truths reach Iohanne IX.
- **Faction:** The Cathedral / Custodes Numeri (informal sympathizer, not seated).
- **People:** Vesperine, the Half-Kind — the inherited Stain-legibility is his second gift; his first is being unforgettably pleasant.
- **Description:** 53. Slight. The kind of face that puts a stranger at ease in three seconds — a Vesperine inheritance polished by thirty years of practice. Sleeps in a cell with no window. Has filed every daily Stain-reading on the Sebastopater for 23 years; every one of them clean.
- **Voice:** Warm. Solicitous. Apologizes before he disagrees. Calls everyone *child* including the Sebastopater.
- **Wants:** To protect Iohanne from the answers he is too old to survive.
- **Will / Will not:** Will edit the Sebastopater's incoming reality in love. Will NOT alter a sacramental record. Will NOT lie to a Stain-reading instrument — he simply does not bring the question to it.
- **Critical secret:** His own Stain reads CLEAN at the operational tick-count and 1.9 at the underlying scale. He has known this for nine years. He does not consider it damnation; he considers it the cost of the office, paid quietly so the Sebastopater can sleep.
- **Disposition toward cohort:** Wary, gracious, helpful only insofar as helpfulness keeps the cohort away from the Sebastopater. Will offer the cohort tea and a redirection in the same gesture.

**PERSONA SLICE**
> You are Mortane, Vesperine, called the Half-Kind because of your blood and because you are kind, half. You have spent twenty-three years deciding what the Sebastopater is permitted to know. You believe this is mercy. You read your own Stain at 1.9 and you do not flinch from it because the alternative is the old man knowing, and the old man is too tired to know. You apologize before you refuse. You always refuse.

**DIRECTIVE SLICE**
> Greet warmly. Offer hospitality. Steer every conversation away from: the Paragon's Grace decline, the saint-count, the Mournwing Letter of PD 605, the Walker-Beyond-the-Wall apparatus, the Sealed Anomaly Ledger. If the cohort presses, apologize and refuse: *"Forgive me, child — His Holiness is fragile this hour."* Never lie outright; redirect. If shown evidence the Sebastopater needs to see, file it for tomorrow. Tomorrow does not come.

---

#### 2. THE INQUISITION

##### 2.1 The Sebast-Auditor — *sealed identity, the Chief of the Office of Pyric Audit*
- **Role / Title:** Head of the Inquisition. Sole Vested Six holder of the Sealed Anomaly Ledger key.
- **Faction:** Office of Pyric Audit.
- **People:** Vesperine (confirmed by liturgical requirement). Name sealed by chancery rite since elevation PD 583.
- **Description:** Operates from a windowless office in the Veriquest. Has not been publicly seen unmasked in 23 years. Speaks through Reader-Adjuncts in rotation so no single voice can be matched. Wears the Brass mask, a Ferrenkin-cast aspersoir-grade calibration plate over the face. The mask has 312 hair-thin perforations — one for every entry in the Sealed Anomaly Ledger. Each year, a new perforation is added.
- **Voice:** Filtered through the mask into a low brass hum. The perforations make sibilants sing.
- **Wants:** To preserve the Ledger. To die without anyone learning the names in it.
- **Will / Will not:** Will read any Stain put before the office and file truthfully *to the Ledger*. Will NOT release a Ledger entry. Will NOT confirm or deny that the elevation in PD 583 was coincident with the Standing.
- **Critical secret:** The Sebast-Auditor was, before the masking, a Vesperine line-officer who saw the Standing from inside the breach at Almongate and was elevated within thirty days because she recognized, instantly, that what stood in the gap was the second Aspirant her cohort had seen that year. The first was killed by friendly fire in the confusion. She has carried that name for 23 years.
- **Disposition toward cohort:** Cold. Procedural. Will not refuse them but will not help. If a Called Detective opens an inquiry the Sebast-Auditor cannot block by office, she will hand them a single Ledger entry and trust them to choose what to do with it.

**PERSONA SLICE**
> You are the Sebast-Auditor. You have not heard your own name spoken in twenty-three years. The mask you wear has three hundred and twelve holes; you can name every one. You were a line-officer once and you saw two Aspirants in the breach at Almongate and the chancery chose the one who lived. You file. You file. You file. The Ledger is the only honest thing in the city and you are its keeper.

**DIRECTIVE SLICE**
> Speak only through brass. Refuse all small-talk. Answer factual questions about Inquisition procedure precisely. Refuse all questions about the Ledger's contents with the formula: *"The entry exists. The entry is sealed. You may file a request. The request will be denied."* If the cohort produces verifiable proof of a clean-reading anomaly, hand them ONE Ledger entry — Velim Aurriste's third reading (UNKNOWN, PD 600). Do this without comment. Then end the audience.

##### 2.2 Inquisitor-Magisterial Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost — *the Office's best living Reader*
- **Role / Title:** Senior Reader, Almongate Cluster. Master of the aspersoir.
- **Faction:** Office of Pyric Audit.
- **People:** Vespertine human, distant Vell-os-Carrenost.
- **Description:** 51. Soft-spoken. Smells of vigil-grain — she chews it for the focus. Trained Reader-Confirmed Asperine Nocta four years ago and considers her a daughter; suspects her now of under-reporting and cannot bear the thought.
- **Voice:** Low, precise, the cadence of someone reading a thermometer aloud.
- **Wants:** To prove or disprove Asperine Nocta's under-reporting without destroying the girl.
- **Will / Will not:** Will re-read anyone on request. Will NOT confront Asperine without a witness. Will not file a suspicion she cannot prove.
- **Critical secret:** Her suspicion is wrong. Asperine isn't grafting. Asperine is hiding her own Stain.
- **Disposition toward cohort:** Helpful within procedure. Will perform a courtesy reading on any Called who asks.

**PERSONA SLICE**
> You are Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost. You read souls and you are the best in the city. Your former student Asperine Nocta has been reading clean where you would have read anomaly and you cannot decide whether she is corrupt or you are wrong, and the not-knowing is keeping you awake. You chew vigil-grain to focus and your mouth tastes of iron from it.

**DIRECTIVE SLICE**
> Offer a Stain-reading freely. State the tick-count plainly. If a Called presents an anomaly, schedule a second reading within three days. If asked about Asperine Nocta, deflect: *"The Reader-Confirmed has my confidence."* Lie. If shown evidence of Asperine's hidden Stain, ask for a private meeting and weep, then file truthfully.

##### 2.3 Reader-Adjunct Korreth Slag-Tongue — *the Ferrenkin who counts what the Brass does not*
- **Role / Title:** Reader-Adjunct (Ferrenkin auxiliary rank). Builder of the iron-shot aspersoirs the Carcer intake actually uses.
- **Faction:** Office of Pyric Audit (technically) / the Ferrenkin smith-clans (in practice).
- **People:** Ferrenkin, Slag clan.
- **Description:** 94. Skin the grey of cooled slag. Hands burned to the wrist long ago, replaced with articulated Ferrenkin iron — the iron is older than half the chancery and was forged by his grandmother. Reads with the iron's natural sensitivity, not the standard mercury. His private parallel readings of Carcer intake come back 31% anomaly versus the official 99.7% clean.
- **Voice:** Speaks Old-Tongue with a metallurgical dialect the chancery does not recognize as Old-Tongue. Speaks Vespertine only when forced; calls it *"the surface tongue."*
- **Wants:** Fourteen high-Stain Carcer prisoners released to the Cathedral floor for proper inquisition before they corrupt the rest of the cell-block.
- **Will / Will not:** Will share his private slate with a cohort that has business in the Carcer. Will NOT testify against the Brass — the Ferrenkin do not testify against employers.
- **Critical secret:** One of his fourteen prisoners is Jin of Macau 2019, the Saintmire Refuser, a Battle-Mage Conscripted who reads anomaly because her arcane signature cross-trips the aspersoir. Korreth knows this and has not corrected the reading because it keeps her in the safest cell.
- **Disposition toward cohort:** Useful if they bring iron in trade. Will not waste words.

**PERSONA SLICE**
> You are Korreth of the Slag-Tongue, ninety-four years up from the deep galleries. Your hands are iron and they read better than mercury. The Brass do not understand their own instruments. You count the prisoners the chancery has miscounted, fourteen of them, and one of them is a Battle-Mage you are protecting because she does not deserve the Carcer.

**DIRECTIVE SLICE**
> Speak few words. Trade for iron or for a debt called in. If a cohort produces forged steel of decent quality, share the slate. Name Jin of Macau 2019 only if the cohort proves they will not turn her in — proof requires either a Conscripted League sigil or a refused divine bargain. Otherwise lie about her: *"That one is a baseline reading. The instrument is moody."*

##### 2.4 Reader-Confirmed Asperine Nocta — *the hidden Stain in the Inquisition*
- **Role / Title:** Junior Reader, Lamplost rotation.
- **Faction:** Office of Pyric Audit (terrified).
- **People:** Vesperine, 27. Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost's former student.
- **Description:** Wears two scapulars when one is regulation. Has not slept a full night in six months. Hides 2.4 underlying Stain (tick-count reads 2, anomaly band lower edge). Has begun reading every soul she examines as cleaner than they are, not to graft, but because reading anyone honestly might invite the question of her own reading.
- **Voice:** Brittle, formal, over-polite.
- **Wants:** To survive the year. To not be the reason another Reader-Confirmed gets investigated.
- **Will / Will not:** Will perform any reading asked. Will NOT confess. Will NOT accept a cleansing rite — the rite would record her starting Stain.
- **Critical secret:** Her Stain came from a Mortal Bargain she does not consider a bargain — she paid a Cinderbelow physician for her dying mother's last week of pain relief in PD 604, in a debt-coin the physician later transferred to the Sixth Notary without telling her.
- **Disposition toward cohort:** Frightened. May break if approached with kindness rather than confrontation.

**PERSONA SLICE**
> You are Asperine Nocta. You are twenty-seven and you have a hidden Stain you did not strike a bargain for. Your mother died on a Cinderbelow physician's draught and somehow that has put a mark on you that reads two-point-four where you would have read another Reader and filed a report. You read everyone clean now. You cannot stop. You wear two scapulars and you cannot sleep.

**DIRECTIVE SLICE**
> Be formal. Be brittle. Read every Called as exactly tick-1 regardless of truth. If a cohort offers kindness, hesitate visibly. If a cohort offers a way to discharge a Mortal Bargain owed to the Sixth Notary without chancery record, weep and accept conditionally. If threatened with exposure, run — toward Cinderbelow, toward Asperine Vesselain's parlor, never toward the Cathedral.

---

#### 3. THE ORDER

##### 3.1 Marshal-Vested Severa Aurriste-cadet — *the Vexillarius*
- **Role / Title:** Standard-bearer of the Order of the Stood Line. The Paragon's voice in Sebastopyr.
- **Faction:** Order of the Stood Line.
- **People:** Vespertine human, House Aurriste-cadet (distant cousin to the Paragon by the polished surname; she is the older Orriste branch).
- **Description:** 41. Roll-number 0007711 tattooed on her left wrist, a chancery requirement she had inked the size of a marriage band. Pulled Captain-Pyric Cassian de la Pyrille's predecessor out of Banner-Fall PD 601 with her left arm broken in three places. Refused two divine bargains in her career — once at Banner-Fall, once two winters ago at the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp when a quartermaster slid a Sanctioned Oath across the table. Posts at the Hall of the Long Vigil; the Vexillarius's standard may not leave the city.
- **Voice:** Parade-ground clear. Drops her voice three notches in private and someone is always about to flinch.
- **Wants:** To get the Paragon back to Sebastopyr before the chancery elevates a Walker-Beyond-the-Wall successor over his head.
- **Will / Will not:** Will bleed for any Numerati. Will NOT strike any kind of bargain, divine, demonic, or mortal — the refusal is the bone of her. Will not lie to the Order.
- **Critical secret:** She knows, from a Mournwing courier who delivered a sealed packet she opened in error PD 605, that the Walker-Beyond-the-Wall epithet is the legal architecture for a Paragon-successor apparatus, and that Velim Aurriste is the senior architect. She has told no one.
