#### ONE-PAGE PLAYER HANDOUT — *"Names You'll Hear in Sebastopyr"*

> *Read this before you sleep. You'll hear most of these tomorrow.*

- **The Sebastopater** — the old man at the top. Eighty-one. Weeps when he Calls you. Means it.
- **The Paragon** — the saint at Ferrostat. Fifty-one. Has not been in Sebastopyr in ten years. Will write you back.
- **Mortane the Half-Kind** — the priest at the Sebastopater's door. He will not let you in. He will be very polite about it.
- **The Sebast-Auditor** — wears a brass mask with three hundred and twelve holes. Will not speak to you. Will sometimes hand you a single piece of paper.
- **Velim Aurriste, Cantor-Magisterial** — beautiful, charming, lethal. If he writes you a sermon, you will remember it forever. That is the warning.
- **Asperine os Veillarde, Cantor-Magisterial** — the singer. Lonely. Knows more than she has said. Trust earlier than feels safe.
- **Severa Aurriste-cadet** — Vexillarius. Refused two bargains. Will trust you if you have refused one. Will not work with you if you have accepted one.
- **Old Pell** — pours tea in the Cinderbelow with his left hand. The right is bandaged. Don't ask. Pay for the second answer.
- **Mother Aspine** — bakes the bread and brokers the small demonic bargains. Cousin to the Sebastopater. She is sincere. That is what makes her dangerous.
- **Asperine Vesselain** — the heretic-broker. Writes in a tongue older than the Old Tongue. Will warn you what the Calling did to your soul before she sells you anything new.
- **Wren Ashlin** — the Conscripted League. She has been here eight years. Curses in your tongue if she shares it.
- **Hester Brunn** — the Brother with the cinder hand. Prints the truth weekly. Will not print rumor.
- **The Quartermaster of Tongues** — a duke of hell who looks like a quartermaster. Bargains paid in words you will never speak again. Has an open account on the Paragon.

> *If you remember nothing else: the Paragon is real. The miracle is real. The danger is what was buried to make the miracle the only one. Faith is operational. Damnation hides. Power has a price. The righteous are the danger. Watch the rain on the cathedral stones. Watch who is sure.*

> *Sustineo. Nec frangor.*

---

## IX. Plot Threads — The Twelve Master Arcs

### Master Plot Threads — Sebastopyr, PD 606

> *"The bell rings; the count is kept; the saint endures; the lamp does not go out — yet."*

The world holds twelve master threads. Eight are required by canon; four are derived. Every thread carries at least one throughline test. None resolves cleanly. The engine disposes; the chancery curates; the threads pull.

**STATUS LEGEND**
- **LATENT** — present in the world but not yet pressing on any PC. Hooks exist; no clock is ticking.
- **ACTIVE** — currently moving; NPCs are taking actions; the world will advance it whether or not PCs engage.
- **BURNING** — on a clock. Will fire within the current arc unless interrupted. A canonical_moment is queued or has already fired.

**URGENCY** — narrative pressure in the next 1d10 sessions (1 = background hum; 10 = the cathedral cracks tonight).

---

#### REQUIRED THREADS

##### THREAD 1 — The Murder of Confessor Thelos di Carrenost (the Cathedral Murder)

**STATUS:** active
**URGENCY:** 8

The seventh-seat Annotator of the Custodes Numeri was found dead in the Cantor's Stair, three landings below the Mort-Censorium, on the eve of the Octave of Triumph PD 606. Cause of death listed as "vigil-collapse"; actual cause: a beeswax stylus, warmed in palm, driven through the soft palate. The body was found by a Postulant, not a Confessor, which is why the report exists at all. The Cantorial Scribes' own bone-handled scalpels were missing from the wax-tray that morning. They were returned to the tray by sunset, cleaned, by a hand the Sebast-Auditor has not named.

Inspector Nera Cazares (Called, 1947 Earth, Detective prototype) was assigned the case because no Pyrian inquisitor could be trusted with it and a Called woman with no factional debt could be spent if she got too close. She has been working it for nine days. The clue-state is contested: three witnesses give incompatible accounts and one of them is Postulant Liturge di Carrenost, the dead man's niece, who is reading her uncle's commonplace book at night and asking the wrong questions at chapter.

**HOOKS**
- Cazares needs a translator for *cursivus sebastinus minor* and can only get one through the Inquisition, which is exactly who she cannot trust
- Liturge di Carrenost will approach a PC who shows competence and a willingness to be discreet; she has her uncle's last three folio-leaves and does not know what they say
- Thelos's chambers were searched three times after death — by three different hands in three different orders, none of them official
- Marshal-Vested Severa Aurriste-cadet has taken a private interest because Thelos was her confessor for eleven years; she is making her own list
- A Mournwing courier delivered a black-canvas folio to Thelos the morning he died; the Mournwing roll has been struck through with iron-stylus and the courier (a girl named Wren of the High Roost) is in the wind

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- Killer named in chancery or before a witness with Standing â‰¥ Inquisitor-Vested AND
- The folio's content surfaces (it is the partial-name of the Sixth Notary, copied from a Mournwing intercept) OR is destroyed before surfacing
- The empty seventh seat of the Custodes Numeri is either filled (Liturge accepts) or refused (Liturge defects)

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Vigil at the Empty Wax-Tray* — the moment the killer's identity is spoken aloud in the Audit-Below, the bone-handled scalpels are found rearranged, and whoever is standing in that room learns that the killer was already inside the Custodes Numeri. (Not yet fired.)

---

##### THREAD 2 — The Buried Saint-Count (How Many Have There Been)

**STATUS:** burning
**URGENCY:** 9

The Cathedral teaches one Paragon in living memory. The closed sheets in the Audit-Below name seventy-three souls authenticated as paragons between 51 PD and 583 PD, plus forty-eight nameless (the Cohort of the Lost Vespers and its kin). At least four Paragons in living memory. Two were women. One was Caer-Druin. The count of 143 official saints is unrelated; that is a different curated registry. The Plate of Sebastian (the forty-foot stratum of fused saint-bone beneath the Cathedral) is a third. The full answer is held by the Custodes Numeri, written in *cursivus sebastinus minor* by bone-handled scalpel into wax, and walked down the Cantor's Stair after every emendation.

The Paragon himself asked. The Mournwing Letter of PD 605 — three folded sheets in Halidan's own hand, addressed to the Sebastopater, carried by a Mournwing courier — asked the chancery how many saints there have been. The letter was intercepted by Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind, broken-and-resealed, filed without answer in the Audit-Below's eighth stratum. Mortane wept doing it.

Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde has been singing fragments of the Vocatio Aurriste (PD 581 — two years before the Standing) alone in her chamber, and her Stain has not moved. She knows whose hand wrote the suppression order on the 584 PD requisition slip; she has not said. Postulant Liturge is closing on the cursivus sebastinus minor. Brak Iron-Eye keeps his own private slate.

**HOOKS**
- A character with access to the Audit-Below (Inquisition badge, Cantorial Scribe escort, mortal-bargain debt with Old Pell) can reach the eighth stratum but not the ninth
- The unread Mournwing Letter is in Mortane's locked desk in the Vocation House; the lock is mortal
- Asperine os Veillarde will teach *cursivus sebastinus minor* to one student who can be trusted to keep silent — she is auditioning candidates
- The Brothers of the Cinder Hand are about to publish a list of nine suppressed paragon-names in *The Refusal*; their source is a defected Inquisitor-Vested who has the wrong four of the nine
- Hierarch Nocta's sealed fourth report on the Paragon's PD 583 ANOMALY reading exists in the Sebast-Auditor's keep

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- A true count, with names, surfaces in a forum the chancery cannot suppress (printed; sung; spoken in open chapter) OR
- The Audit-Below's eighth-and-ninth-stratum ledgers are destroyed, sealing the question forever OR
- The Sebastopater is told and chooses (the canon does not foreclose his answer)

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Reading of the Names in the Sanctuary Ring* — the unspoken paragon-names read aloud at the Cathedral steps during the Octave, with Sebastopater Iohanne weeping at his eleven-thousand-four-hundred-and-forty-seventh bead, and Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste standing in the chancel with his hands flat on the rail and his face unreadable. (Not yet fired.)

---

##### THREAD 3 — The Next Demonic Advance (The Carrion Census at Ferrostat)

**STATUS:** burning
**URGENCY:** 10

The Sixth Notary — *Numerator-Sextus-Qui-In-Margine-Scribit*, also known as *Sextus-Qui-Sine-Verbo-Signat* — has been composing his true name in the registers of hell since PD 565. The composition is not complete. When it completes, the Notary attains the right to file a writ of foreclosure under the Long Ledger's procedural rules. The first writ is already drafted in the Quartermaster's anteroom: it names Ferrostat-on-the-Mire as collateral on an unpaid bargain, and it names Saint-Aspirant Halidan Aurriste as a CLERICAL ERROR TO BE CORRECTED.

The chancery does not have this intelligence. The Mournwing have it. The Mournwing have not shared it.

The advance is not soldiers at the wall. It is a writ. The Hordes will be the enforcers, but the legal action will precede them by hours, and Ferrostat's defenses are calibrated to a siege, not to a foreclosure. The mechanism: a flock of carrion-birds will land on the Mire walls and read the writ aloud in unison in a Vespertine dialect that has been dead for four hundred years. Captain-Pyric Cassian de la Pyrille's Reclamation Corps has been drilling for an assault. They have not drilled for a document.

The window: the Notary's name is twelve to forty syllables from completion (estimates vary; Bera Quist's Ferrenkin assistant has done the audit). At the rate hell composes, that is somewhere between three weeks and six months.

**HOOKS**
- The Mournwing's silence is brokerable. Their head courier, Ven of the High Roost, will trade the partial name for protection of the four hundred remaining Mournwing under a Cathedral seal her people do not currently hold
- A binding of the Sixth Notary BEFORE name-completion can sunder him; this requires the partial name, a Vested Six binding-formula, and a soul willing to perform the rite (the rite costs Grace AND a binding-clause oath, which is itself a Divine Bargain with the Order of Sanctioned Bindings)
- Confessor-Ordinary Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost at Ferrostat is filing daily Stain-readings of the Paragon that come back CLEAN; if the Notary's writ names Halidan a clerical error, Mauritz's CLEAN readings are the Cathedral's only legal defense
- The carrion-birds have begun gathering on the Mire's outer pickets. The Order has not yet asked why
- Heretic-broker Asperine Vesselain has sold pieces of the partial name to seven different buyers as "marketable intelligence"; one of the buyers is House Halidan-Aurriste

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- The Sixth Notary is bound or sundered before name-completion OR
- Ferrostat falls (Halidan's Grace pool exhausted; the writ is read; the Mire walls are vacated) OR
- The writ is paid: a substitute soul accepts the clerical-error designation in Halidan's place (the Cathedral will allow this if the substitute volunteers; the Conscripted League will not, on principle)

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Reading of the Writ at the Mire* — carrion-birds in pre-Vespertine dialect at dawn, Halidan in black silk glove drawing the Vas Halidani's last sext-hour ration, Captain-Pyric Cassian's Auxiliary dead piling on the picket-line for a battle whose paperwork they have already lost. (Not yet fired.)

---

##### THREAD 4 — The False-Singularity of the Paragon (Not False-Paragon — Curated Count)

**STATUS:** active
**URGENCY:** 7

Halidan Aurriste is a real Paragon. His miracle is real. His Stain readings come back CLEAN every dawn for twenty-three years; the chancery's own Vesperine minority report demands re-reading and is sealed. He refused the Quartermaster of Tongues' offer the night of the Standing. His Grace pool is genuine, his Onus Aspectus is at *gradus undecim*, his weight is killing him slowly, and he does the work because the work is his.

The lie is not him. The lie is the SINGULARITY — that he is the first. The lie is the Polishing of the Roll, the renumbering of the towers in PD 583, the chancery clerk's stroke in PD 602 that prevented the cross-reference between his polished surname *Aurriste* and the Aurriste keel-block installed beneath the Sebastopater's throne in PD 73. The lie is the Walker-Beyond-the-Wall succession apparatus Cantor-Magisterial Velim co-authored in PD 597 — the procedure for replacing Halidan when his Grace runs out, written without his knowledge, naming Orric Aurriste-cadet of Ferrostat as the queued successor.

Halidan suspects something. He wrote the Mournwing Letter. He has begun asking after earlier saints, and the Aspirant-Clerks have a precise liturgical deflection formula they apply with smiles. He does not know the keel-throne. He does not know about Orric. He does not know about Velim's Octave Bargain. He does not know that his Grace pool is projected to reach minimum-operational threshold in eleven years, and that the chancery is preparing for that day without preparing him.

**HOOKS**
- Orric Aurriste-cadet of Ferrostat (28, currently a Captain-Vested in the Reclamation Corps, doesn't know he is being queued) is being courted by Custodes Numeri envoys and House Veillarde marriage-brokers in the same week
- The Vas Halidani cistern's emptying rate has visibly increased; Ferrenkin engineers can prove the Grace-decline curve from the hydraulics alone
- A PC who delivers Halidan the Mournwing Letter's unedited text restores his question; a PC who delivers the curated reply seals it
- Halidan keeps a desk-letter he has written and not sent, addressed to the Cathedral, asking to come home; Confessor-Ordinary Mauritz has read it
- Captain-Pyric Cassian de la Pyrille knows about the Auxiliary Roll's true scale and has begun named-saying his Auxiliary dead at vespers — a small heresy that the chancery has chosen not to notice yet

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- Halidan is told and chooses (the doctrine of singularity dies with his knowledge; the kingdom's faith is tested) OR
- The Walker-Beyond-the-Wall apparatus fires (Halidan's Grace fails; Orric is elevated; the curation continues for another generation) OR
- A second living Paragon rises before either event, breaking the singularity by simple arithmetic

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Paragon at the Keel-Throne* — Halidan walks the seven concentric courses descending and stands in the Sanctuary Ring before the Sebastopater's throne and asks, in Old-Tongue accusative-vocative, the name carved in the keel-block. The answer is his own. (Not yet fired.)

---

##### THREAD 5 — The Stain-in-the-Inquisition (Asperine Nocta's Hidden 2.4)

**STATUS:** active
**URGENCY:** 6

Reader-Confirmed Asperine Nocta, 27, Vesperine, trained by Inquisitor-Magisterial Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost, currently posts at the Almongate Cluster. She hides 2.4 Stain. Her aspersoir-readings of others come back accurately. Her own self-reads (which Inquisition Vesperines are required to perform monthly) come back CLEAN. She has been managing this for nineteen months. She knows that her tick-band 2 readings on others within the 1.5-3.0 underlying range are the ones the chancery has been quietly recalibrating, and she has begun under-reporting borderline cases not for profit but because she has worked out — correctly — that the operational thresholds are being moved upward to hide the rising baseline. Her instructor Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost has noted the under-reporting and suspects her of graft. Severa is preparing a sealed report.

Asperine is not the worst of it. The pattern is: the Cathedral's own measurement is corrupting the Cathedral's own measurers. The Sealed Anomaly Ledger holds 312 entries. Many of those entries are reader-self-reads filed as ANOMALY by Vesperine readers protecting themselves. The Sebast-Auditor has the access. The Sebast-Auditor has not acted, because the Sebast-Auditor (sealed identity, served since PD 583) has reasons.

Inquisitor-Vested Asperine de la Pyrille's Wednesday Lamplost readings come back clean for nineteen months. She is not corrupt. Her instrument is. The Almoner of Lamplost has begun a parallel ledger. She does not know.

**HOOKS**
- Asperine Nocta will break and confess to one person who finds her without a Cathedral witness; she has been rehearsing the words for six months
- Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost's sealed report names the wrong woman; a PC who reads it and corrects it can save the wrong career or destroy it
- The Almoner of Lamplost (Veriarch Pell di Almongate, 51) keeps the parallel ledger in a locked vesper-box and will share it with someone who can prove they are not Inquisition
- Reader-Adjunct Korreth Slag-Tongue's iron-shot aspersoirs read 31% anomaly against the official 99.7% clean and he can prove the calibration drift in twenty minutes given access to the chancery instruments
- A PC who is themselves Stained and reads CLEAN on a chancery aspersoir has hard evidence that the instrument lies; spending that evidence is a Mortal Bargain at minimum

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- The instrument-calibration drift is proven in open chapter (publication; Octave-of-Triumph reading; Cathedral inspection demanded) OR
- Asperine Nocta is exposed (chancery binding; her 2.4 becomes 6; she is taken) OR
- The Sealed Anomaly Ledger is read by someone outside the Vested Six and the contents are spoken

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Aspersoir at the Almongate* — a single PC holds the Cathedral's own instrument over Inquisitor-Magisterial Severa di Vell-os-Carrenost's tea and the mercury boils at tick-3, and Severa — who has been silent and right for thirty-one years — sets down the cup and says, in Old-Tongue indicative, "Per Sebast. So that is what it has been." (Not yet fired.)

---

##### THREAD 6 — The Noble-House Bargain-Maker (Lady Severa Veillarde and the Fever Ledger)

**STATUS:** active
**URGENCY:** 5

Three winters ago Lady Severa Veillarde of the Lower Pyr, sister of the Regent and matron of the Veillarde tithe-rolls, struck a Long Ledger bargain with *Liber-Quod-Numerat-In-Aeternum* for a guarantee she will not name. The price-clause specified payment in monthly "fever" deaths drawn from her tithe-rolls — names she selects, deaths the Ledger accepts as audited. She has paid eleven names. The twelfth is due at the next full moon. The thirteenth is due at the moon after. The Ledger does not specify when the count ends. She has begun to believe it does not end.

Lady Severa is not a monster. She is a desperate matron whose son was born with the wasting-sickness and would have died at four; the guarantee she purchased was his life to eighteen years. He is fifteen. She has three more years on the bargain she knows about and an indeterminate count of names beyond that. She selects from the elderly, the consumptive, the unredeemable; she has rules. The under-ward calls them the Veillarde Vespers. The Cathedral does not.

The bargain was sanctioned by no one. It was witnessed by Velim Aurriste of the Pyric Wall, who wrote the price-clause first and recorded it in the Curiate Vincula's Mirror Audit — which the chancery would consider a heresy if anyone asked. No one has asked, because the Veillarde tithes pay for the Cinderbelow Concord and the Bypassed Pensions, and the Office of Sanctioned Bindings has chosen not to know.

**HOOKS**
- The daughter, Asperine Veillarde, betrothed to Halidan's deputy, has found her mother's contract and does not yet know what it says
- A PC working under-ward charity will encounter the Veillarde Vespers as a statistical pattern in a parish death-roll; one such roll is kept by Veriarch Thelos di Cinderost (who also runs the Reflected printer's press)
- Old Pell the Rationer knows; he has refused to broker any of Lady Severa's grain purchases for four years and the Regent has noticed
- The Long Ledger's enforcer (an entity called the Sixth Counter, distinct from the Notary) walks the Lower Pyr every full moon at the hour the fever-death is logged, collecting an audit-mark; this is visible to Stain-Readers and to characters with the Detective prototype's clue-state machine at "inferred" or higher
- A PC with Standing in the Veillarde household can be drawn into the selection of the twelfth name

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- The bargain is paid out (the son lives to eighteen; the indeterminate count begins to ramify) OR
- The bargain is broken (Lady Severa accepts the son's death and confesses; the Long Ledger collects the difference in a manner the Cathedral will record as a household tragedy) OR
- A substitute is offered (a soul of equivalent Grace-weight; only the Paragon has it and he does not know)

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Twelfth Vesper* — Lady Severa stands at her tithe-roll at moonrise with her stylus over a name and a PC at her elbow, and the choice she makes is heard in the Long Ledger's hall by a voice that says only "audited." (Not yet fired.)

---

##### THREAD 7 — The Heretical Rising in the Lower Wards (The Brothers of the Cinder Hand)

**STATUS:** active
**URGENCY:** 7

The Brothers of the Cinder Hand began as three Refused Called souls (Hester Brunn, a coal-miner from 1923 Wales; Tomas Reyes, a labor organizer from 1968 Mexico City; Skar Slag-Hand, a Ferrenkin defector from the north Pyric Wall) printing the weekly broadsheet *The Refusal* on the Reflected press in the Lamplost Compact. They are now twenty-three known members, four Inquisitor-Vested defectors (the Cathedral does not yet have a complete list), and an unknown number of sympathetic Veriarchs in the Lamplost and Quietus wards. They print on Sundays. The Inquisition has been hunting them for nine years. The press is at Veriarch Thelos di Cinderost's chapel; the Inquisition does not know because the chapel is consecrated and the Wednesday readings come back clean.

*The Refusal* publishes four kinds of intelligence: (1) names of the Conscripted dead the Cathedral has not named; (2) testimony from Refused Called souls; (3) the under-ward Bench Rate, weekly, with chancery comparisons; (4) suppressed paragon-names obtained from defected Inquisitor-Vested sources. The fourth category is new. The current run names four paragons. Three are correct. The fourth (a "Saint-Aspirant Veridia of Saintmire, 481 PD") is a fabrication planted by Custodes Numeri to discredit the source. The Brothers do not know.

The rising is not armed. It is documentary. The Inquisition fears it because the doctrine of singularity is fragile to argumentation and the Cathedral has no good theological response to seventy-three names. The Cathedral's preparation: Hierarch-of-the-Mire Cassian Aurriste's Vesperine Loyalty Tally, which is staffing the next purge.

**HOOKS**
- The Reflected press needs a new ink-supply because the previous source (a Ferrenkin smith) was taken last month; a PC who can broker ink without chancery markers becomes load-bearing
- Hester Brunn is dying of black-lung and has six weeks; her successor is contested between Tomas (caution) and Skar (escalation)
- Postulant Liturge di Carrenost has reached out to the Brothers via a Mournwing intermediary; she has the cursivus sebastinus minor key
- The fabricated fourth name will be printed in the next issue if not stopped; printing it discredits the entire list
- Inquisitor-Vested Mauritz Aurriste-cadet (one of the four defectors, the Cathedral does not know) is about to be ordered to lead the Loyalty Tally's first raid and must choose

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- The Brothers are taken (raid succeeds; the press is destroyed; the doctrine of singularity holds for another generation) OR
- The Brothers print the verified list (chapter is forced to respond; the kingdom's faith is tested in the open) OR
- The Brothers are coopted (the Cathedral admits the suppressed count and absorbs the Brothers into a sanctioned Historical Commission; this is the option Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste is privately preparing as fallback)

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Wednesday That Was Not Clean* — the Inquisition raids Cinderost's chapel; the Wednesday readings come back ANOMALY for the first time in nineteen months; Veriarch Thelos di Cinderost stands at the altar with a printed sheet in his hand and reads four names aloud before the Inquisitor-Vested can stop him. (Not yet fired.)

---

##### THREAD 8 — The Doctrinal Feud: Eternal-War vs Young-Triumph

**STATUS:** active
**URGENCY:** 6

The Cathedral is split. The split is not personal — it is *systemic*, and it is *aging*.

**THE ETERNALISTS** (led by Archvigil Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost, 71, the head of wall-rites; supported by Marshal-Vested Orric Veillarde of the Lower Pyr, the dying wall-commander; and by the older Veriarchs of the Pyric Ward) hold that the war is *deemed eternal* in the old liturgical indicative, that the Paragon's miracle is a real grace but does not abrogate the doctrine of endurance, that the Reclamation has overextended, that the next advance will break the wall's logistics of Grace, and that Halidan should be recalled to Sebastopyr to hold the Sanctuary Ring rather than to take Mire-Beyond. They have control of the wall. They have lost control of the doctrine.

**THE TRIUMPHALISTS** (led by Hierarch-of-the-Mire Cassian Aurriste, 52, the senior cleric of the Reclaimed Crown; supported by Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste, the Custodes Numeri, the Vesperine majority opinion, the new-wealth House Halidan-Aurriste, and the Reclamation Concession) hold that the war's eternity was a curated lie now superseded, that the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity is the new orthodoxy, that the next advance must be taken in the next campaign season, that the Cathedral's logistics can sustain it, and that the Eternalists are senile heretics endangering the kingdom by their nostalgia. They have control of the doctrine. They have not yet purged the wall.

The Sebastopater Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX is structurally an Eternalist by lineage and a Triumphalist by signature (he signed the Doctrine's reaffirmation in PD 605). He weeps. He is filtered. He is not the deciding party.

The feud is not about theology — it is about LOGISTICS. The Vas Halidani's emptying rate is falsifiable. The Grace-decline projection is filed. The Eternalists are reading it correctly and saying so. The Triumphalists are reading it correctly and saying nothing, because the Walker-Beyond-the-Wall apparatus has them covered.

**HOOKS**
- Marshal-Vested Orric Veillarde of the Lower Pyr is dying; the Cathedral infirmary knows, the Order does not. His succession will fall to either Severa Aurriste-cadet (Triumphalist by family, Eternalist by sympathy) or Captain-Pyric Cassian de la Pyrille (Triumphalist, frontier-loyal). The choice is being brokered.
- Hierarch Cassian Aurriste's Loyalty Tally is staffing the purge of Vesperine clerics suspected of Eternalist sympathies; Marent de la Pyrille (his secretary) keeps the list and has begun adding names without instruction
- Archvigil Mauritz Vell-os-Carrenost drinks heavily in the Marshal Ring and has been saying out loud, in the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp, that the next advance is the kingdom's death
- A leaked Grace-decline projection from Confessor-Ordinary Mauritz at Ferrostat would settle the doctrinal question; the projection is in a sealed Mournwing folio
- A PC siding with the Eternalists gains Standing in the Order and the Pyric Ward and loses Standing in the chancery and the Reclamation Corps; siding with the Triumphalists, the reverse. Refusing the choice opens neither door.

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- The next advance is taken and succeeds (Triumphalists vindicated; Eternalists purged; the wall is thinned; the Cathedral commits to the new doctrine) OR
- The next advance is taken and fails (Eternalists vindicated; Triumphalists purged or reduced; Halidan is recalled; the doctrine of endurance returns) OR
- The next advance is canceled (a third faction — possibly the Conscripted League, possibly a Caer-Druin singer's intervention, possibly the Paragon's own refusal — forces a stay)

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Council at the Lampgate* — Archvigil and Hierarch and Cantor-Magisterial in the same chamber for the first time in three years, Sebastopater Iohanne weeping at the head of the table, and a single PC reading aloud from a sealed Mournwing folio the Grace-decline projection that ends the argument. (Not yet fired.)

---

#### DERIVED THREADS

##### THREAD 9 — Velim Aurriste's Octave Bargain (The Open Account)

**STATUS:** active
**URGENCY:** 6

In PD 588, one year after the Standing, Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste — then a thirty-one-year-old Confessor-Ordinary newly appointed to the chancery's doctrinal team — struck a bargain with the Quartermaster of Tongues in the Octave-of-Triumph anteroom of the Audit-Below. The grant: clarity. The Quartermaster gave him the structural argument for the Doctrine of Rescinded Eternity, complete, in three sentences of pre-Vespertine Old-Tongue, which Velim recorded that night and developed across the following twelve months into the Doctrine that founded the Reclaimed Crown. The price: *a future silence to be named*. The clause was not specified at the time and has not been collected. Velim's Stain readings: PD 588 CLEAN, PD 594 ANOMALY, PD 600 UNKNOWN. His fourth reading is scheduled for the Octave of Triumph PD 608. He has not stopped composing.

Velim is one of the most certain men in the city. He believes the Doctrine. He believes the bargain was a divine intervention through a heretical channel and is theologically sanitizable. He believes the Quartermaster will never collect because the Quartermaster has nothing to collect — a future silence is a future inaction, and Velim's life is a life of action. He is wrong about all three.

**HOOKS**
- The Quartermaster of Tongues has rationed his contracts for four years (per canon); the contraction is preparing room for collection
- Velim's fourth reading falls on the Octave of Triumph PD 608 — the same Octave the Carrion Census's writ-of-foreclosure is expected to fire
- Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde has been singing fragments of the Vocatio Aurriste, which is structurally related to Velim's bargain (both are pre-Standing chancery artifacts); she does not know the connection
- A PC who obtains the Quartermaster's contract-copy (it exists in the Audit-Below's seventh stratum) can prove the bargain to the Cathedral; the proof costs at minimum a Mortal Bargain with a Ferrenkin needle-smith for safe handling
- The price-clause "a future silence to be named" is collectible at any moment; the Quartermaster is waiting for the Octave of Triumph PD 608 to name it

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- The bargain is paid (Velim is silenced at the moment the chancery most needs him to speak; the Carrion Census writ goes uncontested) OR
- The bargain is exposed and broken (Velim's Doctrine is theologically suspect retroactively; the kingdom's founding logic shakes; Velim is taken before the Sebast-Auditor) OR
- Velim names the silence himself (he refuses the Doctrine in open chapter and surrenders his seat; the Custodes Numeri loses its senior; the Cathedral fractures)

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Silence at the Octave* — the Doctrine is read aloud and Velim Aurriste stands to defend it and his throat closes and no sound comes out, and the carrion-birds in the Mire begin to read the writ at the same instant. (Not yet fired.)

---

##### THREAD 10 — The Mournwing's Withheld Intelligence

**STATUS:** latent
**URGENCY:** 4

The Mournwing have, by their own martyr-roll, three pieces of intelligence the Cathedral does not:

1. The partial name of the Sixth Notary, in pre-Vespertine accusative-vocative, sixteen syllables of forty
2. The complete list of which Vesperine inquisitors have filed self-reads as ANOMALY in the past nineteen months (forty-one names; the Sealed Anomaly Ledger has 312 entries but only 41 are self-reads)
3. The location and current condition of the Cohort of the Lost Vespers' suppressed memorial — a sealed crypt under the Quietus Ward containing the partial relics of 117 paragon-adjacent souls

They withhold this intelligence not from malice but from policy. The Cathedral has not earned the Mournwing's trust since the cousins-in-the-open-sky did not return. The Mournwing are four hundred. They cannot afford to be wrong about the cost of cooperation. Their head, Ven of the High Roost (52, female, courier in her youth, now spire-watch), is brokerable. The brokerage requires a Cathedral seal guaranteeing the Mournwing's autonomy in their upper-spire roosts in perpetuity. No Sebastopater has been willing to grant it because the precedent would extend to the Caer-Druin and the Ferrenkin.

**HOOKS**
- Ven of the High Roost will meet a PC at the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp during the off-hour pour if approached through Old Pell the Rationer
- The Mournwing courier Wren of the High Roost (mentioned in Thread 1) is hiding in the upper roosts and has the original Thelos folio
- A PC who returns the Mournwing's pre-collapse martyr-roll (a fragment of which is in the Audit-Below's third stratum, mistaken for Cathedral property) earns Standing
- The Mournwing martyr-roll is the only document outside the Audit-Below that names the four pre-Halidan Paragons of living memory

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- The Cathedral seal is granted (Mournwing share all three intelligences; the Carrion Census, the Sealed Anomaly Ledger, and the Cohort of the Lost Vespers all surface in one week) OR
- The Mournwing are coerced (an Inquisition raid on the upper roosts; the intelligence is taken by force; the Mournwing scatter or die) OR
- The Mournwing are bypassed (a PC obtains the three intelligences without their cooperation; the threads above resolve without them; the Mournwing remain silent and wronged for another generation)

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Seal in the Sanctuary Ring* — Sebastopater Iohanne, weeping, signs the Mournwing Charter at the Cathedral steps, and Ven of the High Roost reads the Sixth Notary's partial name aloud in pre-Vespertine for the first time in the Cathedral's history, and the Mournwing in the upper spires sing for the first time since the cousins did not return. (Not yet fired.)

---

##### THREAD 11 — The Walker-Beyond-the-Wall Succession Apparatus

**STATUS:** latent
**URGENCY:** 5

In PD 597, by chancery decree, the Cathedral promulgated the fourth epithet of the Paragon: *Walker-Beyond-the-Wall*. The epithet was decreed under the cover of liturgical enrichment. Its actual function — known to the Vested Six, to Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste who co-authored it, and to Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind who administers it — is the SUCCESSION FORMULA. *Walker-Beyond-the-Wall* is liturgically separable from *the Arrow-Stander* and *He-Who-Was-Looked-Upon*; the chancery can transfer the title without canonizing Halidan (he is the Aspirant, the unique living-saint rank; canonization is reserved for the dead). The transfer requires three things: (1) the current Walker has been beyond the Pyric Wall continuously for â‰¥ ten years; (2) the queued successor has been beyond the Pyric Wall continuously for â‰¥ five years and has accepted a Divine Bargain administered by the Office of Sanctioned Bindings; (3) the Sebast-Auditor signs a finding of *Aspirant Grace Insufficiency*.

Halidan has been beyond the Wall continuously for ten years and three months. Orric Aurriste-cadet of Ferrostat (28, Captain-Vested, Reclamation Corps) has been beyond the Wall continuously for six years. He has not yet accepted the bargain because he has not yet been offered it. He will be offered it in the spring. The Sebast-Auditor's finding is in draft; the Vas Halidani readings support it.

Orric is a kind young man. He resembles Halden Orriste in the muster-roll sketch, which is not coincidence — he was selected ten years ago from a Carrenost orphanage on the basis of measured features. He does not know any of this.

**HOOKS**
- House Veillarde marriage-broker Lady Asperine Veillarde (the younger daughter, distinct from her Lady Severa mother) is attending Orric at Ferrostat under the cover of a winter visit; she is the bargain-witness the chancery has chosen
- A PC at Ferrostat can intercept the bargain-offering or warn Orric; the warning is a Mortal Bargain at minimum (someone in the chancery learns of the leak)
- Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind has the draft Aspirant Grace Insufficiency finding in his locked desk (see Thread 2 hooks)
- Halidan himself, if he learns of Orric, will refuse — but his refusal can be bypassed by a Sebast-Auditor finding because the Aspirant's consent is not canonically required
- The Conscripted League is preparing an action to deny the chancery the queued successor; their plan involves removing Orric from the Reclamation Corps roll by faking his Stain-reading at 5.0

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- The succession fires (Halidan's Grace fails; Orric is elevated; the kingdom has a new Paragon and the old one walks into the Mire) OR
- The succession is exposed (Halidan is told; Orric is told; the apparatus is read aloud in open chapter; the doctrine of singularity is rebuilt as a doctrine of LINEAGE, which the Triumphalists can sell and the Eternalists cannot) OR
- The succession is broken (Orric refuses the bargain; the chancery has no queued successor; the Cathedral is forced to canonize Halidan posthumously or admit a multi-Paragon canon)

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Offering at the Ferrostat Picket-Line* — Lady Asperine Veillarde at the gate of Ferrostat with the bargain-clause in a beeswax-sealed folio and Orric Aurriste-cadet in his Captain-Vested's cloak with the unread folio in his hand and Halidan in the keep behind him drawing his sext-hour ration; whichever of them speaks first determines the kingdom's next century. (Not yet fired.)

---

##### THREAD 12 — The Conscripted League's Active Refusal

**STATUS:** active
**URGENCY:** 7

The Conscripted League is the operational arm of Called souls who refuse the Calling's framing. Headed by Wren Ashlin (former Cohort of the Long Patience battle-mage, 31, arrived in PD 599 from a city the chancery cannot locate on any Aevarn map), the League meets at the Last Lamp tea-house in the Cinderbelow on new-moon nights. Membership: thirty-seven active, ninety sympathetic, perhaps three hundred who would help if asked once. They are politically distinct from the Brothers of the Cinder Hand (who are *documentarians*); the League is *operational*. They are preparing three actions:

1. The targeted incapacitation of Archvigil Severa di Mauritz at the next Vocation House Discernment, to disrupt the prototype-routing of the next Cohort and force the chancery to receive the new Called as a single ungoverned mass
2. The Ferrostat substitute — placing a willing Conscripted soul in the path of the Sixth Notary's writ as a clerical-error substitute for Halidan (this requires a Conscripted volunteer with Grace-weight; only one exists — Wren herself, who will not say so to the others)
3. The Saintmire Refuser extraction — recovering Jin of Macau (Battle-Mage prototype, Carcer cell three doors from where Hester Brunn was held) before her Aspirant-Reluctant classification expires and she is sent to the Reclamation Corps's Auxiliary Roll

The League is not allied with the Brothers; they share intelligence sometimes. The League's Saintmire extraction depends on the Brothers' Reflected press for forged Carcer-release documents. Neither faction trusts the other not to be infiltrated by Inquisition.

**HOOKS**
- Wren Ashlin will recruit a PC who has refused something — a Calling, a bargain, an oath. The recruitment ritual is silent and involves shared bread.
- Archvigil Severa di Mauritz drinks at the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp three nights in seven; she is marked for incapacitation, not death, but the League has not finalized the means
- Jin of Macau is in Carcer cell number fourteen and Korreth Slag-Tongue (Reader-Adjunct, Ferrenkin) has identified her as one of the fourteen high-Stain prisoners — but her "Stain" reads anomalously because her Battle-Mage arcane signature cross-trips the Vesperine aspersoir; she is not damned
- A PC who learns that Wren is the only viable Ferrostat substitute and tells the League changes the action
- The Brothers will refuse to print the forged Carcer-release documents unless the League shares the partial-name intelligence the Mournwing have not given them — which they do not have

**RESOLUTION CONDITIONS**
- The three actions fire in some combination (chancery destabilizes; Cohort arrival is ungoverned; Jin walks; Halidan is unwritten from the writ but Wren is consumed) OR
- The League is taken (Inquisition raid; Wren is read CLEAN by the broken aspersoir and released by accident; the League scatters) OR
- The League is absorbed (Conscripted Charter granted; the Calling rite is amended to allow Refusal as a sanctioned status; the League becomes a chancery faction with seats)

**CANONICAL MOMENT IF FIRED:**
*The Last Lamp Goes Out* — new-moon night, the Cinderbelow's tea-house emptied, Wren Ashlin walking east toward the Ferrostat road with a Conscripted-League seal in her pocket and the partial name of the Sixth Notary on her tongue, and the lamp at the door extinguished by the proprietor who will not say who paid for the dark. (Not yet fired.)

---

#### NPC VOICES (Quick-Reference Bench)

| NPC | Voice |
|---|---|
| **Sebastopater Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost IX** | Soft, slow, weeps at sermons, calls every Called soul "child of the calling," cannot count past eleven thousand four hundred and forty without losing the bead, will say "Per Sebast" when uncertain |
| **Saint-Aspirant Halidan Aurriste** | Heavy. Slow. Calls subordinates by full name and rank. Says "the wall holds" the way other men say "good morning." Has not laughed in eleven years. The black silk glove never comes off in public. |
| **Cantor-Magisterial Velim Aurriste** | Precise, clipped, beautiful Old-Tongue, never raises his voice, uses the indicative when the deemed is correct. Writes everything down. |
| **Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde** | Sings even when speaking. Operatic. Uses musical metaphor for theology. Hums fragments she should not know. |
| **Marshal-Vested Severa Aurriste-cadet** | Short sentences. Field-officer cadence. Refuses to swear in Old-Tongue. Says "Roll-number 0007711" before her name when announcing herself. |
| **Confessor Mortane the Half-Kind** | Gentle, courteous, careful. Sees you as a problem to be solved compassionately. Will lie to your face for your own good and feel it as love. |
| **Old Pell the Rationer** | Under-ward dialect, drops the liturgical particles, says "tally it" before tea. Honest about everything except his own age. |
| **Wren Ashlin** | Quiet. Listens twice before speaking. Battle-Mage hand-cant unconscious when angry. Calls the chancery "the office" the way a Detective would. |
| **Inspector Nera Cazares** | 1947 noir. "Pal." "See here." Smokes in the Mort-Censorium because the priest cannot stop her. Treats the case-file as the only theology she will respect. |
| **Lady Severa Veillarde** | Court Vespertine. Knows everyone's house-words. Has not slept eight hours in eleven months. Speaks of her son in the present tense only. |

#### RPG-MCP DELIVERY

The threads above are ready for `narrative_manage` batch_add. Structured entries follow.

## X. Player Brief — What Your Character Knows Day One

### Player Brief — What Your Character Knows Day One

*For the player. Read this tonight. Tomorrow you wake up in a city that was named for a saint who endured arrows and was clubbed to death anyway.*

---

#### YOU JUST ARRIVED. HERE'S WHAT YOU NEED TO KNOW.

You don't know any of this from a book. You know it because a Veriarch in a damp grey vestment told you, because a woman in the bread line muttered it, because a Lampwarden snapped at you when you said the wrong word, because the priest who pinned a tin sigil on your collar said *welcome* and the inquisitor three steps behind him did not smile.

You have been in Sebastopyr for **less than a week**. The Cathedral calls you **one of the Called**. Some of the other people they pulled across with you have started calling themselves something else. You haven't decided yet.

This brief is the surface of what the city teaches you in your first week. It is not the truth. It is what is *taught*, *whispered*, and *worried about*. Hold both columns at once.

---

#### I. THE OFFICIAL STORY (what the Church tells you, your first morning)

You are walked from the **Vocation House** in the Choir Ring to a stone bench in the **Sanctuary Ring** and given hot watered wine and a Postulant-Lector reads the **Catechism of the Called** to you. It takes nine minutes. It is the same nine minutes every cohort gets. Here is what it says, plain:

> *Soul-of-the-borne-across, you were not stolen. You were Called.*
>
> *Sebastopyr is the last bastion. The wall holds. Beyond the wall, the Hordes. Beneath the world, hell. Within the city, the only light left.*
>
> *We have been at war six hundred and six years. The war was once deemed eternal. It is no longer. Twenty-three years ago, a sergeant of the Fourth Shieldwall stood at the wall past the hour a body holds, and a divine attention found him, and we have a **Paragon** now. He commands from **Ferrostat**, beyond the wall. He has taken back ground. He will take more. You are part of the next advance.*
>
> *You will be given a station. You will be given an oath. You will be given **Grace**. You will be given a place in the only war that matters. Weep if you must. Eat. Then come to the Lector.*

That is the official voice. **It is sincere.** The Lector who read it to you was weeping a little by the end. He believed every word. That is the first hard thing about this city: **the people doing this to you are not villains**. They think they're rescuing you.

---

#### II. CHURCH PUBLIC TEACHING (the four things everyone learns by their fourth day)

These get drilled into you at orientation, repeated by parish priests, painted on the walls of the Marshal Ring, sung in the **Watch-Cantos** at dusk:

| Teaching | What it actually means in practice |
|---|---|
| **The wall holds.** | The Pyric Wall has stood six centuries. Don't ask about the towers. |
| **The Paragon is the proof.** | One man's miracle reopened the future. The war is no longer deemed eternal. *(Old word: "deemed." Not "is." This matters more than you think.)* |
| **Grace is sacred. Grace is metered.** | Holy power is a fuel. The Cathedral grants it. The Cathedral can withdraw it. **You will be tested for it.** |
| **The Stain is real, and it hides.** | Damnation is a thing you can carry without knowing. The Inquisition reads souls. Most readings come back **CLEAN**. Some come back **ANOMALY**. A few come back **UNKNOWN**, and that is theologically worse than ANOMALY. |

**Things the Church does NOT teach you in week one, but assumes you know:**
- That **the Paragon is the first.** (He is *deemed* the first. No catechism says "the first." They say "*ours.*" Listen for it.)
- That your refusal is possible. (It is. But every Lector pretends it isn't.)
- That the Calling is a **Bargain**. (It is. Power for a price. They call it *a gift*.)

---

#### III. LOWER WARDS WHISPERS (what you hear when no Lector is in the room)

You will end up in the **Under-Ward Ring** at some point in your first week. Maybe you go down for cheap bread. Maybe a fellow Called drags you to the **Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp** because she has heard there are *others*. Maybe you get lost. Down there, in the rain-light of the Cinderbelow, in tea-houses that smell like coal and incense and wet wool, you hear different things.

These are not lies. They are not facts either. They are *whispers*, and a whisper in Sebastopyr is its own kind of currency.

- **"They call you Called. We call ourselves Conscripted."** — said by someone who looks tired and is watching the door.
- **"Don't take a bargain at the Lampgate bench. Mother Aspine is lovely. The thing she works for is not."**
- **"The aspersoir doesn't read Battle-Mages right. If they read you and it ticks anomaly, that's the arcane crossing the holy. It's not damnation. Probably."**
- **"Tower count on the wall is eighty. Ask any soldier. Then ask a Ferrenkin. The number changes."**
- **"The Paragon hasn't been to the city in ten years. The chancery told him not to come."**
- **"There was a saint in five hundred eighty-one. Two years before the Standing. There's a chant for her in the archive. They don't sing it."**
- **"If your Stain reads CLEAN three times in a row, that's not clean. That's something else."**
- **"Old Pell at the Last Lamp will trade you Grace for a favor. Don't owe Old Pell more than one favor. Two is the death of you."**
- **"The Mournwing courier broke the seal on a letter last summer. The letter was the Paragon's. The letter asked a question. The chancery filed it."**

You don't know which of these are paranoia and which are load-bearing. **That is the point.** The city teaches you to live without certainty, while telling you certainty is the only thing worth dying for.

---

#### IV. COMMON NEWCOMER CONCERNS (what every Called asks in their first week)

The Lectors have rehearsed answers for the first four. The fifth they pretend you didn't ask. The sixth they will report.

1. **"Can I go home?"**
   — *"You are home, soul-of-the-borne-across. The world that bore you is not the world that needs you. Drink your wine."*
   *(Actual answer: No. No one has. The rite is one-way. The Conscripted League knows of three attempts; all three are dead.)*

2. **"What if I refuse?"**
   — *"Refusal is a holy right. The Refused are tended by the Brothers of the Cinder Hand and kept in the Carcer until grace finds them."*
   *(Actual answer: You go to the Carcer. Some come out. Some are still there from cohorts twenty years past. There is a cell — number eight — with someone in it who has not aged since 591 PD and speaks only in the indicative case of a language no one alive remembers.)*

3. **"Am I damned?"**
   — *"You will be Read. The reading will tell. Most are clean. Be of comfort."*
   *(Actual answer: The reading tells you what the instrument tells you. The instrument is calibrated. The calibration has been adjusted four times in living memory. The threshold has gone **up.** Be of comfort.)*

4. **"What is Grace and why do I keep hearing about it?"**
   — *"Grace is the divine fuel of the holy work. You will be granted a measure suitable to your station. Spend it well. Rest restores it. Sin does not."*
   *(Actual answer: It's a metered pool. You spend, you run out, you can't do the holy thing anymore. The Cathedral holds the spigot. If they decide you are heretical, the spigot closes. The mercenary and the saint draw from the same well by the same rules. Belief does not refill it.)*

5. **"Why are some people on the wall called Numerati?"**
   — *(Lector glances up, then down.)* — *"The Order of the Stood Line keeps the count. It is a sacred office. You needn't trouble."*
   *(Actual answer: The Order's central doctrine is that the count of the dead **is** the holiness. They are not guardians. They are witnesses. Their motto is SUSTINEO ET NUMERO — *I endure and I count.* They don't expect to win. They expect to be counted. This is supposed to be a comfort.)*

6. **"How many saints have there been?"**
   — *(Long pause. Lector smiles.)* — *"One hundred and forty-three, child. The list is in the lectionary. Now, your station."*
   *(Actual answer: Nobody asks this. The Lectors have a rehearsed pause for it. The Paragon asked it last year, in a letter, and the letter was intercepted and never answered. **Do not be the second person to ask this in writing.**)*

---

#### V. THE SUMMONERS' WELCOME vs THE WATCHFUL PRIEST AFTERWARD

This is the most important page of this brief. Read it twice.

##### The Welcome (Vocation House, the moment after the rite)

There are **twenty-four summoners** in the Vocation House. They wear plain white and ash-grey, their faces are wet with sweat from the thirteen-hour rite, and when you stagger out of the door of crossing onto the cold flagstones, they **lift you up**. They wrap you in a wool blanket. The eldest of them — usually **Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde**, a woman of sixty-two who used to sing opera in the Reliquary Ward — touches your forehead with her thumb and says, in Old-Tongue:

> *"Per Sebast — venisti. Numero te."*
> *"By the Enduring One — you came. I count you."*

She means it. She is weeping. They all are. This is, to them, the most sacred moment in their year. They have just **pulled a soul out of the dark** and into the only war that matters, and they love you for it before they know your name. They will press warm bread into your hands. One of them will say in halting Vespertine, *"You are our gift to the wall. Thank you, thank you, thank you."*

**The summoners are not lying.** They are not cynics. They believe with their whole hearts that they have just saved you. This is the Constantine heart of the whole city: **the worst thing being done to you is being done by people who are sure they are doing good, and who weep doing it.**

##### The Priest Afterward (the bench in the Sanctuary Ring, nine minutes later)

After the welcome, you are walked — gently, with a hand at your elbow — out of the Vocation House and up the **Cantor's Stair** to the Sanctuary Ring. You are seated on a stone bench. You are given hot wine. A different cleric sits down across from you. He is younger. His vestments are darker. He has a small brass instrument on a chain at his belt that **ticks** when he sets it on the bench.

He smiles. He does not weep. He is **kind** and he is **watching**.

He is a **Reader** of the **Office of the Pyric Audit** — what the streets call the Inquisition. He is here, in his own words, *"only to take your first reading, child. It is the gentlest of rites. A formality."*

He places the **aspersoir** — a small clear vial of mercury with a brass tick-counter beside it — between you and him. He says a low phrase in Old-Tongue. The mercury moves a little. The brass clicks: *one, two…*

He smiles wider. *"CLEAN, soul-of-the-borne-across. As is proper."*

He writes it down in a small book with a beeswax stylus. He stands up. He pats your knee. He says, *"Welcome to the bastion. You will be very useful."*

**The gap between those two clerics is the moral spine of this city.** One of them loves you. One of them is filing you. They are wearing the same robes. They went to the same seminary. They both believe.

---

#### VI. LEXICON — TERMS YOU WILL HEAR IN WEEK ONE

Memorize these. If you don't know them by the third day, someone will mark you as ignorant — which in Sebastopyr is not the same as innocent.

##### THE BIG WORDS

| Term | What it means (street level) | What it actually is (deeper) |
|---|---|---|
| **GRACE** | The holy fuel. The thing in your soul the Cathedral grants you. Spent on warding, holy fire, healing, on burning the Damned. | A metered resource. `{ current, max }`. Affordability is checked. Out of Grace, the holy weapon is just a weapon. **Recovers on rest and rite, not on belief.** |
| **THE STAIN** | Damnation in a soul. What the aspersoir reads. What hides. | A hidden state. Has an **actual** value and an **apparent** value. The instrument reads the apparent. The apparent can be wrong. **Especially when it says CLEAN.** |
| **A BARGAIN** | A deal — for power, for access, for a favor. | One of three kinds: **demonic** (paid in Stain), **divine** (paid in oath to the Cathedral), **mortal** (paid in debt to a person). All three are logged. Something always collects. |
| **THE CALLED** | What the Cathedral calls you and the others pulled across in the rite. | The Cathedral's gentle word. It implies *chosen*. Cf. Conscripted, below. |
| **THE CONSCRIPTED** | What the refused and the bitter Called call themselves. | The same population as the Called, named honestly. **Which word you use is a confession of what you think happened to you.** |
| **THE PARAGON** | Halidan Aurriste. The living saint. The one who Stood. Commands from Ferrostat. | A real, weary, holy man. Fifty-one. Has a tremor in his left hand. Has not been to Sebastopyr in ten years. Asked a question last year that no one will answer. |
| **THE YOUNG TRIUMPH** | The last twenty-three years. The Reclamation. The kingdom rising. | The Reclaimed Crown of Vespertin. A modest, bleeding, daily-harassed frontier. The doctrine that grew up around the Paragon's miracle and now profits from itself. |
| **THE WALL** | The Pyric Wall. Sebastopyr's curtain. The thing the Hordes break against. | Seven concentric courses. Eighty towers on the chancery roll. Eighty-four if you ask a Ferrenkin. Four condemned the year of the Standing, which is a coincidence the chancery does not discuss. |
| **THE HORDES** | The damned host beyond the wall. The enemy. | They are real. They come at every dawn. They are the *loud* enemy. The Stain inside the city is the *quiet* one, and the city is half-blind to it. |

##### THE SMALLER WORDS (heard in the first week)

- **The Pyr** — colloquial for Sebastopyr. *"Welcome to the Pyr."* Lets the speaker forget that *pyr* means *wall* and *sebast-* in its bitter sense means *the one who endured for nothing.*
- **The Cathedral** — the Cathedral of the Enduring One. The institution. Capital-C is the building; lowercase-c is the bureaucracy.
- **The Sebastopater** — the living head of the Cathedral. Currently **Iohanne Vell-os-Carrenost the Ninth**, 81 years old, blind in his left eye, carries ivory tally-beads for every soul personally summoned, weeps at every Calling. Beloved. Filtered.
- **The Order** — the Order of the Stood Line. The military arm. Witnesses, not guardians. Motto: *SUSTINEO ET NUMERO.*
- **The Inquisition / the Office / the Brass / the Tickers** — the Office of the Pyric Audit. They read Stain. They are usually polite.
- **A Lector** — a junior priest. The one who reads to you on your first day.
- **A Veriarch** — a parish priest. The one in your ward.
- **A Confessor** — a senior cleric, usually Vesperine, with the gift of reading Stain by hand. Powerful. Always watched.
- **A Vesperine** — a person of the half-kind elder bloodline. Outwardly human. More sensitive to Stain. Most of the high Inquisition is Vesperine. They are not entirely sure if they are trusted servants or hostages.
- **A Ferrenkin** — a stone-and-iron person. Grey-skinned, forge-eyed, smaller than humans. They make the wall-plate, the rail-guns, the censers. They remember things the chancery doesn't.
- **A Caer-Druin** — one of the hollowed hill-court folk. They sing the Watch-Cantos at dusk. The Cathedral claims their songs were always Vespertine. They permit this.
- **A Mournwing** — one of the winged courier folk. Black canvas wing-sheaths. They do not fly beyond the wall.
- **The aspersoir** — the Stain-reading instrument. A vial of mercury, a brass tick-counter. *CLICK* once: clean. *CLICK CLICK CLICK*: anomaly. Anything more: trouble.
- **The Vocation House** — where the Calling rite is performed. In the Choir Ring.
- **Ferrostat-on-the-Mire** — the frontier outpost. The Paragon's seat. A day's ride out, a day's ride back, more if the road is wet.
- **The Cinderbelow** — the lowest ring of the city. Hell-adjacent. The brokers work there.
- **The Carcer** — the prison-quarter. *"The Carcer"* with the article. Not *Carcer Ward.*
- **A Numerati** — a soldier of the Order who has taken the Oath of Numeration. Their hand is tattooed with a roll-number.
- **The Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp** — a tea-house in the Cinderbelow. Where you go when you need something nobody official will give you.

##### THE OATHS-AS-EXPLETIVES (you will hear these in the first hour)

- **"Per Sebast!"** — *By the Enduring One!* A mild oath. *Damn.*
- **"Sustineo!"** — *I endure!* A weary sigh. *Of course this is happening.*
- **"Nec frangor."** — *I do not break.* Muttered. Stubborn refusal.
- **"Ad audit!"** — *To the Audit!* The bastion's equivalent of *to hell with it.* Invokes the demonic Auditor. Considered crude but used freely.
- **"Numero te."** — *I count you.* The summoners' greeting. Also said at deaths. Also said before bargains.

---

#### VII. THINGS THAT WILL TRIP YOU UP (first-week mistakes)

- **Saying "you kidnapped me."** The summoners will look at you like you slapped a grandmother. They will be **hurt**. They will pray for you. They will not stop summoning.
- **Calling Grace "magic."** This is a category error and an offense. Magic is what Battle-Mages carry from their old lives. Grace is what the Cathedral grants. *They draw from different wells.* (Yours draw from a third — the Conscripted will ask which.)
- **Asking how many saints there have been.** Don't do this in writing. Don't do this near a Veriarch. If you must ask, ask Asperine os Veillarde when she is alone, after she has finished singing.
- **Owing Old Pell two favors.** One is a relationship. Two is ownership.
- **Trusting a CLEAN reading.** Clean means the instrument said clean. It does not mean clean.
- **Trusting an ANOMALY reading either.** Anomaly is what they call it when they don't want to say what it is. Battle-Mages tick anomaly on a third of readings because the arcane crosses the holy and the brass doesn't know the difference.
- **Mentioning the Quartermaster of Tongues by name.** Use *the office.* Use *the duke.* Don't use the name *Vox-Quae-In-Tenebris-Numerat.* It writes itself down when said aloud.

---

#### VIII. WHAT YOU ARE (the three of you, specifically)

You are a party of three. You came across in the same rite. The Cathedral routes you by what you carry. **Archvigil Severa di Mauritz**, head of the wall-rites, took **nine seconds** to look at each of you and decide where you go. She drinks heavily in the Marshal Ring after every Calling. She did this morning too.

##### THE HUMAN
You came across with nothing the Cathedral can measure. No arcane pool. No clue-engine. **The Cathedral loves this.** You are *theologically clean* — a pure vessel for Grace, eligible for the full grant, routed straight into the **Order Numerati**. You will be offered the **divine bargain** — the oath that grants you Grace in exchange for an obligation to the Order. The price is real. Read every word before you sign. Especially the **gap-where-the-saint-stood** — the mandated breath of silence between the grant-clause and the price-clause. Three hundred fourteen years of records show no one has ever used it to withdraw. **You could be the first.** *(They will be very surprised if you are.)*

##### THE BATTLE-MAGE
You came across with an **arcane pool** the Cathedral did not give you. This is **theologically inconvenient**. Your magic predates their grant. They cannot take credit for it and they cannot fully trust it. You will be routed to the **Reclamation Corps** at Ferrostat — frontier work, out beyond the wall, far from the city's measurements. They will offer you Grace alongside your arcane pool, but Grace will be **rationed** and **watched**. Your aspersoir readings will run hot — **expect ANOMALY in your first reading**, which is not necessarily damnation but is *definitely* a flag in your file. A clerical category was invented two cohorts ago for people like you: **Aspirant-Reluctant.** It is a holding pattern. It means *we do not know what to do with you and we are watching.* The **Brothers of the Cinder Hand** will know your name within three days.

##### THE DETECTIVE
You came across with no magic and no holy capacity — and an instinct for what people are not saying. The Cathedral has a use for this. You will be routed to the **Inquisition** or to the **Order's officer-track**. There is currently an open case the chancery is quietly looking for someone to assign: **the murder of Confessor Thelos di Carrenost**, a senior cleric of the Cantorial Scribes, killed clean three months ago. The official line is *heretical agents.* The Inquisition has not solved it. They have not really tried. **You may be offered this case.** If you accept, you will be given a tin sigil and a small allowance of Grace-by-proxy (you can call on it through a confessor). You will also be given a **partner**, who will be a Vesperine confessor with their own agenda. Treat every clue as **status: unknown** until you can mark it **proven**. *The Cathedral marks things proven all the time. They are often wrong, and they are never overruled.*

---

#### IX. WHAT YOU FEAR (honestly, the three of you, on day one)

- That the rite was not a calling but a harvest.
- That the kind clerics are the dangerous ones.
- That refusal is possible but exits only into the Carcer.
- That CLEAN is worse than ANOMALY.
- That the Paragon is real, and the doctrine around him is not.
- That something you do not see is keeping a ledger on you, and the ledger started the moment the rite finished.
- That you will start to believe.
- *That you will be useful.*

---

#### X. THE SHAPE OF YOUR FIRST WEEK (so you can plan tonight)

**Day 1 (today, in fiction):** The rite. The welcome. The Reader. Hot wine. A bed in the Postulants' Hall above the Vocation House. The bell at midnight that wakes you sobbing without knowing why.

**Day 2:** Catechism. Stain reading recorded. Station assigned. (Human: Order. Battle-Mage: Reclamation Corps, posting to Ferrostat pending. Detective: case file delivered.) You will be given a tin sigil with your **roll-number**. Memorize it. They will ask you for it the rest of your life.

**Day 3:** Your first descent into the Common Ring on your own errand. You will see the city without a Lector at your elbow. You will hear, for the first time, the word **Conscripted**.

**Day 4:** First contact with someone who is not what they appear. (DM will engineer this.) You will need to decide, fast, whether you trust your gut or the catechism. You will not know yet which is worse to trust.

**Day 5:** The first **Bargain** is offered to you. Could be divine. Could be mortal. Could — quietly, in a doorway in the Cinderbelow — be demonic. **The price is logged the instant it is struck.** The clerk does not need to be present. The ledger writes itself.

**Day 6:** You meet someone who knew the rite was coming for you before it did.

**Day 7:** First sabbath. The Watch-Cantos at dusk. The Caer-Druin singing in a tongue older than the Cathedral. The Cathedral folding the song into their orthodoxy in real time. You will feel something you cannot name and will not be able to ask about safely.

---

#### XI. A CLOSING NOTE FROM THE DM

You are not playing heroes. You are not playing villains. You are playing people who **just arrived** in a city that thinks it saved you, that is wrong about almost everything it is most sure of, and that will hand you holy fuel and a sword and ask you to count the dead.

Faith here is **operational**. Damnation **hides**. Every deal has a **price**. The righteous are the **danger**. The official story is **curated**.

You will be told, every day, that the war is being won.

It is. A little. For now.

The lamp does not go out — yet.

**Welcome to the Pyr.**

**Per Sebast — venisti. Numero te.**

---

## Appendix — Throughline Coherence Check

"The world holds all six throughline tests, and holds them at every scale from the saint-day pie to the demonic foreclosure-writ. The canon is, as it must be, OPERATIONAL: Test 1 (faith operational) is everywhere — the Vas Halidani's seventeen-ton cistern emptying by sext, the libellus gratiae chits, the Pyric Bell tolling for every soul's last Grace-spending, the aspersoir's dual-scale meter, the Onus Aspectus gradus, the Marshal Ring's Counting cadence, the Held Breath silencing dawn bargains across the city. Test 2 (damnation hides) is the spine of the Stain pillar and shows in Asperine Nocta's 2.4 hidden Stain, Confessor Mortane's 23 years of clean readings, the broken Listening Arches the Vested Six refuses to repair, the Stain-Reader's Avenue's statistically-impossible four-boils-a-year, the Sealed Anomaly Ledger's 312 entries, Cantor-Magisterial Velim's CLEAN/ANOMALY/UNKNOWN sequence, and Captain-Pyric Cassian's filed-and-not-actioned anomaly. Test 3 (everything is a ledger) is structural at every level: the Curiate Vincula and the Mirror Audit, the Bench Rate, the Stipend of the Wrong, the Cinderbelow Concord with its two non-matching copies, the Auxiliary Roll, the Bypassed Pensions crisis, the Lampwarden's day-book, the Long Ledger, the Mort-Censorium's case-closure double-entries with Audit-Below paragon-deaths. Test 4 (the righteous are the danger) has FOUR fully-developed certain-righteous figures (Velim Aurriste, Severa Aurriste-cadet, Soror-Prima Marent, Inquisitor-Vested Mauritz Aurriste-cadet) plus second-tier (Cantor-Magisterial Asperine os Veillarde the discoverer-who-cannot-speak, Confessor Mortane editing truth in love, Hierarch Cassian Aurriste preparing the Inquisition purge, Severa Veillarde paying in 11 names for grain, Lampwarden Marent de la Pyrille keeping her day-book chained to her wrist not knowing whom from, Captain-Pyric Cassian de la Pyrille named-saying his Auxiliary dead with the Paragon's 'Count them well' as the only authorization). Test 5 (sacred and seedy share the street) lives in the Reliquary Ward's relic-mongers next to brothels, the Drinkings-of-the-Last-Lamp's off-hour pour, the censer-tender's marker-keeping work, Mother Aspine's parish bread and Stain-1 brokerage from the same bench, the Mort-Censorium ash baking the city's bread, the Cinderbelow children's whistling-language, the saint-day pie slashed in the under-wards for whatever could be scrounged. Test 6 (the official story is curated) is the throughline's KEEL and runs through every single entry — the Polishing of the Roll, the Cohort of the Lost Vespers, the Walker-Beyond-the-Wall decree, the Wall-of-Names re-facing four times, the renumbered towers (timed to the Standing year), the Bell-distance hiding travel-times, the consolidated thirteen-hour rite, the Watershed Reversal preached as holy mouths, the Pyrian children's truncated Arrow-Counter's Rhyme, the Long Vigil Plays missing eighteenth play, the Aspersoir Scale's three quiet recalibrations, the keel-throne / Paragon surname coincidence protected by a chancery clerk's stroke, the Cantorial Scribes' bone-handled scalpels. NO LAYER IS DRIFTING — but TWO points of strain require flagging: (a) the proliferation of Aurriste, Vell-os-Carrenost, Cassian, and Severa names tests reader memory — this is canon-consistent (the Aurriste fashion is itself test-6) but worth a glossary discipline going forward; (b) the demonic offices are split across multiple layers with slightly different focuses (the_bargain_economy treats them as bureaucratic counterparties; cosmology_hell treats them as principalities; threats activates the Sixth Notary as imminent threat) — the resolution preserves all three readings as facets of the same offices but a future hell-layer pass could harmonize voice. CRITICAL THROUGHLINE INTEGRITY: the canon refuses the cheap-corrupt-Paragon story and preserves the harder Constantine read — Halidan is genuinely without measurable Stain, he refused the Quartermaster's offer, his miracle is REAL, and the danger is that everything around the miracle (the singularity doctrine, the saint-count curation, the chancery succession apparatus, the Octave Bargain his cousin struck, the Auxiliary dead piling up uncounted, the Carrion Census foreclosure preparing at Ferrostat) is rotten. The Paragon stands on a curated lie that was built around him by people who love him, and he is asking the question (the Mournwing Letter) that the doctrine cannot survive, and the chancery has chosen not to answer. That is the world holding. The bell rings; the count is kept; the saint endures; the lamp does not go out — yet."

---

*End of campaign bible. The companion engine bootstrap lives at `rpg-mcp-bootstrap.json` and is loadable by the rpg-mcp `narrative_manage`, `spatial_manage`, `character_manage`, and `agent_manage` tools.*
